Allah's Existence
beginner
10 min
Believers' Analysis vs Materialist Evasion
Buti contrasts the believers' analysis with the materialist's evasion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the believers' causal chain ending with a Necessary Being is more coherent than the materialist's appeal to ignorance and how the category of contingency invalidates the question 'Who created God?'.

Core Idea
The believers' analysis avoids logical dead ends; the materialist's 'I don't know' is not science.

This passage from Buti highlights the stark contrast between the believer's rational analysis of existence and the materialist's reliance on nebulae. The believer traces all contingent existence back to a Necessary Being, avoiding logical fallacies. The materialist, when pressed, appeals to ignorance and threatens with the question 'Who created God?'. Buti reveals the category error behind that question.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two contrasting analyses presented.
The passage is a direct comparison; try to identify the believer's argument and the materialist's response.
2
Identify the believers' three impossibilities
Buti says the believers' analysis avoids circularity, infinite regress, and preponderance without a preponderator. Understand each of these logical problems.
These are classical kalam concepts for proving the necessity of a First Cause.
3
Examine the materialist's evasion
The materialist says the origin is the nebula, and when asked for its origin, says 'I don't know' – presenting ignorance as a scientific foundation.
This is an argument from ignorance, not a scientific explanation.
4
Grasp the category error
The materialist asks 'Who created God?', assuming God and the nebula are the same kind of being. Buti corrects: the nebula is contingent (mumkin), while God is necessary (wajib).
The question of origin only applies to contingent things, not the Necessary Being.
5
Reflect on coherence
Compare the two analyses: one provides a coherent logical chain, the other ends in ignorance. Which is truly scientific?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن المؤمنين بالله قد فرغوا من تحليل ظاهرة الوجود هذه عندما قالوا إن سلسلة الموجودات بأسرها لا بد من أن تعتمد في وجودها على ذات واجبة الوجود ينبثق الوجود من ذاتها ولا يفيض عليها من غيرها، وهو الله عز وجل. وعلى هذا لا يرد شيء من المستحيلات كالدور والتسلسل والرجحان بدون مرجح. ونحن نراه تحليلاً علمياً لا يعتريه أي تهافت أو خلف. فما هو التحليل العلمي لظاهرة الوجود عند المنكرين لوجود الله؟ لقد أجاب المخرّف العلمي، عندما قال: إن أصل الموجودات كلها هو السديم، ولمـا قيل له فما هو أصل السديم وما سر وجوده أجاب بأنه لا ثم راح يقرر أن هذا الجهل هو خير مستند علمي يقام عليه سر الوجود!!. وهددنـا إن لم نقبل بهذا المستند، بأنه سيطرح نفس السؤال علينا فيفاجئنا بقوله: فمن الذي أوجد الله؟!. هكذا يتصور الرجل المفتون بكلمة العلم والمفتقر إلى مضمونها!. إنه يحسب أن السديم والله شيء واحد في وجودهما؛ وإنما اختار المؤمنون «اعتباطاً» أن يؤلهوا الثاني ويتركوا الأول. وإذا كان معنى الوجود فيها واحداً فقد صح له أن يسأل عن موجد الله عز وجل كما له أن يسأل عن موجد السديم تماماً!! ونحن نقول لهذا المخرّف العلمي: إن السديم من نوع الممكن. ووجود الممكنات كلها.
Then indeed the believers in God have completed their analysis of this phenomenon of existence when they said that the entire chain of contingent beings must in their existence depend on a self-necessary being (dhāt wājib al-wujūd) from whose essence existence emanates and does not overflow onto it from another, and that is God Almighty. And upon this none of the impossibilities such as circularity, infinite regress, and preponderance without a preponderator occur. And we see it as a scientific analysis that has no inconsistency or contradiction. So what is the scientific analysis of the phenomenon of existence according to the deniers of God's existence? The scientific obfuscator has answered when he said: The origin of all existents is the nebula. And when it was said to him: What is the origin of the nebula and the secret of its existence? He answered: I don't know. Then he proceeded to declare that this ignorance is the best scientific basis upon which the secret of existence is established!! And he threatened us that if we do not accept this basis, he will pose the same question to us and surprise us by saying: So who created God?! This is how the man infatuated with the word 'science' but lacking its content imagines! He thinks that the nebula and God are one thing in their existence; and that the believers have arbitrarily chosen to deify the second and leave the first. And if the meaning of existence in them is one, then it is valid for him to ask about the originator of God Almighty just as it is valid for him to ask about the originator of the nebula completely!! And we say to this scientific obfuscator: The nebula is of the type of the contingent (al-mumkin). And the existence of all contingent things...
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a comparison and refutation. Buti first presents the believers' analysis: the entire chain of contingent beings requires a Necessary Being to avoid circularity, infinite regress, and the need for a preponderator. He calls this a scientific analysis without inconsistency. Then he presents the materialist's answer: the origin is the nebula, and when asked for its origin, he says 'I don't know' – presenting that ignorance as a scientific foundation. The materialist then threatens to ask 'Who created God?', assuming that God and the nebula are similar in being contingent. Buti refutes: the nebula is contingent (mumkin), while God is necessary (wājib). The question about God's origin does not apply to the Necessary Being.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود (necessary being)
ممكن (contingent)
دور (circularity)
تسلسل (infinite regress)
رجحان بلا مرجح (preponderance without preponderator)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God must have a creator just like the nebula does.
Correction: God is the Necessary Being (wājib al-wujūd), not contingent (mumkin). Only contingent things require a cause. The question 'Who created God?' is invalid because it assumes God is contingent.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what category of existence does the nebula belong to?
A) The necessary being
B) The contingent
C) The impossible
D) The divine

Key Takeaway
The believer's causal reasoning leads to a Necessary Being, while the materialist's appeal to ignorance collapses under scrutiny.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever avoided the deep question of existence by saying 'I don't know' like the materialist, instead of pursuing the truth wholeheartedly? What would it mean for you today to honestly follow the believers' analysis?
?
The materialist treated Allah as if He were a contingent being, limited and dependent. In what areas of your life have you acted as though Allah is dependent on causes or weak, instead of affirming His absolute necessity and independence?
?
Buti calls the materialist's answer 'scientific obfuscation.' Are you hiding behind comfortable 'I don't know' answers in your own search for truth about Allah, afraid of what accepting the full implications might demand of you?

The Islamic Analysis of Existence and Its Logical Soundness
Buti presents the Islamic analysis of existence and its logical advantages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic cosmological argument: that all contingent beings depend on a Necessary Existent, thereby avoiding logical absurdities such as circularity, infinite regress, and preponderance without a preponderant.

Core Idea
All existence relies on a self-necessary source, avoiding three logical impossibilities.

Buti begins by presenting the Islamic analysis of existence as a complete and coherent explanation. He states that believers have already resolved the question of existence by affirming a Necessary Being (wājib al-wujūd) upon which all contingent things depend. This analysis, he argues, is scientifically sound and free from internal contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Islamic analysis
Read the first part of the passage where Buti summarizes the Islamic position: the entire chain of existents depends on a self-necessary essence (dhāt wājibat al-wujūd).
Notice the phrase 'ينبثق الوجود من ذاتها' (existence emanates from its essence).
2
Identify the three avoided impossibilities
Buti mentions three logical absurdities that this analysis avoids: circularity (al-dawr), infinite regress (al-tasalsul), and preponderance without a preponderant (al-tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ). Reflect on why each is problematic.
These are classical kalam arguments against infinite causal chains.
3
Understand the claim of scientific validity
Buti asserts that this analysis is 'scientific' and free from contradiction. Consider what he means by 'scientific' in this context—not empirical science but rational, logical analysis.
He uses the term 'taḥlīl ʿilmī' (scientific analysis) to emphasize rigor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن المؤمنين بالله قد فرغوا من تحليل ظاهرة الوجود هذه عندما قالوا إن سلسلة الموجودات بأسرها لا بد من أن تعتمد في وجودها على ذات واجبة الوجود ينبثق الوجود من ذاتها ولا يفيض عليها من غيرها ، وهو الله عز وجل . وعلى هذا لا يرد شيء من المستحيلات كالدور والتسلسل والرجحان بدون مرجح . ونحن نراه تحليلاً علمياً لا يعتريه أي تهافت أو خلف . فما هو التحليل العلمي لظاهرة الوجود عند المنكرين لوجود الله ؟ لقد أجاب المخرّف العلمي ، عندما قال : إن أصل الموجودات كلها هو السديم ، ولمـا قيل له فما هو أصل السديم وما سر وجوده أجاب بأنه لا ثم راح يقرر أن هذا الجهل هو خير مستند علمي يقام عليه سر الوجود !! . وهددنـا إن لم نقبل بهذا المستند ، بأنه سيطرح نفس السؤال علينا فيفاجئنا بقوله : فمن الذي أوجد الله ؟! يدري !!.. هكذا يتصور الرجل المفتون بكلمة العلم والمفتقر إلى مضمونها !. إنه يحسب أن السديم والله شيء واحد في وجودهما ؛ وإنما اختار المؤمنون « اعتباطاً » أن يؤلهوا الثاني ويتركوا الأول . وإذا كان معنى الوجود فيها واحداً فقد صح له أن يسأل عن موجد له أن يسأل عن موجد الله عز وجل كما له أن يسأل عن موجد السديم تماماً !!.. يصح ونحن نقول لهذا المخرّف العلمي : إن السديم من نوع الممكن . ووجود الممكنات كلها إنما يكون بتأثير من غيرها . وإلا فكيف يترجح فيها أحد طرفي الإمكان ؟ أما الله عز وجل فهو واجب الوجود أي إن وجوده من ذاته هو ، وليس فيضاً أو بتأثير من غيره ، وهذا هو معنى كونه إلهاً . ولذلك لا يرد هذا السؤال بالنسبة لذات الله تعالى إطلاقاً إذا كان السائل مؤمناً بألوهيته ، أما إذا لم يكن يؤمن بها فإن السؤال عنث ، لأن مؤرد السؤال مختلف بين السائل والمجيب
Then the believers in God have finished analyzing this phenomenon of existence when they said: The entire chain of existents must in their existence depend upon a self-necessary essence (dhāt wājibat al-wujūd), from whose essence existence emanates and does not flow upon it from other than it, and He is God, Mighty and Majestic. So upon this, nothing of impossibilities occurs like circularity, infinite regress, and preponderance without a preponderant. And we see it as a scientific analysis that no contradiction or defect confronts it. So what is the scientific analysis of the phenomenon of existence according to the deniers of God's existence? The scientific falsifier has answered when he said: The origin of all existents is the nebula. And when it was said to him: What is the origin of the nebula and the secret of its existence? He answered: There is none. Then he proceeded to assert that this ignorance is the best scientific basis upon which the secret of existence is established!! And he threatened us, if we do not accept this basis, that he will pose the same question to us and surprise us with his saying: Who created God? He knows!! Thus imagines the man infatuated with the word of science and in need of its content! He thinks that the nebula and God are one thing in their existence; and that the believers only arbitrarily chose to deify the second and leave the first. And if the meaning of existence in them is one, then he is correct to ask about the creator—he is correct to ask about the creator of God, Mighty and Majestic, just as he is correct to ask about the creator of the nebula!! He is correct. And we say to this scientific falsifier: The nebula is of the type of the possible (al-mumkin). And the existence of all possible things is only by the influence of other than them. Otherwise, how would one of the two sides of possibility be preponderated? As for God, Mighty and Majestic, He is the Necessary Existent (wājib al-wujūd), i.e., His existence is from His own essence, not a flow or by the influence of another, and this is the meaning of His being God. Therefore, this question is not posed regarding the essence of God, Exalted, at all if the questioner believes in His divinity. But if he does not believe in it, then the question is [unclear], because the subject of the question is different between the questioner and the respondent.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the materialist position on the origin of existence. Buti begins by summarizing the Islamic analysis: the entire chain of contingent existents must depend on a self-necessary Essence (wājib al-wujūd), thereby avoiding absurdities like circularity, infinite regress, and preponderance without a preponderant. He calls this a valid scientific analysis. He then asks what the materialist alternative is, and cites the claim that the origin is the nebula. When pressed on the origin of the nebula, the materialist admits ignorance and calls this ignorance a scientific basis. Moreover, the materialist threatens to ask the believer 'Who created God?' implying inconsistency. Buti exposes the error: the materialist mistakenly equates the nebula and God as the same kind of existence, thinking both need a creator. Buti then clarifies: the nebula is of the type of the possible (mumkin), which requires an external cause for its existence to preponderate one of its two possibilities. God, however, is the Necessary Existent, whose existence is from itself, not from another. Therefore, the question 'Who created God?' does not apply to God's essence when one believes in His divinity. If the questioner does not believe, the question's premise is different, leading to a category mistake.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود
الدور
التسلسل
الرجحان بدون مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Islamic analysis of existence is just faith-based and not rational.
Correction: Buti argues it is a rigorous scientific (rational) analysis that avoids logical absurdities.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what three impossibilities does the Islamic analysis of existence avoid?
A) Circularity, infinite regress, and preponderance without a preponderant
B) Atheism, agnosticism, and skepticism
C) Chaos, randomness, and chance
D) Evolution, mutation, and natural selection

Key Takeaway
The Islamic insistence on a Necessary Existent provides a logically coherent foundation for existence, avoiding three classic absurdities of infinite causal chains.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that your existence depends entirely on Allah's necessity, why do you still live as if you are self-sufficient? When was the last time you felt the weight of your absolute need for Him in a concrete moment?
?
The argument says that without a Necessary Being, the chain of contingency collapses into absurdity. In your own life, what are you relying on—health, wealth, relationships—as if it were necessary? How would your daily choices change if you really internalized that only Allah is necessary?
?
Buti claims this analysis is 'scientific' and free from contradiction. Are you intellectually convinced by this argument, or do you harbor lingering doubts? If doubts remain, what is holding you back from full submission of your intellect to this truth—and what would it cost you to surrender that reservation?

Allah's Existence

Refuting Materialism: The Nebula and the Necessary Existent
Buti refutes the materialist nebula theory and the 'Who created God?' objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the materialist objection 'Who created God?' is invalid, based on the distinction between contingent (mumkin) and necessary (wājib) existence.

Core Idea
The nebula is contingent; God is necessary. They are not comparable.

Buti now turns to the materialist alternative, which posits the nebula as the origin of all things. He exposes the weakness of this position: when asked about the nebula's origin, the materialist admits ignorance and calls it science. Worse, the materialist tries to turn the tables by asking 'Who created God?' Buti prepares a precise refutation based on the categories of necessary and contingent existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the materialist claim and the objection
Read the part where Buti presents the materialist claim that the nebula is the origin, and the response to the question about its origin: 'There is none.' Also note the materialist's counter-question: 'Who created God?'
Observe the materialist's tactic of threatening to ask the same question.
2
Identify the materialist's mistake
Buti says the materialist thinks the nebula and God are the same type of existence. Reflect on why this is a category error.
The materialist assumes both need a creator because he views both as beings that exist similarly.
3
Understand the distinction: mumkin vs. wājib
Buti explains that the nebula is of the type 'possible' (mumkin), which requires an external cause. But God is 'necessary existent' (wājib al-wujūd), whose existence is from itself. Therefore, the question 'Who created God?' does not apply.
The distinction hinges on whether existence is self-derived or received from another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Asking 'Who created God?' is a valid refutation of the existence of God.
Correction: The question is invalid because God is defined as the Necessary Existent, who by definition has no cause.

Checkpoint
Why does Buti say the question 'Who created God?' does not apply to God?
A) Because God is eternal and beyond time
B) Because God is the Necessary Existent, whose existence is from Himself
C) Because the question is grammatically incorrect
D) Because the materialist has no evidence for the nebula

Key Takeaway
The materialist's 'Who created God?' is a category mistake; contingent things need a cause, but the Necessary Existent is uncaused by definition.

Allah's Existence
beginner
5 min
Why the Question of a Cause Does Not Apply to God
Al-Buti explains why the question of a cause does not apply to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the question of a cause does not apply to God according to Al-Buti, based on the distinction between contingent and necessary existence.

Core Idea
God is necessary existence, so He needs no cause.

Al-Buti addresses a common objection: if everything needs a cause, who created God? He argues that the question is based on a misunderstanding. Contingent things require an external cause to tip the balance, but God is necessary existence—His existence is from Himself. Therefore, the question does not apply.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Al-Buti uses a very concise style here.
2
Identify the two types of existence
The passage distinguishes between contingent beings (mumkin) and Necessary Being (wajib al-wujud). Find where each is discussed.
Contingent beings are those whose existence is possible but not necessary.
3
Understand why contingent beings need a cause
Al-Buti says contingent beings only come about through the influence of another, otherwise there would be no preponderance of one possibility over another. Grasp this reasoning.
4
See why God does not need a cause
God is necessary existence, so the question of an external cause does not apply to His essence. Understand the shift.
This is the key point of the lesson.
5
Consider the role of the questioner's belief
Al-Buti notes that if the questioner already believes in God's divinity, the question is irrelevant; if not, the premises differ. Reflect on this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنما يكون بتأثير من غيرها . وإلا فكيف يترجح فيها أحد طرفي الإمكان ؟ أما الله عز وجل فهو واجب الوجود أي إن وجوده من ذاته هو ، وليس فيضاً أو بتأثير من غيره ، وهذا هو معنى كونه إلهاً . ولذلك لا يرد هذا السؤال بالنسبة لذات الله تعالى إطلاقاً إذا كان السائل مؤمناً بألوهيته ، أما إذا لم يكن يؤمن بها فإن السؤال عنث [؟]، لأن مؤرد السؤال مختلف بين السائل والمجيب
It only comes about through the influence of another. Otherwise, how could one of the two sides of possibility be preponderated? As for God Almighty, He is Necessary Existence, meaning that His existence is from His own self, and not an emanation or through the influence of another. This is the meaning of His being God. Therefore, this question does not arise with respect to the essence of God Almighty at all if the questioner believes in His divinity. But if he does not believe in it, then the question is [؟], because the scope of the question differs between the questioner and the answerer.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author addresses a hypothetical question: why does the contingent world need an external cause? He first states that contingent things only come about through an external influence; otherwise, there would be no preponderance of one possibility over another. Then he distinguishes God: He is necessary existence, so the question does not apply to Him. The distinction is important: if the questioner already believes in God's divinity, the question is irrelevant; if not, the question is invalid because the questioner and answerer have different premises.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود
ممكن
تأثير
ترجيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The question 'who created God?' is a valid question that applies to God.
Correction: God is Necessary Existence, so He requires no external cause, making the question invalid.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the question 'who created God?' not arise?
A) God is eternal.
B) God is necessary existence and requires no external cause.
C) The question is unanswerable.
D) God created Himself.

Key Takeaway
God's self-existence (wajib al-wujud) means He is uncaused, so the question 'who created God?' is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Social Impact of Islamic Creed
Buti states the social role of Islamic creed and proves it from the story of Musa and Fir'awn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Islamic creed transforms society by humbling the arrogant and elevating the oppressed, as argued by Buti and exemplified in the Quranic story of Musa and Fir'awn.

Core Idea
Islamic creed balances society: it humbles tyrants and empowers the weak.

Buti presents a powerful thesis: the Islamic creed is not just personal belief but a social force that restructures power relations. Before we examine his proof from the Quran, he summarizes the creed's twofold effect on the arrogant and the oppressed. This passage grounds the social justice dimension of faith in both reason and revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read Buti's comprehensive statement
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its rhythm. Then read the translation. Notice how Buti presents his thesis in a single, flowing sentence.
Pay attention to the contrast between المتألهين والمتكبرين and الدهماء والمستضعفين.
2
Identify the twofold effect
The passage describes two simultaneous movements: the creed brings down the arrogant and raises the oppressed. Find where each is mentioned and note the result: a just equilibrium.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Buti cites verses 4-6 of Surah Al-Qasas. Read the verses carefully and see how they illustrate the same two movements: Pharaoh's tyranny and God's promise to empower the oppressed.
The verse shows the divine intervention that fulfills the creed's social role.
4
Reflect on the social balance
Consider how this passage refutes the idea that Islam only cares for the weak. Buti insists that the creed restrains the powerful as well, creating equal limits for all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبكلمة جامعة نقول إن من شأن العقيدة الإسلامية أن تنزل بالمتألهين والمتكبرين من عليائهم وجبروتهم، وتحجزهم عن التطاول على الآخرين؛ وأن ترتفع بالدهماء والمستضعفين عن مناخ الذل والصغار الذي فرض عليهم وتطلقهم فوق صعيد الحرية والكرامة، وتعيد إلى كيانهم مشاعر العز والإباء. وبذلك يلتقي هؤلاء وأولئك عند حدود عادلة متساوية لا تدع لهذا الجانب أو ذاك فرصة لاستغلال أو وسيلة لاستعباد. ووقائع التاريخ ونماذج الحياة الإسلامية التي قامت على هذه الأرض خير دليل على هذه الحقيقة البدهية الواضحة. ويتمثل هذا المعنى بوضوح تام، في قوله سبحانه وتعالى، وهو يوضح الحكمة من إرسال موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى فرعون منذراً وهادياً: {إِنَّ فِرعَونَ عَلا فِي الأَرضِ وَجَعَلَ أَهلَها شِيَعًا يَستَضعِفُ طائِفَةً مِنهُم يُذَبِّحُ أَبناءَهُم وَيَستَحيِي نِساءَهُم إِنَّهُ كانَ مِنَ المُفسِدِينَ. وَنُريدُ أَن نَمُنَّ عَلَى الَّذينَ استُضعِفوا في الأَرضِ وَنَجعَلَهُم أَئِمَّةً وَنَجعَلَهُمُ الوارِثينَ. وَنُمَكِّنَ لَهُم في الأَرضِ وَنُرِيَ فِرعَونَ وهامانَ وَجُنودَهُما مِنهُم ما كانوا يَحذَرُونَ} [القصص: 4-6]
And with a comprehensive statement, we say that it is the function of the Islamic creed to bring down the self-deifiers and the arrogant from their high places and their tyranny, and to restrain them from encroaching upon others; and to raise the common people and the oppressed from the climate of humiliation and lowliness that was imposed upon them, and to launch them upon the plain of freedom and dignity, and to restore to their being the feelings of honor and pride. Thus these and those meet at just and equal limits that leave no opportunity for this side or that for exploitation or a means for enslavement. The facts of history and the models of Islamic life that were established on this earth are the best evidence for this clear self-evident truth. And this meaning is perfectly exemplified in His saying, Exalted and Majestic, as He explains the wisdom behind sending Moses, peace be upon him, to Pharaoh as a warner and guide: {Indeed, Pharaoh exalted himself in the land and made its people factions, oppressing a group among them, slaughtering their sons and keeping their women alive; indeed, he was of the corrupters. And We wanted to bestow favor upon those who were oppressed in the land and make them leaders and make them the inheritors. And to establish them in the land and to show Pharaoh and Haman and their soldiers from them what they feared} [Al-Qasas: 4-6].
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a proof and demonstration of the social function of the Islamic creed. Buti begins by summarizing the twofold effect: it humbles the arrogant and tyrannical, preventing them from oppressing others, and simultaneously elevates the weak and oppressed, granting them freedom, dignity, and honor. The result is a just equilibrium where both parties meet on equal terms, eliminating exploitation and enslavement. He then claims that historical evidence and Islamic civilization provide abundant proof of this reality. To crystallize this meaning, he cites the Quranic account of Pharaoh's tyranny against the Children of Israel and God's promise to empower the oppressed, making them leaders and inheritors. The verse illustrates how divine intervention overturns the unjust order, fulfilling precisely the social role Buti attributes to the Islamic creed. The passage thus uses scripture as the ultimate warrant for the creed's transformative power in society.

Key Takeaway

The Real Reason for Worship: Our Need, Not God's Need
Buti explains that human need for God drives belief, not God's need for worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the obligation to believe in God and worship Him stems from our own need for happiness, not from any need on God's part.

Core Idea
Our need for God drives our worship, not God's need for us.

Buti, having established the rational arguments for God's existence, now turns to the purpose of faith and worship. He clarifies a fundamental misconception: God does not benefit from our worship; rather, it is we who need it for our own well-being, both in this life and the next. This lesson explores that profound shift in perspective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting Buti's clear statement of causality.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ليس هو المحتاج' – He is not in need.
2
Identify the key claim
Notice how Buti asserts that humanity's need for submission is not because God requires it, but because our happiness depends on it.
The word 'سعادتنا' (our happiness) is central.
3
Connect to the Quranic verse
See how the verse from Adh-Dhariyat supports Buti's argument by emphasizing God's self-sufficiency and the purpose of creation.
The verse explicitly states God does not desire provision from us.
4
Reflect on the implication
Think about how this understanding changes the motivation for worship from obligation to personal necessity.
This reframes worship as a need, not a duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن هنا كانت حاجة الإنسانية كلها إلى أن تدين لبارئها عز وجل بالاعتقاد الجازم بوجوده ووحدانيته، وأن تدين له بالعبودية المطلقة في كل شؤونه وأطوار حياته، أي إن الله عز وجل ليس هو المحتاج إلى شيء من هذه الدينونة له أو التمسك بأمره، ولكن سعادتنا الدنيوية - فضلاً عن الأخروية - هي التي تحوجنا وتضطرنا إلى هذه الدينونة. وصدق الله رب العالمين إذ يقول {وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون، ما أريد منهم من رزق وما أريد أن يطعمون، إن الله هو الرزاق ذو القوة المتين} [الذاريات: 56-58]
Hence the need of all humanity to submit to their Creator, Mighty and Majestic, with firm belief in His existence and His oneness, and to submit to Him with absolute servitude in all their affairs and stages of life—that is, God, Mighty and Majestic, is not in need of any of this submission to Him or adherence to His command; rather, our worldly happiness—let alone the afterlife—is what makes us need and compels us to this submission. And God, Lord of the worlds, speaks the truth when He says {And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me. I do not desire from them any provision, nor do I desire that they should feed Me. Indeed, God is the Provider, the Possessor of strength, the Firm} [Adh-Dhariyat: 56-58].
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion drawn from the preceding argument, explaining the ultimate reason for human obligation to believe and submit. Buti begins by stating the necessary need of all humanity to affirm firmly God's existence and oneness, and to dedicate absolute servitude to Him in every aspect of life. He immediately clarifies a potential misunderstanding: God is not in need of this submission or obedience; rather, it is our own well-being—both in this world and the Hereafter—that necessitates it. The worldly happiness is the primary driver, and the afterlife is an added reason. He then supports this with the Quranic verse stating that God created jinn and mankind solely for worship, emphasizing that He does not require their provisions, for He alone is the Provider and Strong. The verse reinforces the idea that worship is for the creature's benefit, not the Creator's.

The Foundation of Creed: God's Existence and the Two Methods of Investigation
Buti introduces the centrality of God's existence and the first method of investigation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in God's existence is the foundation of all creedal matters and be introduced to the two methods of investigating non-observable scientific claims.

Core Idea
Belief in God's existence is the root from which all other creedal truths branch.

This passage opens the discussion on God's existence by establishing its primacy in faith. Buti explains that all other beliefs depend on this core truth. He then outlines the methodological challenge: since God's existence cannot be observed, we must use one of two rational methods. This lesson focuses on the first method, direct investigation through certain proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Buti builds his argument from the foundational role of God's existence to the methodological approach.
2
Identify the main claim
What does Buti say about belief in God's existence? It is the foundation of all creedal matters and from it branch out other doctrinal matters.
3
Understand the metaphor
Buti uses the metaphor of an effusion from one supreme reality. All realities of the universe flow from God's Essence. This reinforces the idea that you must know the source first.
4
Recognize the two methods
Buti states that God's existence is a scientific claim not subject to observation. Therefore, there are two ways to investigate it. The first way is direct investigation using the methodology for unobserved scientific matters, leading to certain proofs.
The second method is not fully given in this passage, but it is implied.
5
Reflect on the objection
Buti anticipates the objection 'I do not believe in the Creator' and responds that such a person must investigate well and verify their disbelief to avoid error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة :
أولاً وجود الله عزوجل
والإيمان بوجود الله عز وجل أساس مسائل العقيدة كلها ، وعنه تتفرع بقية الأمور الاعتقادية التي يجب إنهاض العقل للتأمل فيها ثم الإيمان بها
•
وبتعبير آخر نقول : إن ما تراه من حقائق الكون كلها إنما هو فيض عن حقيقة واحدة كبرى ، ألا ذات الله عز وجل . ومن المحال أن تدرك ماهية وهي الحقائق المتفرعة الصغرى قبل أن تدرك منبعها وأصلها الأول . فكان لابد إذاً ، لكي تستطيع التعرف على الكون من أن تعرف خالقه أولاً .
قد تقول : ولكني لا أؤمن بالخالق ، فجوابي لك : إن عليك أن تبحث جيداً في موضوع وجوده وأن تحقق في فكرة عدم إيمانك به ، وذلك كي لا تخطئ أخيراً في فهمك للكون ومعنى وجودك فيه
·

( وجود الله عز وجل ) : دعوى علمية تتعلق من العلم بجانب لا يخضع للتجربة والمشاهدة
ولذلك فإن السبيل إلى التحقيق فيها إنما يكون بأحد طريقين :
الطريق الأول : التحقيق في وجود الله مباشرة طبق المنهج الذي ذكرناه بالنسبة للقضايا العلمية غير المشاهدة ، حتى إذا ثبت عندنا ذلك بالبراهين اليقينية ، دلنـا وجوده على أنه لم يخلق شيئاً من هذا الكون عبثاً ، ودلنـا هـذا
Introduction: First, the existence of God Almighty. And belief in the existence of God Almighty is the foundation of all matters of creed, and from it branch out the rest of the doctrinal matters which the intellect must be roused to contemplate and then believe in. • In other words, we say: What you see of all the realities of the universe is only an effusion from one supreme reality, namely the Essence of God Almighty. And it is impossible to comprehend a whatness—the small branching realities—before you comprehend their source and first origin. So it is necessary, therefore, in order for you to be able to know the universe, that you know its Creator first. You might say: But I do not believe in the Creator. My answer to you is: You must investigate well the subject of His existence and verify the idea of your disbelief in Him, so that you do not ultimately err in your understanding of the universe and the meaning of your existence in it. • And let us begin proceeding, following the methodology we have explained. • (The existence of God Almighty): A scientific claim that pertains to that aspect of science which is not subject to experimentation and observation. Therefore, the way to investigation in it is only through one of two ways: The first way: investigating the existence of God directly according to the methodology we mentioned for unobserved scientific matters, so that when that is established for us by certain proofs, His existence shows us that He did not create anything of this universe in vain, and this shows us
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the section on the existence of God Almighty. It begins by establishing that belief in God's existence is the foundation of all creedal matters; all other doctrinal issues branch out from it. The author then restates this using a metaphor: all perceived realities of the universe emanate from a single supreme Reality—God's Essence. He argues that one cannot grasp the subsidiary, smaller realities without first knowing their source. Therefore, to know the universe, one must first know its Creator. The author then addresses a potential objection from someone who says: 'I do not believe in the Creator.' The response is that such a person must seriously investigate the subject of God's existence and critically examine their own disbelief, lest they ultimately misunderstand the universe and their own purpose. The author then states they will proceed according to the methodology already explained. Next, he characterizes the claim of God's existence as a scientific claim belonging to that part of science which is not subject to experimentation and observation. Consequently, the only way to investigate it is through one of two methods. Only the first method is detailed here: direct investigation using the methodology for unobserved scientific matters, such that once God's existence is established through certain proofs, that existence proves that He did not create anything in vain. The passage cuts off mid-sentence, but the intended structure is clear.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's existence can be proven through empirical observation and experimentation.
Correction: The author clarifies that God's existence is a scientific claim that is not subject to experimentation and observation; it must be investigated through rational proof.

Checkpoint

Starting with God's Existence
Establishes belief in God as foundation of all creedal matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in God's existence is the necessary foundation for all creedal matters and how all realities depend on Him.

Core Idea
Belief in God is the key that unlocks understanding of the universe.

This passage from Dr. Ramadan al-Buti sets the stage for the entire study of creed. He argues that before we can explore any other theological topic, we must first establish the reality of God's existence. Because all truths in the universe flow from that single supreme truth, we cannot hope to understand the parts without first knowing the whole.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice the author's tone and how he structures the introduction.
2
Identify the central claim
Look for the sentence that says belief in God is the foundation of all creedal matters. This is the core assertion.
3
Understand the argument
The author explains that all cosmic realities are an emanation from God. Reflect on why he says it is impossible to know the branches without knowing the source.
4
Consider the objection and response
Read the hypothetical objection from someone who does not believe in the Creator. Note the author's answer: investigate thoroughly to avoid error.

Introduction: First, the existence of God Almighty. Belief in the existence of God Almighty is the foundation of all creedal matters, and from it branch all other matters of belief which must be undertaken by the intellect to contemplate them and then believe in them. In other words, we say: all that you see of the realities of the universe are but an emanation from one great reality, namely the Self of God Almighty. And it is impossible for you to comprehend the nature of the small branching realities before you comprehend their source and first origin. Therefore, it was necessary, for you to be able to recognize the universe, that you recognize its Creator first. You might say: But I do not believe in the Creator; my answer to you is: you must examine well the subject of His existence and investigate the idea of your disbelief in Him, so that you might not err ultimately in your understanding of the universe and the meaning of your existence in it. Let us begin the journey following the methodology we have clarified.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is an introduction establishing the necessity of beginning with belief in God's existence. The author first asserts that belief in God is the foundation of all creedal matters. He justifies this by stating that all cosmic realities emanate from the single supreme reality of God, and it is impossible to understand the derived realities before their source. He then anticipates an objection from one who does not believe in the Creator and advises that such a person must investigate the matter thoroughly to avoid error. Finally, he signals the start of the journey according to the methodology already explained.

The Top-Down Method: Direct Proof of God
Introduces the top-down method for proving God's existence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the top-down method that begins with direct rational proof of God's existence and then deduces prophethood and scripture.

Core Idea
From God to everything: the highest proof leads to all truths.

Buti first clarifies that the claim of God's existence is not empirically testable. He then presents two valid methods of investigation. The first, which he calls 'gradual progress from the highest', starts with direct rational arguments for God, then moves step by step to the purpose of creation, the truth of prophets, and ultimately the contents of scripture.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening definition
Understand why the existence of God is a 'scientific claim' not subject to experiment.
This sets the stage for why rational methods are needed.
2
Trace the deductive chain
Follow the sequence: direct proof of God → purposeful creation → truth of messengers → truth of scriptures → all contents.
Each step relies on the previous one.
3
Note the name of the method
Buti calls this 'the way of gradual progress from the highest' because it starts with the highest reality, God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( وجود الله عز وجل ) : دعوى علمية تتعلق من العلم بجانب لا يخضع للتجربة والمشاهدة
ولذلك فإن السبيل إلى التحقيق فيها إنما يكون بأحد طريقين :
الطريق الأول : التحقيق في وجود الله مباشرة طبق المنهج الذي ذكرناه بالنسبة للقضايا العلمية غير المشاهدة ، حتى إذا ثبت عندنا ذلك بالبراهين اليقينية ، دلنـا وجوده على أنه لم يخلق شيئاً من هذا الكون عبثاً ، ودلنـا هـذا بدوره على صدق الرسل والأنبياء فيما بعثوا به من التكاليف ، ودلنا الإيمان بالرسل على الإيمان بالكتب وبالقرآن أنه كلام الله عز وجل ، ثم دلنـا الإيمان بكلام الله على الإيمان بكل ما تضمنه من أخبار وأحكام وأوامر ونواه مختلفة · ولنسم هذا الطريق بطريق التدرج من الأعلى ·
الطريق الثاني : ترك البحث في ذات الله ، والبدء بالنظر في خبر نقل إلينا عن حقيقة هذا الكتاب الذي بين يدينا والذي اسمه القرآن . حتى إذا علمنا بالبرهان اليقيني المتعلق بتحقيق النقول والأخبار أنه قد وصل إلينا بواسطة محمد ، وأنه قال عنه إنه وحي من الله عز وجل ، أخذنا نحقق في معنى الوحي كما فسره الرسول ولولا الله نفسه بالبراهين العلمية المنسجمة مع علوم هذه الدعوى ، وهي برهان التلازم البين وقياس الأولى طبق ما ذكرناه وبشروطه السالفة الاستقراء التام وغيره من حتى إذا ثبت لدينا صدق دعوى الرسول مع الله وأن الوحي حقيقة لا اختيار وساء للرسول فيها وليس معنى شعورياً نابعاً من كيانه ، بحثنا فيما عسى أن يكون مصدراً لهذا الوحي ، ببرهان التلازم القائم على الاستقراء التام . حتى إذا ثبت لدينا بواسطة الاستقصاء أنه لا يمكن أن يكون لهذا الوحي مُنْزِل إلا الله جل جلاله ، دلنا ذلك على وجود الله عز وجل ، وازداد بذلك إيماننا بكل المراحل التي كنا قد اجتزناها بالبحث . ولنسم هذه الطريقة بطريق التدرج من الأدنى
(The existence of God Almighty) is a scientific claim pertaining to a side of science that is not subject to experiment and observation. Therefore the path to investigation in it is only by one of two ways: The first way: investigating the existence of God directly according to the methodology we mentioned regarding unobserved scientific issues, so that when that is established for us with certain proofs, His existence indicates to us that He did not create anything of this universe in vain, and this in turn indicates the truthfulness of the messengers and prophets in the duties they were sent with, and belief in the messengers indicates belief in the scriptures and in the Quran that it is the speech of God Almighty, then belief in the speech of God indicates belief in all that it contains of reports, rulings, commands and prohibitions, various. And let us call this way the way of gradual progress from the highest. The second way: leaving research into the Self of God, and beginning by examining a report transmitted to us about the reality of this book that is in our hands, whose name is the Quran. So that when we know by certain proof related to verifying transmissions and reports that it has reached us through Muhammad, and that he said about it that it is a revelation from God Almighty, we begin to investigate the meaning of revelation as the Messenger explained, and were it not for God Himself, through scientific proofs consistent with the sciences of this claim, which are the proof of evident correlation and the argument of priority as we mentioned with its preceding conditions, complete induction and others, until when the truthfulness of the Messenger's claim with God is established for us and that revelation is a reality—neither choice nor evil for the Messenger in it—and not a subjective meaning emanating from his being, we search for what might be a source for this revelation, by the proof of correlation based on complete induction. So that when it is established for us by thorough investigation that there cannot be for this revelation any sender except God, may His Majesty be exalted, that indicates to us the existence of God Almighty, and thereby our faith increases in all the stages we had passed through in research. And let us call this method the way of gradual progress from the lowest.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage defines the claim of God's existence as a scientific claim not subject to experiment, then classifies two methods for investigating it. The first method (top-down) begins with direct proof of God's existence using arguments for unobserved phenomena, then derives from that the purposeful nature of creation, then the truth of prophets, scriptures, and all their contents. The second method (bottom-up) begins with the historical transmission of the Quran, establishes its veracity through critical analysis of reports, then uses scientific reasoning to confirm revelation as truly from God, then by elimination concludes that only God could be its source, thus proving His existence. Both methods are named: 'gradual progress from the highest' (top-down) and 'gradual progress from the lowest' (bottom-up).

دعوى علمية
لا يخضع للتجربة والمشاهدة
طريقين
البراهين اليقينية
صدق الرسل
التدرج من الأعلى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Direct rational proof of God's existence
C) Examining historical reports
D) Accepting the purpose of creation

Key Takeaway
The top-down method starts with rational proof of God and then deduces all other religious truths in a logical chain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Bottom-Up Method: Starting from the Quran
Describes the bottom-up method for proving God's existence through the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the bottom-up method that begins with historical verification of the Quran and then ascends to prove God's existence.

Core Idea
From the Quran to God: the historical record leads to the divine.

The second method takes a different starting point: instead of proving God directly, it begins with the Quran as a historical document. By critically examining its transmission and content, we first verify that it came from Muhammad and that he claimed it was revelation. Then using rational arguments, particularly the proof of correlation and the argument of priority, we conclude that only God could be its source, thereby proving His existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the second method
Notice that it starts by 'leaving research into the Self of God' and instead examines the Quran.
This method is empirical in a historical sense.
2
Identify the stages of verification
Follow the sequence: verify Quran's transmission → confirm Muhammad's claim → investigate meaning of revelation → prove its source is God.
The key tools are 'proof of correlation' and 'argument of priority'.
3
Note the name of the method
Buti calls this 'the way of gradual progress from the lowest' because it starts with a created object (the Quran) and ascends to God.

beginner
5 min
Proof from Impossibility of Preponderance without a Preferrer
Buti defines 'preponderance without a preferrer' and states its self-evident falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of 'preponderance without a preferrer' and why it is considered self-evidently invalid by all rational people.

Core Idea
Every change requires a cause; uncaused change is impossible.

Buti begins by introducing one of the most foundational rational proofs for God's existence. He defines a key term and asserts its self-evident falsehood. This principle will later be applied to argue for a Creator. Let's read the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the translation to get a clear understanding of Buti's words.
2
Identify the definition
Find the sentence that defines 'preponderance without a preferrer'. Notice the key terms: 'مغير' (changer) and 'محول' (transformer).
3
Grasp the rational principle
The passage states that all rational people know that things remain as they are unless a changer imposes a new state. Understand why this is self-evident.
This principle is not controversial; it is a basic law of reasoning.
4
Recognize the application signal
Buti ends by saying 'if you have understood this, let us apply this proof to the existence of Allah'. Note that the application is not in this passage, but the foundation is laid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولاً - برهان بطلان الرجحان بدون مرجح :

ومعنى الرجحان بدون مرجح ، أن يكون الشيء جارياً على نسق معين ، ثم يتغير عن نسقه ويتحول عنه بدون وجود أي مغير أو محول إطلاقاً ، فهذا من الأمور الواضحة البطلان ، وجميع العقلاء يعلمون أن الأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان عليه ، ولابد لتحويله عن حاله السابقة من محول ومؤثر يفرض عليه هذا الوضع الجديد وينسخ حاله القديمة

فإذا عرفت هذا ، فلنطبق هذا البرهان على مسألة وجود الله عز وجل :
First: The proof of the invalidity of preponderance without a preferrer:

And the meaning of preponderance without a preferrer is that a thing is proceeding on a certain pattern, then it changes from its pattern and shifts away from it without the existence of any changer or transformer whatsoever. So this is among matters clearly invalid. And all rational people know that the original state is that what was remains as it was, and to change it from its previous state there must be a changer and an effecter that imposes upon it this new state and abrogates its old state.

So if you have understood this, let us apply this proof to the matter of the existence of Allah Almighty:
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents the first of the four self-evident proofs: the proof from the impossibility of preponderance without a preferrer (burhan batalan al-tarjih bila murajjih). The author begins by defining the key concept: 'preponderance without a preferrer' means a thing changing from its established pattern without any cause or changer. This is self-evidently false. All rational people recognize that the default assumption is that a thing remains as it is, and any change requires a changer or an effecting agent that brings about the new state and abrogates the old one. Having established this principle, the author then signals the intention to apply this proof to the existence of God, though the application itself is not given in this passage (it would follow in subsequent text).

Key Terms
الرجحان بدون مرجح
برهان بطلان الرجحان
المغير
المحول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this principle rejects all change, insisting that things never change.
Correction: The principle does not reject change itself; it only rejects uncaused change. Every change must have a cause or changer.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'preponderance without a preferrer' mean?
A) A thing remaining in its original state forever
B) A thing changing from its pattern without any changer or transformer
C) The impossibility of multiple causes for a single effect
D) The logical priority of a cause over its effect

Key Takeaway
Change in the world cannot occur without a cause; the impossibility of uncaused change is a rational foundation for proving the existence of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a significant change in your life—a decision you made, a belief you abandoned, or a habit you formed. What caused that change? Can you honestly identify a specific cause, or have you assumed it happened randomly? How does the impossibility of uncaused change challenge you to take responsibility for that change?
?
If you believe in a Creator, does your daily life reflect that you see every change—even small ones—as caused by Him? Where might you be living as if changes happen without a cause, forgetting the Preferrer? Commit to recognizing one cause today and thank the One who brought it about.
?
Consider an area of confusion or uncertainty in your faith. What is the 'cause' of that confusion? Is it rooted in a lack of evidence, or in a failure to apply the rational principle that every effect has a cause? What step can you take today to seek the true cause and remove that uncertainty?

The Three Rational Categories and the Possibility of the Universe
Buti defines preponderance without a preponderator and introduces the three categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational judgments (necessary, impossible, possible) and why the universe belongs to the category of possibility, requiring an external preponderator.

Core Idea
The universe is not necessary or impossible, so it needs a cause outside itself.

This lesson introduces the foundational threefold division of all concepts in the mind into necessary, impossible, and possible. Once we see that the universe is possible—neither inevitable nor inconceivable—we realise it cannot exist without something that tips the balance from non-existence to existence. This sets the stage for the proof of God's existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of preponderance without a preponderator
Understand the principle: a change without a cause is rationally impossible. This is the basis of the proof.
2
Identify the three rational categories
Find where the author lists al-wujub, al-istihala, and al-imkan. Note how each is defined by what the mind deems impossible.
These categories are axiomatic in Islamic theology.
3
Classify the universe
See why the universe is possible (mumkin): its non-existence does not lead to a mental contradiction. Therefore it cannot be necessary or impossible.
This is a key step in the argument.
4
Draw the conclusion
Everything possible requires an external preponderator to tip it from non-existence to existence. This points to a cause beyond the universe.
The preponderator is identified as God in the next lesson.

Source Text

، وهو باطل كما

First: The proof of the impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator: And the meaning of preponderance without a preponderator is that a thing runs on a certain course, then changes from its course and turns away from it without the presence of any changer or transformer at all. This is among the matters whose falsehood is clear, and all rational people know that the original rule is the permanence of what was upon what it was, and to change it from its previous state there must be a changer and an effecter that imposes upon it this new state and abrogates its old state. If you have understood this, let us apply this proof to the issue of the existence of God, Mighty and Majestic: All matters and forms supposed in the mind are only characterized by one of three attributes: obligation (al-wujūb), impossibility (al-istiḥāla), and possibility (al-imkān). That which is characterized by obligation is that whose non-existence the mind deems impossible; that which is characterized by impossibility is that whose existence the mind deems impossible; and that which is characterized by possibility is that whose existence and non-existence the mind does not deem impossible. And this universe that we see in its entirety is only of the type of the possible, meaning that the mind affirms that no impossibility follows from assuming its non-existence and sees that it is possible that reasons for its non-existence exist from its origin without that entailing an impossibility that the mind does not accept. Therefore, the existence of the universe in itself is not necessary and is not an inevitable stroke. And everything that is such must have an external effecter that preponderates in it one of the two sides of possibility and removes the other side from it. And this means that this universe, which in its origin was equally receptive to both existence and non-existence, must have an external power affecting it, specifying it for the side of existence, and that power is the power of God, Mighty and Majestic. If you say: I suppose that it came to be by itself without any affecting power from outside, your supposition necessitates the statement of preponderance of a thing without a preponderator for it, as you have known, and it is false as it is, so the supposition that necessitated it also becomes false. And we add further clarification, saying: There is no doubt that there came a time in time when this universe was not a thing mentioned, for absolute non-existence was spread out in the place of existence today, and the meaning of that is that the scale of non-existence was then the preponderant, and the matter was continuous upon that. Then the matter reversed afterwards, and the scale of existence became preponderant over the scale of absolute non-existence. If you say that the world came to be by an inherent power in it without need of an originator, then that means that you are saying that the scale of existence preponderated over the scale of non-existence and the reversal of the matter that was continuous without

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof: the impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator. The author defines it clearly: when something changes without a cause, that is rationally impossible. The proof is then applied to God's existence by first dividing all mental concepts into three categories: necessary (wajib), impossible (mustahil), and possible (mumkin). The universe is shown to be possible (mumkin) because its non-existence does not entail a contradiction. As a possible entity, it requires an external preponderator to tip the balance from non-existence to existence. This preponderator is God. The author then addresses an objection that the universe could exist by itself, showing that this would entail preponderance without a preponderator, which is absurd. Finally, a historical illustration is given: there was a time when the universe did not exist, then it came to exist, indicating a change that requires a preponderator.

الوجوب
الاستحالة
الإمكان
المؤثر الخارجي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'possible' (mumkin) means 'uncertain' or 'probable' in a statistical sense.
Correction: In this context, 'possible' means logically neutral: the mind can accept both its existence and non-existence without contradiction. It does not imply probability.

A) That whose existence the mind deems impossible
B) That whose non-existence the mind deems impossible
C) That whose existence and non-existence the mind does not deem impossible
D) That which exists without a cause

Key Takeaway
The universe is logically possible, so it cannot be its own cause; it requires an external preponderator to bring it into existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The passage says all rational people know that change requires a cause. When you reflect on your own habits, have you been ignoring this principle by assuming you can change without divine assistance?

Applying the Proof: The Universe Needs a Preponderator
Buti refutes the objection of self-existence and uses historical argument to confirm the need for a preponderator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that the universe could exist by itself leads to the absurdity of preponderance without a preponderator, and why the historical timeline confirms the need for a creator.

Core Idea
A change from non-existence to existence without a cause is impossible, so the universe must have a creator.

Now that we have seen the universe is possible, we address a potential objection: perhaps the universe simply came to be on its own. Buti shows that this would mean an effect without a cause, which is impossible. He then reinforces the argument with a historical observation: there was a time when the universe did not exist, then it did—a change that demands a preponderator.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Buti imagines someone saying the universe came to be by itself, without any external influence.
2
Understand the refutation
This claim implies that something changed from non-existence to existence without a cause—a clear case of preponderance without a preponderator, which is impossible.
The earlier principle is applied directly.
3
Examine the historical timeline
Buti points out that there was a time of absolute non-existence, then the universe appeared. This change from non-existence to existence requires a cause.
This illustrates the principle in a concrete way.
4
Conclude the proof
The only remaining possibility is that an external preponderator—God—tipped the balance from non-existence to existence.
This completes the proof of God's existence.

The Balance Analogy: Impossibility of Ex Nihilo Creation Without a Cause
Buti presents a balance analogy to prove that a cause is necessary for any change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the balance analogy demonstrates that something cannot come from nothing without a cause, and why this is known by innate disposition.

Core Idea
A scale cannot tip without a weight; similarly, existence cannot arise from nothing without a cause.

Buti begins by appealing to a universal human intuition: no change occurs without a cause. He illustrates this with the vivid analogy of a perfectly balanced scale that suddenly tilts for no reason. This impossibility mirrors the claim that absolute non-existence could transform into existence without a cause. Let's read the passage to see how this argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the balance analogy and its application to the question of existence.
The stray '· الله' is likely a footnote marker; ignore it.
2
Identify the key analogy
Buti uses two scenarios: (1) a balanced scale tipping without any weight, (2) a scale with a weight behaving contrary to expectation. Understand why both are impossible.
3
Apply the analogy to existence
The main claim: the transformation of non-existence into existence without a cause is as impossible as the absurd scale scenarios. Notice how Buti uses 'pure innate disposition' as the basis.
This is a foundational argument in kalam for the necessity of a Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجود أي عامل لهذا الرجحان أو الانعكاس الطارئ . وهذا أمر يعرف الانسان بطلانه بمحض الفطرة .
إنك لو ذهبت تزعم بأنك قد أمسكت الميزان من حلقه الدقيق وتركت الكفتين فيه بوزن واحد دون وجود أي ثقل إضافي في إحداهما ؛ وبينما الكفتان متساويتان إذا واحدة منهما ترجح والأخرى تطيش دون أي مؤثر خارجي يتصوره الذهن - تركت الناس كلهم يشفقون على فكرك وعقلك . فكيف لو قلت لهم بأنك قد وضعت ثقلاً في إحدى الكفتين ، وبينما أنت تمسك الميزان من حلقه والكفة الثقيلة راجحة تنوء بحملها ، إذا الأمر يختلف : تطيش الثقيلة بثقلها وتهبط الخفيفة رغم خفتها ؟!.
إن القول بأن العدم المطلق المستمر ، تحول فجأة إلى وجود يتفاعل ويتوالد دون أي مسبب خارجي لهذا التحول - ليس بأقل استحالة وغرابة من دعوى صاحب الميزان
·
الله
غير أنك قد علمت أن هذا كله جار على فرض أن المتشكك في وجود يقول كما يعتقد عامة العقلاء بأن العالم حادث ، أي سبقـه عـدم مهما كان عمر هذا الوجود متطاولاً
ولكن ماذا ، لو قال لنا بعد هذه الحجة البدهية الواضحة : فأنا أفرض أن العالم قديم في وجوده هذا ، لا أول له ولا سبق للعدم عليه وبذلك لا توجد إلا كفة واحدة ولا حجة لك تلزمني فيما تقول ؟..
هنا ننتقل إلى الحقيقة الفطرية الثانية
The existence of any factor for this inclination or the accidental reversal. And this is something that man knows its falsehood by pure innate disposition. If you were to claim that you have held the balance from its delicate neck and left the two pans in it with equal weight without the existence of any additional weight in one of them; and while the two pans are equal, suddenly one of them tilts and the other swings without any external influence that the mind can conceive - you would leave all people pitying your thought and intellect. So how would it be if you said to them that you have placed a weight in one of the pans, and while you are holding the balance from its neck and the heavy pan is tilting, groaning under its load, suddenly the matter is different: the heavy one swings with its weight and the light one descends despite its lightness?!. Indeed, the claim that absolute continuous non-existence suddenly turned into an interacting and generating existence without any external cause for this transformation - is not less impossible and strange than the claim of the owner of the balance. · God. However, you have known that all this proceeds on the assumption that the skeptic about existence says, as the general public of rational people believe, that the world is originated, i.e., non-existence preceded it, no matter how long the age of this existence may be. But what if, after this clear self-evident argument, he says to us: I assume that the world is eternal in this existence of it, having no beginning and no non-existence preceding it, and thus there is only one pan and no argument binding me in what you say?.. Here we move to the second innate truth.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a proof by analogy against the possibility of something coming into existence without a cause. Buti begins by stating that the absence of any factor for a change (such as a balance tipping) is known to be false by pure innate disposition. He then illustrates with a balance: if you claim that a perfectly balanced scale tips without any external weight, people would pity your intellect. Even more absurd would be claiming that a scale with a weight in one pan behaves opposite to expectation. This analogy is applied to the claim that absolute non-existence could transform into existence without a cause—such a claim is not less impossible. Buti then notes that this reasoning rests on the assumption that the world is originated (hadith), which is commonly accepted. However, an objector might say the world is eternal (qadim) with no beginning. This objection leads to the second innate truth (the proof against infinite regress), which is introduced in the next lesson. The key point is that the balance analogy demonstrates the necessity of a cause for any change or existence.

Key Terms
عدم

The Objection of an Eternal World and the Transition to the Second Innate Truth
Buti presents an objection to the balance analogy and transitions to the next argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objector's claim that the world is eternal and how Buti responds by moving to the second innate truth.

Core Idea
If the world is eternal, the balance analogy fails; a different argument is needed.

After presenting the balance analogy, Buti anticipates a possible objection: what if the world is eternal with no beginning? In that case, there is no transition from non-existence to existence, so the analogy does not apply. Buti acknowledges this and announces a shift to the 'second innate truth'—which will be a separate proof. Let's read how he sets up this objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice that Buti first states that the previous argument assumes the world is originated (hadith). Then he presents the objector's alternative view: the world is eternal (qadim).
2
Understand the objector's logic
If the world is eternal, there was no non-existence preceding it. So the balance analogy (which compares the transition from non-existence to existence) does not apply. The objector says there is only 'one pan'—meaning no need for a cause because no change.
This is a common skeptical position.
3
Note Buti's response
Buti accepts the objection leads to a different line of reasoning. He says 'here we move to the second innate truth.' This signals that a new argument is needed to refute the eternal world assumption.
The second innate truth will be the argument against infinite regress or the argument from contingency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجود أي عامل لهذا الرجحان أو الانعكاس الطارئ . وهذا أمر يعرف الانسان بطلانه بمحض الفطرة .
إنك لو ذهبت تزعم بأنك قد أمسكت الميزان من حلقه الدقيق وتركت الكفتين فيه بوزن واحد دون وجود أي ثقل إضافي في إحداهما ؛ وبينما الكفتان متساويتان إذا واحدة منهما ترجح والأخرى تطيش دون أي مؤثر خارجي يتصوره الذهن - تركت الناس كلهم يشفقون على فكرك وعقلك . فكيف لو قلت لهم بأنك قد وضعت ثقلاً في إحدى الكفتين ، وبينما أنت تمسك الميزان من حلقه والكفة الثقيلة راجحة تنوء بحملها ، إذا الأمر يختلف : تطيش الثقيلة بثقلها وتهبط الخفيفة رغم خفتها ؟!.

The existence of any factor for this inclination or the accidental reversal. And this is something that man knows its falsehood by pure innate disposition. If you were to claim that you have held the balance from its delicate neck and left the two pans in it with equal weight without the existence of any additional weight in one of them; and while the two pans are equal, suddenly one of them tilts and the other swings without any external influence that the mind can conceive - you would leave all people pitying your thought and intellect. So how would it be if you said to them that you have placed a weight in one of the pans, and while you are holding the balance from its neck and the heavy pan is tilting, groaning under its load, suddenly the matter is different: the heavy one swings with its weight and the light one descends despite its lightness?!. Indeed, the claim that absolute continuous non-existence suddenly turned into an interacting and generating existence without any external cause for this transformation - is not less impossible and strange than the claim of the owner of the balance. · God. However, you have known that all this proceeds on the assumption that the skeptic about existence says, as the general public of rational people believe, that the world is originated, i.e., non-existence preceded it, no matter how long the age of this existence may be. But what if, after this clear self-evident argument, he says to us: I assume that the world is eternal in this existence of it, having no beginning and no non-existence preceding it, and thus there is only one pan and no argument binding me in what you say?.. Here we move to the second innate truth.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a proof by analogy against the possibility of something coming into existence without a cause. Buti begins by stating that the absence of any factor for a change (such as a balance tipping) is known to be false by pure innate disposition. He then illustrates with a balance: if you claim that a perfectly balanced scale tips without any external weight, people would pity your intellect. Even more absurd would be claiming that a scale with a weight in one pan behaves opposite to expectation. This analogy is applied to the claim that absolute non-existence could transform into existence without a cause—such a claim is not less impossible. Buti then notes that this reasoning rests on the assumption that the world is originated (hadith), which is commonly accepted. However, an objector might say the world is eternal (qadim) with no beginning. This objection leads to the second innate truth (the proof against infinite regress), which is introduced in the next lesson. The key point is that the balance analogy demonstrates the necessity of a cause for any change or existence.

This passage reveals Buti's intellectual honesty in admitting the limitation of the first argument. Are you honest about the limits of your own understanding, or do you pretend your arguments are airtight? What might God be teaching you through the gaps in your reasoning right now?
