The Proof Against Infinite Regress (Burhan Batalan al-Tasalsul)
Buti refutes infinite regress with logical proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why infinite regress is impossible and how it leads to the necessity of a Necessary Being.

Core Idea
An infinite chain of contingents still needs a Necessary Cause.

Buti presents the second innate truth: the logical impossibility of an infinite regress. This argument refutes the idea that the world could be self-caused through an endless chain. By examining the nature of contingent beings, Buti shows that even an infinite series requires an external source of existence, pointing to the Necessary Being.

Guided Path
1
Understand the assumption
Read the passage's opening where Buti describes the worldview implying infinite regress: self-generation without beginning.
This sets up what is being refuted.
2
Grasp the definition of tasalsul
Focus on Buti's definition: each thing is effect of prior and cause of next, with no ultimate source.
This is key to understanding why it's impossible.
3
Follow the logical refutation
Buti argues that no matter how long, the series of possibles remains contingent, so needs an external cause. Then he presents two options and disproves the first.
The conclusion is that the series must originate from a Necessary Being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً - برهان بطلان التسلسل :
نقول له عندئذ : إنك تعني إذاً أن هذا العالم مستمر بحكم التوالد الذاتي الذي لا أول له . وهذا الفرض يستلزم إمكان التسلسل ، وقد علم العقلاء كلهم بحكم البداهة أن التسلسل محال ، فيتبيَّن بذلك استحالة الفرضية التي أدت إليه ومعنى التسلسل ، فرض أن المخلوقات كلها متوالدة عن بعضها إلى ما لا نهاية ، بحيث يكون كل واحد منها معلولاً لما قبله وعلـة لما بعده دون أن هذه السلسلة أخيراً من علة واجبة الوجود هي التي تضفي التأثير المتوالد على سائر تلك الحلقات
تنبع
مرجح
فهذا الفرض ، باطل يحكم العقل باستحالته بالضرورة . إذ إن سلسلة المخلوقات الممكنة مهما طالت وطالت ، فإن استمرار طولها لا يخرجها على كل حال عن كونها ممكنة . والممكنات لا بد لرجحان أحد طرفي الإمكان فيها من كما قلنا . فهذه السلسلة الطويلة التي تقول إنها ماضية في غور سحيق لا ينتهي ، ، مكونة من حلقات كل منها لم يكن يوجد لولا أن الحلقة السابقة عليها أعطتها الحياة والوجود ، وتلك التي أعطتها الحياة كذلك . إذاً فحلقـات السلسلة كلها لا تأثير ذاتي في واحدة منها مهما طالت ، وإذا فلكي نصدق أنها موجودة لا بد أن ننتظر ظهور المؤثر الخارجي الذي أمد السلسلة بالحياة التي راحت بدورها تنتقل من حلقة إلى حلقة . وإلا كان لا بد من الجزم بأحـد أمرين : إما أن هذه السلسلة كلها مفقودة ، إذ لم يثبت وجود ذلك الذي قذف فيها الحياة ، وإما أنها موجودة ولكنها تنبع أخيراً من ذات واجبة الوجود تؤثر فيها ولا تتأثر هي بشيء . فأما الأمر الأول فظاهر البطلان ، لأن الحس والمشاهدة يكذبانه ، والعالم موجود وتوالد العلل شيء مرئي ومحسوس . بقي الأمر الثاني وهو تيقن أن لا بد له من مصدر ذاتي وهبه الحياة والقدرة على الحركة والتطور والتوالد ، فبطل التسلسل المذكور .
Second - The proof of the impossibility of infinite regress: We say to him then: You mean, therefore, that this world is continuous by virtue of self-generation that has no beginning. And this assumption necessitates the possibility of infinite regress, and all rational people have known by virtue of intuition that infinite regress is impossible, so the impossibility of the assumption that led to it becomes clear. And the meaning of infinite regress is the assumption that all created things are generated from each other ad infinitum, such that each one of them is an effect of what precedes it and a cause of what follows it, without this series ultimately originating from a necessary being that bestows the generative influence on all those links. [تنبع] [مرجح] So this assumption is false; the mind judges its impossibility necessarily. For the series of possible creatures, however long it extends, its continued length does not remove it in any case from being possible. And possibles require, for the preponderance of one of the two sides of possibility, as we have said. So this long series that you say is proceeding in a bottomless abyss, composed of links each of which would not exist were it not that the previous link gave it life and existence, and that which gave it life likewise. Therefore, all the links of the series have no intrinsic effect in any one of them, no matter how long. And if so, in order for us to believe that they exist, we must await the appearance of the external influencer that supplied the series with the life that in turn began to transfer from link to link. Otherwise, one of two things must be asserted: either this entire series is non-existent, since the existence of that which cast life into it has not been established, or it exists but ultimately originates from a self-necessary being that influences it and is not influenced by anything. As for the first possibility, its falsehood is apparent, because sensory perception and observation falsify it, and the world exists and the generation of causes is something visible and sensible. The second possibility remains, which is the certainty that it must have a self-source that bestowed upon it life and the ability to move, develop, and generate. So the mentioned infinite regress is invalidated.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage presents the second innate truth: the proof against infinite regress (burtahan batalan al-tasalsul). Buti begins by addressing an objector who claims the world is eternal through self-generation. This assumption implies the possibility of an infinite regress, which rational people know intuitively to be impossible. Buti defines infinite regress as the assumption that all created things are generated from each other ad infinitum, with no ultimate necessary being. This assumption is false because the entire series consists of possible beings (mumkinat), and possibles need an external cause for their existence. Even if the series is infinitely long, it remains composed of contingent beings, each dependent on the previous. Thus, to account for the existence of the series, we must either accept that the series does not exist (which contradicts observation) or that it ultimately originates from a necessary being (wajib al-wujud) that gives it existence and causal power. Since the world clearly exists, the second alternative is necessary, and infinite regress is invalidated. The key is that an infinite chain of contingents cannot exist without a necessary cause.

تسلسل
ممكن
واجب الوجود
علة
معلول

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Infinite regress is possible in mathematics, so it should be possible in actual existence.
Correction: Buti argues that actual existence of contingent beings cannot form an infinite chain without a necessary cause. Mathematical infinities are abstract, not causally dependent.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Buti gives for the impossibility of infinite regress?
A) Because the universe had a beginning
B) Because an infinite chain of possible beings still requires an external necessary cause
C) Because the mind cannot conceive of infinity
D) Because the world is eternal

Key Takeaway
Infinite regress of contingent beings is impossible; a Necessary Being must exist as the ultimate cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Buti argues that every contingent being depends on an external cause. Look at your own existence: what are the things you rely on daily? Have you ever truly considered that your very existence moment by moment is utterly dependent on the One who is self-sufficient? Write down one specific area of your life where you act as if you are self-sufficient, and commit to acknowledging your need for Allah in that area today.
?
The proof shows that an infinite chain of causes cannot exist—there must be a First Cause. How does this logical certainty confront the way you live? Do you live as though your life has a definite purpose from that First Cause, or do you drift as if it were an endless chain of random events? What concrete step can you take today to align your daily actions with the reality that your existence originates from Allah?

Proof against Infinite Regress (Tasalsul)
Buti proves the impossibility of an infinite causal chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an infinite chain of contingent causes is impossible and why a necessary first cause is required.

Core Idea
An infinite chain of possible beings cannot explain its own existence.

Buti presents a foundational argument for the necessity of a first cause. He demonstrates that assuming an infinite regress of causes leads to a logical contradiction. This lesson guides you through his proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the full translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument from hypothesis to conclusion.
Focus on the definition of tasalsul and the two alternatives presented.
2
Understand the meaning of tasalsul
Buti defines tasalsul as an infinite chain where each being is effect of the previous and cause of the next, without an ultimate necessary cause. Grasp this before proceeding.
3
Examine the core argument
Notice how Buti argues that even an infinite chain of possible things remains contingent and requires an external preponderator. Why can't contingency be self-resolving?
Contingency means the being could exist or not; something must tip the balance.
4
Follow the two alternatives
Buti presents two possibilities: either the chain is nonexistent (contradicted by observation) or it derives from a necessary existent. Trace how he eliminates the first alternative.
The first alternative is shown false by the evident existence of the world.
5
Conclude the necessity of a first cause
The second alternative is the only remaining logical possibility, proving that infinite regress is impossible and a necessary cause must exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا أول له . وهذا الفرض يستلزم إمكان التسلسل ، وقد علم العقلاء كلهم بحكم البداهة أن التسلسل محال ، فيتبيَّن بذلك استحالة الفرضية التي أدت إليه ومعنى التسلسل ، فرض أن المخلوقات كلها متوالدة عن بعضها إلى ما لا نهاية ، بحيث يكون كل واحد منها معلولاً لما قبله وعلـة لما بعده دون أن هذه السلسلة أخيراً من علة واجبة الوجود هي التي تضفي التأثير المتوالد على سائر تلك الحلقات [تنبع؟] [مرجح؟] فهذا الفرض ، باطل يحكم العقل باستحالته بالضرورة . إذ إن سلسلة المخلوقات الممكنة مهما طالت وطالت ، فإن استمرار طولها لا يخرجها على كل حال عن كونها ممكنة . والممكنات لا بد لرجحان أحد طرفي الإمكان فيها من [؟] كما قلنا . فهذه السلسلة الطويلة التي تقول إنها ماضية في غور سحيق لا ينتهي ، مكونة من حلقات كل منها لم يكن يوجد لولا أن الحلقة السابقة عليها أعطتها الحياة والوجود ، وتلك التي أعطتها الحياة كذلك . إذاً فحلقـات السلسلة كلها لا تأثير ذاتي في واحدة منها مهما طالت ، وإذا فلكي نصدق أنها موجودة لا بد أن ننتظر ظهور المؤثر الخارجي الذي أمد السلسلة بالحياة التي راحت بدورها تنتقل من حلقة إلى حلقة . وإلا كان لا بد من الجزم بأحـد أمرين : إما أن هذه السلسلة كلها مفقودة ، إذ لم يثبت وجود ذلك الذي قذف فيها الحياة ، وإما أنها موجودة ولكنها تنبع أخيراً من ذات واجبة الوجود تؤثر فيها ولا تتأثر هي بشيء . فأما الأمر الأول فظاهر البطلان ، لأن الحس والمشاهدة يكذبانه ، والعالم موجود وتوالد العلل شيء مرئي ومحسوس . بقي الأمر الثاني وهو تيقن أن لا بد له من مصدر ذاتي وهبه الحياة والقدرة على الحركة والتطور والتوالد ، فبطل التسلسل المذكور .
It has no beginning. This assumption necessitates the possibility of infinite regress (tasalsul), and all rational people know by the judgment of intuition (badaha) that infinite regress is impossible. Thus the impossibility of the hypothesis that led to it and the meaning of infinite regress become clear: the assumption that all created things are generated from each other without end, such that each one is an effect (ma'lul) of what precedes it and a cause ('illa) of what follows it, without this chain [ending?] [preponderator?] ultimately in a necessary existent (wajib al-wujud) cause that imparts the generative influence on all those links. So this assumption is false; reason judges its impossibility necessarily. For the chain of possible (mumkin) creatures, however long it extends, its prolonged length does not, in any case, remove it from being possible. And possibles must have a preponderator for one of the two possibilities, as we said. So this long chain, which you say extends into an unending deep abyss, composed of links each of which would not exist were it not that the preceding link gave it life and existence, and that which gave it life as well. Therefore, all the links of the chain have no intrinsic effect in any of them, no matter how long it extends. And so, for us to believe that they exist, we must await the appearance of the external agent that supplied the chain with the life that then began to transfer from link to link. Otherwise, we must decide one of two things: either this entire chain is nonexistent, since the existence of that which cast life into it has not been established; or it exists but ultimately derives from a self-subsistent necessary existent that affects it and is not affected by anything. As for the first alternative, its falsehood is apparent, because sense perception and observation belie it, and the world exists and the generation of causes is something visible and observable. So the second alternative remains: the certainty that it must have an intrinsic source that granted it life and the capacity for motion, development, and generation. Thus the aforementioned infinite regress is invalidated.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a proof against infinite regress (tasalsul) in causal chains. Buti begins by stating that assuming a chain with no first cause leads to infinite regress, which is intuitively impossible. He defines tasalsul as the assumption that creatures generate from each other infinitely without a necessary cause at the end. He argues that even an infinite chain of contingent beings remains contingent and requires an external preponderator. He presents two alternatives: either the chain is nonexistent (contradicted by observation) or it originates from a necessary existent that imparts existence and causality. The proof concludes that tasalsul is false, affirming the necessity of a first cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite chain of contingent causes could be self-sufficient and explain its own existence.
Correction: Buti shows that even an infinite chain of possible beings remains contingent; each link depends on a preceding cause, and the entire chain requires an external preponderator to exist.

Checkpoint

B) Either the chain is nonexistent or it derives from a necessary existent.
C) Either the chain is self-caused or it has no beginning.
D) Either the chain is finite or it is infinite.

Key Takeaway
An infinite regress of contingent beings is impossible because each link remains contingent and requires a cause; thus a necessary first cause must exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the chain of causes in your own life—your parents, your teachers, the events that shaped you—do you ever feel a deep unease that this chain, if endless, would leave you ultimately unsupported? How does Buti’s argument force you to confront the need for a Cause that is not itself caused?
?
Have you ever caught yourself living as if the world runs on autopilot, as if causes and effects just keep going without a constant Sustainer? If the entire existence of every link depends on a Necessary Existent from moment to moment, what does that demand from you in terms of reliance and gratitude right now?
?
Buti says that rational people know by intuition that infinite regress is impossible. But do you truly feel the impossibility in your heart? Or do you sometimes entertain the thought that maybe things could go on forever without a First Cause? What would it cost you to sincerely admit that your own contingent existence cries out for a Necessary Being?

First Analogy: The Chain of Proofs
Buti's first analogy: infinite regress of proofs requires a self-evident foundation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how an infinite regress of proofs fails to establish any truth, and why a self-evident foundation (بداهة) is necessary.

Core Idea
Infinite regress of proofs is like a chain of shadows — no truth without a self-evident origin.

Buti begins with a simple scenario: someone claims certainty but cannot provide a proof that doesn't rely on another proof. This analogy exposes the logical impossibility of an infinite regress. It shows that without a self-evident truth (بداهة) as a foundation, no claim can be established.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, paying attention to the progression of proofs and the conditional structure.
Notice the conditional: if no foundational truth, then the claim is denied.
2
Identify key elements
Distinguish between the claimed truth, the chain of proofs, and the need for a self-evident foundation (بداهة).
The foundation is a necessary truth known by intuition.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Buti compares the chain to shadows waiting for their origin; without origin, shadows don't exist.
Dependent proofs cannot generate certainty on their own.
4
Apply to the broader argument
The same logic applies to causes in the universe — a chain of dependent causes requires a self-sufficient first cause.
This analogy establishes the principle for the following analogies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ - لو وقفتُ أدعي أمامك حقيقة علمية أستيقنها، ولما سألتني عن الدليل ذكرت لك برهاناً هو نفسه دعوى مجهولة تتوقف على برهان، ولما سألتني عن برهان هذا البرهان، جئتك ببرهان مثله في التوقف على برهان آخر.. وهكذا إلى ما لا نهاية، أي دون أن تنتهي هذه البراهين كلها أخيراً إلى حقيقة ضرورية معروفة بالبداهة، فإنك تكذبني في دعوى اليقين بهذه الحقيقة، بل تكذبني في وجودها أصلاً، إذ لم يقم عليها أي برهان بعد، وكل البراهين المتسلسلة التي فرضنا أن لا نهاية لها ليست إلا ظلالاً تنتظر أصلها الأول، فإن لم يوجد ذلك الأصل فهذه الظلال نفسها غير موجودة، ومن ثم فإن الحقيقة المدعاة أيضاً تكون غير موجودة.
٢ - إذا رأيت رقماً حسابياً طويلاً، يتراصف فيه عدد كبير من الأصفار، فإنك تسرع لتنظر قبل كل شيء إلى الرقم الذاتي الأول الذي رصفت الأصفار عن يمينه، وما لم تقع عينك على ذلك الرقم فإنك لا تعطي تلك الأصفار أي قيمة حسابية. فلماذا؟ ذلك لأنك تعلم أن الصفر وحده لا يحوي أي قيمة عددية بحد ذاته، وإنما يستمد القيمة من الصفر الذي إلى يساره، وهو أيضاً إنما يستمد القيمة العددية من الصفر الثالث فالرابع فالخامس... إلى أن تنتهي الأصفار برقم عددي كالواحد فما فوق. فهذا الرقم هو الذي يملك قيمة ذاتية في داخله، وهو الذي يضفي الحياة والقيمة على الأصفار المتسلسلة التي عن يمينه. فلو فرضنا أن سلسلة الأصفار لم تنته إلى رقم عددي يملك قيمة ذاتية، فهي أصفار خالية عن أي قيمة بل عن أي معنى من معاني الوجود. وافتراض التسلسل اللانهائي فيها لا يغير من طبيعة الحال ولا يجعل لها أي قيمة.
٣ - أبصرت في دار صديقك نباتاً ذا زهر جميل ورائحة زكية، ولما سألته أين وقع على هذه الزهرة الجميلة، قال إنها فرع أخذه من أصل عند دار جاره، ولما سألت الجار أجابك هو الآخر بأن الذي عنده ليس إلا فسخاً أيضاً حصل عليه من بيت أحد أصدقائه، ثم أجابك الثالث أيضاً بمثل جواب الثاني، وهكذا أجاب الرابع فالخامس فالسادس.. ونفرض أن السلسلة استمرت على هذه الشاكلة. كل منهم يجيبك بأن الذي عنده ليس إلا فسخاً من غيره، وعبثاً رحت مع هذه السلسلة لتبحث عن أصل هذا النبت ومولده الذي أعطاه الظهور والتكوين وقابلية التفرع بادئ ذي بدء، إذ قيل لك إن سلسلة هذا التفرع والتفاسخ ماضية إلى غير نهاية.. فما الذي يحكم به عقلك على هذا الكلام عند أدنى تفكير؟ لا ريب أنه يحكم بكذب هذا الكلام. ذلك لأن التفرع مهما توالد وتكاثر فإنه لا يكون إلا نتيجة وجود أصل ثابت بنفسه يمد تلك الفروع بالوجود أو الحياة؛ وإذ قيل: إنه لا يوجد له أصل وفرضنا أن القائل صادق، فمعنى ذلك لم يولد بعد، وإذاً فلا وجود لشيء من هذه التفرعات المزعومة أيضاً؛ أما إذا كنت تجد فروع النبات بعينك فمعنى ذلك أن له أصلاً ذاتياً أمدَّ هذه الفروع كلها بالوجود مهما كان هذا الأصل بعيداً ومهما كنت لا تتذكره أو تقف عليه. إن أي عاقل يدرك أن تسلسل العلل التي تكتسب القدرة على العلية من العلة التي قبلها، مثل تسلسل الأصفار وتسلسل فروع النبات وتسلسل البراهين المذكورة. ولذا فإن أي عاقل لا يستطيع أن يزعم أن وجود العالم كله ليس قائماً إلا على سلسلة متوالدة من غيرها دون أن يكون قبلها مؤثر ذاتي خارج عن حقيقتها واجب الوجود، إلا إذا كان له أن يزعم بأن قيمة المليون لم تتكون إلا من أصفار تتعاور القيمة فيما بينها دون أن تستند إلى رقم ذاتي قبلها، أو أن يزعم بأن الورد المتوافر في الحدائق والبيوت، ليس في أصله إلا فروعاً مأخوذة من بعضها دون أن ترجع إلى نواة كانت قد أمدتها بأصل الوجود.
1. If I were to stand and claim before you a scientific truth of which I am certain, and when you ask me for the proof I mention to you a proof that is itself an unknown claim dependent on a proof, and when you ask me for the proof of this proof I bring you a proof like it in being dependent on another proof, and so on ad infinitum, i.e. without all these proofs finally terminating in a necessary truth known by intuition, then you would deny my claim of certainty about this truth, rather you would deny its existence entirely, since no proof has yet been established for it, and all the sequential proofs that we have supposed are endless are nothing but shadows waiting for their first origin; if that origin does not exist, then these shadows themselves are non-existent, and consequently the claimed truth is also non-existent.
2. If you see a long arithmetic number in which a large number of zeros are arranged, you hasten before everything to look at the first self-subsistent digit on whose right the zeros are arranged, and unless your eye falls upon that digit you do not give those zeros any arithmetic value. Why? Because you know that zero alone contains no numerical value in itself, but it derives value from the zero to its left, and that zero also derives numerical value from the third, fourth, fifth, until the zeros terminate at a numerical digit like one or above. This digit is the one that possesses intrinsic value within itself, and it is the one that imparts life and value to the sequential zeros to its right. If we suppose that the chain of zeros does not terminate in a numerical digit possessing intrinsic value, they are zeros devoid of any value, indeed devoid of any meaning of existence. And the assumption of infinite succession in them does not change the nature of the case nor give them any value.
3. You saw in your friend’s house a plant with beautiful flowers and fragrant scent, and when you asked him where he got this beautiful flower, he said it is a branch he took from a root at his neighbor’s house. When you asked the neighbor, he answered you likewise that what he has is but a cutting obtained from a friend’s house. Then the third answered you likewise, and so the fourth, fifth, sixth answer. Suppose the chain continues in this manner; each of them answers you that what he has is but a cutting from another. In vain did you go along this chain to search for the origin of this plant and its birthplace that gave it appearance, formation, and ability to branch in the first place, since you were told that the chain of this branching and cutting continues ad infinitum. What does your mind judge about this statement at the slightest reflection? Undoubtedly it judges this statement false. That is because branching, however much it proliferates and multiplies, is only a result of the existence of a self- established origin that supplies those branches with existence or life. If it is said that it has no origin and we suppose the speaker is truthful, that means it has not yet been born, and then none of these alleged branchings exist. But if you see the plant’s branches with your own eye, that means it has a self-subsistent origin that supplied all these branches with existence, however distant that origin may be and even if you do not remember it or come upon it. Every rational person realizes that the chain of causes that acquire the power of causality from the cause before it is like the chain of zeros, the chain of plant branches, and the proofs mentioned. Therefore, no rational person can claim that the existence of the entire universe rests only on a chain generated from each other without there being before it a self-subsistent effecter outside its reality, necessarily existent, unless he can claim that the value of a million is only composed of zeros exchanging value among themselves without being based on a preceding self-subsistent digit, or that the roses abundant in gardens and houses originate only from branches taken from each other without going back to a seed that supplied them with the origin of existence.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents three analogies to demonstrate the impossibility of an infinite regress of causes and to prove the necessity of a First Cause (God). Each analogy illustrates the same logical principle: a chain of dependent items cannot exist without a self-subsistent foundation. The first analogy concerns a chain of proofs. If every proof depends on another proof ad infinitum, no truth is ever established. The only way to have certainty is to reach a self-evident truth (بداهة) that requires no further proof. Without such a foundation, the entire chain is merely shadows waiting for a non-existent origin, so the claimed truth cannot exist. The second analogy uses zeros in a number. Zeros on their own have no value; they derive value from a non-zero digit to their left. If the chain of zeros never ends with a digit, the number has no value. Infinite succession does not create value. The third analogy describes a plant branch traced back through cuttings. If each cutting comes from another cutting without end, there is no original plant that generated all the branches. Yet we see the branches exist, so there must be an original root that supplied existence. The conclusion states that every rational person sees the similarity between these examples and the chain of causes in the universe. Causes that acquire their causal power from prior causes cannot go on infinitely. There must be a self-subsistent effecter (مؤثر ذاتي) outside the chain, who is necessarily existent (واجب الوجود). Denying this would be like claiming a million arises from zeros without a digit, or that flowers come only from cuttings without an original seed. The passage uses familiar, concrete examples to make the abstract argument about the necessity of a First Cause accessible.

Key Terms
برهان
بداهة
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite chain of proofs can eventually establish a truth if it goes on forever.
Correction: No, because each proof depends on another; without a self-evident foundation, there is no actual proof for any claim.

Checkpoint
According to the first analogy, what happens if the chain of proofs never ends in a self-evident truth?
A) The claim is uncertain but may be true.
B) The claim is shown to be true.
C) The claim is denied and considered non-existent.
D) The chain continues but eventually provides certainty.

Key Takeaway
Without a self-evident foundation, an infinite chain of proofs cannot establish any truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your deepest beliefs about God, are any of them merely based on a chain of arguments that you have not traced back to a self-evident foundation? What would it cost you to examine that chain today?
?
If you discovered that a core belief you hold is actually like a shadow waiting for an origin that doesn't exist, would you have the courage to let it go? What would that mean for how you live tomorrow?
?
Buti says that without a self-evident origin, the claimed truth is non-existent. Is there any area of your life where you are building certainty on an infinite regress of excuses or justifications rather than on the bedrock of truth? What step will you take to anchor yourself in what is real?

Allah's Existence
beginner

Second Analogy: The Chain of Zeros
Buti's second analogy: zeros must terminate in a non-zero digit to have value.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the zero analogy and how it illustrates that value (existence) cannot arise from a chain of dependent entities without a self-subsistent source.

Core Idea
A chain of zeros has no value without a non-zero digit — just as dependent causes need a self-sufficient cause.

Buti's second analogy uses a familiar mathematical concept: zeros in a number have no value unless anchored by a non-zero digit. This powerfully illustrates that an infinite regress of dependent entities cannot generate existence without a self-subsistent foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the logic of how zeros derive value.
Consider why zero alone has no value.
2
Identify the key elements
Recognize that each zero gets its value from the digit to its left, but ultimately this chain must end in a non-zero digit.
The non-zero digit possesses intrinsic value.
3
Reflect on the conclusion about infinite succession
Buti states that even infinite zeros cannot generate value without a terminating digit.
The assumption of infinity does not change the lack of value.
4
Apply to the causal chain
Just as zeros need a non-zero digit, dependent causes in the universe require a self-subsistent First Cause.
This analogy reinforces the necessity of a Self-Existent Being.

1. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite chain of zeros can represent a large number if there are infinitely many.
Correction: No, because each zero has no intrinsic value; even infinite zeros cannot create value without a non-zero digit.

Checkpoint
What is the role of the non-zero digit in the zero analogy?
A) It is arbitrary; the zeros could still have value.
B) It provides the intrinsic value that zeros lack.
C) It is the first zero in the sequence.
D) It is optional if the zeros are infinite.

Key Takeaway
Zero cannot generate value; it must be grounded in a self-subsistent non-zero digit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that every good thing in your life is like a zero—it has no lasting value unless anchored in Allah. What is one blessing you are currently treating as if it has intrinsic value? How will you consciously redirect its meaning to Allah today?
?
Buti says that without the non-zero digit, all zeros are valueless. Think of a fear or anxiety that consumes you. If you honestly trace its roots, does it ultimately rest on something that is itself dependent? How does seeing Allah as the only Self-Subsistent change your response to that fear?
?
The analogy forces you to confront: are you building your life on an infinite regress of zeros—hoping that more causes will eventually produce meaning? Commit to one concrete action this week that reminds you that only Allah is the source of true existence and value.

Third Analogy and Conclusion: Plant Branches and the First Cause
Buti's third analogy and conclusion: all dependent causes must originate in a self-subsistent First Cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the plant branching analogy and the concluding generalization demonstrate that the entire universe requires a First Cause that is self-subsistent and necessarily existent.

Core Idea
Branches must trace back to an original root; the universe requires a Self-Subsistent Origin.

Buti's third analogy uses plant cuttings to show that every branch depends on an original root. He then generalizes: the same logic applies to causal chains in the universe. The conclusion unifies all three analogies to assert the necessity of a self-subsistent effecter (مؤثر ذاتي) — the Necessary Existent (واجب الوجود).

Guided Path
1
Read the plant analogy
Read the scenario about tracing a plant branch through successive cuttings, considering the chain of dependence.
Notice that each cutting is taken from a previous plant.
2
Understand the mind's judgment
Buti asks: what does your mind judge about an infinite chain of cuttings? It judges it false because branching requires an original root.
The existence of the observed branches proves there is an origin.
3
Identify the generalization
Buti extends the analogy: the chain of causes in the universe is like the chain of branches, zeros, and proofs.
All dependent things must originate from a self-subsistent cause.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The last sentences emphasize that denying a First Cause is as absurd as claiming a million comes from zeros or flowers from cuttings without a seed.
Thus, the Necessary Existent (واجب الوجود) is unavoidable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ - لو وقفتُ أدعي أمامك حقيقة علمية أستيقنها، ولما سألتني عن الدليل ذكرت لك برهاناً هو نفسه دعوى مجهولة تتوقف على برهان، ولما سألتني عن برهان هذا البرهان، جئتك ببرهان مثله في التوقف على برهان آخر.. وهكذا إلى ما لا نهاية، أي دون أن تنتهي هذه البراهين كلها أخيراً إلى حقيقة ضرورية معروفة بالبداهة، فإنك تكذبني في دعوى اليقين بهذه الحقيقة، بل تكذبني في وجودها أصلاً، إذ لم يقم عليها أي برهان بعد، وكل البراهين المتسلسلة التي فرضنا أن لا نهاية لها ليست إلا ظلالاً تنتظر أصلها الأول، فإن لم يوجد ذلك الأصل فهذه الظلال نفسها غير موجودة، ومن ثم فإن الحقيقة المدعاة أيضاً تكون غير موجودة.
٢ - إذا رأيت رقماً حسابياً طويلاً، يتراصف فيه عدد كبير من الأصفار، فإنك تسرع لتنظر قبل كل شيء إلى الرقم الذاتي الأول الذي رصفت الأصفار عن يمينه، وما لم تقع عينك على ذلك الرقم فإنك لا تعطي تلك الأصفار أي قيمة حسابية. فلماذا؟ ذلك لأنك تعلم أن الصفر وحده لا يحوي أي قيمة عددية بحد ذاته، وإنما يستمد القيمة من الصفر الذي إلى يساره، وهو أيضاً إنما يستمد القيمة العددية من الصفر الثالث فالرابع فالخامس... إلى أن تنتهي الأصفار برقم عددي كالواحد فما فوق. فهذا الرقم هو الذي يملك قيمة ذاتية في داخله، وهو الذي يضفي الحياة والقيمة على الأصفار المتسلسلة التي عن يمينه. فلو فرضنا أن سلسلة الأصفار لم تنته إلى رقم عددي يملك قيمة ذاتية، فهي أصفار خالية عن أي قيمة بل عن أي معنى من معاني الوجود. وافتراض التسلسل اللانهائي فيها لا يغير من طبيعة الحال ولا يجعل لها أي قيمة.
٣ - أبصرت في دار صديقك نباتاً ذا زهر جميل ورائحة زكية، ولما سألته أين وقع على هذه الزهرة الجميلة، قال إنها فرع أخذه من أصل عند دار جاره، ولما سألت الجار أجابك هو الآخر بأن الذي عنده ليس إلا فسخاً أيضاً حصل عليه من بيت أحد أصدقائه، ثم أجابك الثالث أيضاً بمثل جواب الثاني، وهكذا أجاب الرابع فالخامس فالسادس.. ونفرض أن السلسلة استمرت على هذه الشاكلة. كل منهم يجيبك بأن الذي عنده ليس إلا فسخاً من غيره، وعبثاً رحت مع هذه السلسلة لتبحث عن أصل هذا النبت ومولده الذي أعطاه الظهور والتكوين وقابلية التفرع بادئ ذي بدء، إذ قيل لك إن سلسلة هذا التفرع والتفاسخ ماضية إلى غير نهاية.. فما الذي يحكم به عقلك على هذا الكلام عند أدنى تفكير؟ لا ريب أنه يحكم بكذب هذا الكلام. ذلك لأن التفرع مهما توالد وتكاثر فإنه لا يكون إلا نتيجة وجود أصل ثابت بنفسه يمد تلك الفروع بالوجود أو الحياة؛ وإذ قيل: إنه لا يوجد له أصل وفرضنا أن القائل صادق، فمعنى ذلك لم يولد بعد، وإذاً فلا وجود لشيء من هذه التفرعات المزعومة أيضاً؛ أما إذا كنت تجد فروع النبات بعينك فمعنى ذلك أن له أصلاً ذاتياً أمدَّ هذه الفروع كلها بالوجود مهما كان هذا الأصل بعيداً ومهما كنت لا تتذكره أو تقف عليه. إن أي عاقل يدرك أن تسلسل العلل التي تكتسب القدرة على العلية من العلة التي قبلها، مثل تسلسل الأصفار وتسلسل فروع النبات وتسلسل البراهين المذكورة. ولذا فإن أي عاقل لا يستطيع أن يزعم أن وجود العالم كله ليس قائماً إلا على سلسلة متوالدة من غيرها دون أن يكون قبلها مؤثر ذاتي خارج عن حقيقتها واجب الوجود، إلا إذا كان له أن يزعم بأن قيمة المليون لم تتكون إلا من أصفار تتعاور القيمة فيما بينها دون أن تستند إلى رقم ذاتي قبلها، أو أن يزعم بأن الورد المتوافر في الحدائق والبيوت، ليس في أصله إلا فروعاً مأخوذة من بعضها دون أن ترجع إلى نواة كانت قد أمدتها بأصل الوجود.
1. If I were to stand and claim before you a scientific truth of which I am certain, and when you ask me for the proof I mention to you a proof that is itself an unknown claim dependent on a proof, and when you ask me for the proof of this proof I bring you a proof like it in being dependent on another proof, and so on ad infinitum, i.e. without all these proofs finally terminating in a necessary truth known by intuition, then you would deny my claim of certainty about this truth, rather you would deny its existence entirely, since no proof has yet been established for it, and all the sequential proofs that we have supposed are endless are nothing but shadows waiting for their first origin; if that origin does not exist, then these shadows themselves are non-existent, and consequently the claimed truth is also non-existent.
2. If you see a long arithmetic number in which a large number of zeros are arranged, you hasten before everything to look at the first self-subsistent digit on whose right the zeros are arranged, and unless your eye falls upon that digit you do not give those zeros any arithmetic value. Why? Because you know that zero alone contains no numerical value in itself, but it derives value from the zero to its left, and that zero also derives numerical value from the third, fourth, fifth, until the zeros terminate at a numerical digit like one or above. This digit is the one that possesses intrinsic value within itself, and it is the one that imparts life and value to the sequential zeros to its right. If we suppose that the chain of zeros does not terminate in a numerical digit possessing intrinsic value, they are zeros devoid of any value, indeed devoid of any meaning of existence. And the assumption of infinite succession in them does not change the nature of the case nor give them any value.
3. You saw in your friend’s house a plant with beautiful flowers and fragrant scent, and when you asked him where he got this beautiful flower, he said it is a branch he took from a root at his neighbor’s house. When you asked the neighbor, he answered you likewise that what he has is but a cutting obtained from a friend’s house. Then the third answered you likewise, and so the fourth, fifth, sixth answer. Suppose the chain continues in this manner; each of them answers you that what he has is but a cutting from another. In vain did you go along this chain to search for the origin of this plant and its birthplace that gave it appearance, formation, and ability to branch in the first place, since you were told that the chain of this branching and cutting continues ad infinitum. What does your mind judge about this statement at the slightest reflection? Undoubtedly it judges this statement false. That is because branching, however much it proliferates and multiplies, is only a result of the existence of a self- established origin that supplies those branches with existence or life. If it is said that it has no origin and we suppose the speaker is truthful, that means it has not yet been born, and then none of these alleged branchings exist. But if you see the plant’s branches with your own eye, that means it has a self-subsistent origin that supplied all these branches with existence, however distant that origin may be and even if you do not remember it or come upon it. Every rational person realizes that the chain of causes that acquire the power of causality from the cause before it is like the chain of zeros, the chain of plant branches, and the proofs mentioned. Therefore, no rational person can claim that the existence of the entire universe rests only on a chain generated from each other without there being before it a self-subsistent effecter outside its reality, necessarily existent, unless he can claim that the value of a million is only composed of zeros exchanging value among themselves without being based on a preceding self-subsistent digit, or that the roses abundant in gardens and houses originate only from branches taken from each other without going back to a seed that supplied them with the origin of existence.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents three analogies to demonstrate the impossibility of an infinite regress of causes and to prove the necessity of a First Cause (God). Each analogy illustrates the same logical principle: a chain of dependent items cannot exist without a self-subsistent foundation. The first analogy concerns a chain of proofs. If every proof depends on another proof ad infinitum, no truth is ever established. The only way to have certainty is to reach a self-evident truth (بداهة) that requires no further proof. Without such a foundation, the entire chain is merely shadows waiting for a non-existent origin, so the claimed truth cannot exist. The second analogy uses zeros in a number. Zeros on their own have no value; they derive value from a non-zero digit to their left. If the chain of zeros never ends with a digit, the number has no value. Infinite succession does not create value. The third analogy describes a plant branch traced back through cuttings. If each cutting comes from another cutting without end, there is no original plant that generated all the branches. Yet we see the branches exist, so there must be an original root that supplied existence. The conclusion states that every rational person sees the similarity between these examples and the chain of causes in the universe. Causes that acquire their causal power from prior causes cannot go on infinitely. There must be a self-subsistent effecter (مؤثر ذاتي) outside the chain, who is necessarily existent (واجب الوجود). Denying this would be like claiming a million arises from zeros without a digit, or that flowers come only from cuttings without an original seed. The passage uses familiar, concrete examples to make the abstract argument about the necessity of a First Cause accessible.

Key Terms
تسلسل
علة
مؤثر ذاتي
واجب الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite chain of cuttings can ultimately produce the original plant.
Correction: No, because each cutting is dependent; without a self-subsistent origin, the entire chain cannot exist.

Checkpoint
According to the third analogy, what does the existence of plant branches necessarily indicate?
A) The branches are self-sufficient.
B) There is an original root that supplied existence.
C) The chain of cuttings is infinite.
D) The origin is unknown and irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The existence of dependent things in the universe necessitates a self-subsistent First Cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that a chain of zeros cannot make a million without a digit. In what areas of your life are you living like a 'zero,' trying to derive value from other zeros? Will you acknowledge today that your worth comes only from the Self-Subsistent, not from the created causes around you?
?
If you truly believe that every good thing in your life ultimately traces back to a single, self-subsistent Origin, why do you still worry as if your provision depends on a chain of uncertain means? What would change if you faced each need with the assurance that the First Cause has supplied it?
?
Consider the plant analogy: without the root, no branch exists. Do you live as if you are a branch disconnected from your Root—acting independently, forgetting that your very next breath depends on Him? What will you do today to consciously reattach your heart to the Origin of your existence?

The Atheist's Deceptive Escape into Infinite Regress
Buti exposes the atheist's infinite regress as a deceptive evasion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the atheist's appeal to infinite regress is a deceptive evasion, not a genuine causal explanation.

Core Idea
Infinite regress is a flight from the question, not an answer.

In this lesson, Buti describes the typical atheist response when pressed for a first cause. Instead of providing a real cause, the atheist points to an endless chain of prior causes. Buti warns that this is a deception—both of the questioner and of oneself. The atheist is unable to produce a cause and masks his inability with an imaginary infinite past.

Guided Path
1
Read the dialogue carefully
Read the Arabic passage describing the conversation with the atheist. Notice how the atheist answers each question with another prior cause, never stopping.
Pay attention to the repetition in the atheist's answers.
2
Identify the evasion
Buti explicitly states that the atheist is deceiving you and himself. Find the phrases where Buti exposes this deception.
Look for words like 'yakhda'uka' (deceives you) and 'yughalituka' (deludes you).
3
Understand why it is not a real answer
Buti argues that an infinite series of causes does not provide a cause for the first existent. Each link in the chain is itself an effect in need of a cause. The chain simply postpones the question.
The phrase 'laysa min dhalika al-illah' indicates that none of the chain is a true cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا قلت للملحد : ما هي علة وجود هذا الموجود الذي يحتاج إلى علّة موجدة ، فأجاب بأنها وجود موجود آخر يتقدمه ... ثم قلت له : وماذا علة وجود ذلك الموجود المتقدم فأجاب بأنها وجود موجود ثالث أقدم في الوجود ، ومثل الثاني في الحاجة إلى العلة الموجدة ، ولم يقطع سلسلة الجواب على هذا المنوال مهما أطلت وتوغلت في السؤال - فاعلم أن هذا الخصم يخدعك ويغالطك ويعللك في أجوبته بما ليس من الجواب في شيء ، كما يخدع نفسه قبلك ويغالطها ويعللها . أعني أنه يعجز عن أن يريك علة لوجود ذلك الموجود الذي سألته أولاً وجوده ، فيفر من الجواب على سؤالك غير شاعر أنه يفر . ثم يحاول أن يستر فراره من الجواب بإحالة الأمر على ظلمات ماض لا بداية له . والذي يخيله إليك أنه علة قبل علة ثم يستمر في هذا التخيل حتى تحصل من ذلك سلسلة العلل لا بداية لها ، فليس شيء من ذلك العلة إذ لا أصل لها ولا وجود . وبعد هذا كله فإن فرض التسلسل منقوض بالحس والمشاهدة نفسها ذلك أننا جميعاً نعلم بأن هناك مخلوقات نوعية انقرضت وانتهت فلو صح أن الموجودات تتسلسل إلى ما لا نهاية بأن يكون كل حلقة فيها معلولاً لما قبلها وعلة لما بعدها لما انقرضت هذه الموجودات . إذ كيف تنقرض وهي علة لما بعدها ؟ فلما دلّ الحس ودلّت المشاهدة على انقراضها وعدم استمرارها في التوالد علمنا أن الحلقة الأخيرة فيها معلولة فقط وليست بعلة كسابقتها ، وهذا إخلال بنظام التسلسل المزعوم وطبيعته ، ودليل على أن ثمة مؤثراً خارجياً زيادة على نظام التسلسل الرتيب
If you say to the atheist: 'What is the cause of the existence of this existent that needs an efficient cause?' and he answers that it is the existence of another preceding existent... then you say: 'And what is the cause of the existence of that preceding existent?' and he answers that it is the existence of a third existent even more ancient, and the second is like the first in need of the efficient cause, and he does not stop this chain of answers no matter how long you prolong and delve into questioning – then know that this opponent is deceiving you and deluding you and giving you answers that are not answers at all, just as he deceives his own soul before you and deludes it. I mean, he is unable to show you a cause for the existence of that existent you first asked about, so he flees from answering your question without realizing he is fleeing. Then he tries to conceal his escape from the answer by referring the matter to darknesses of the past without beginning. What he makes you imagine is a cause before a cause, then he continues in this imagination until you obtain from that a chain of causes without beginning. None of that is a cause, because it has no origin and no existence. After all this, the supposition of infinite regress (tasalsul) is refuted by sense and observation themselves. That is, we all know that there are species of creatures that have become extinct and ended. If it were true that existents regress infinitely such that every link is an effect of what precedes it and a cause of what follows it, then these existents would not become extinct. For how could they become extinct when they are a cause of what comes after them? Since sense and observation indicate their extinction and their lack of continuity in generation, we know that the last link among them is only an effect (ma'lulah) and not a cause like its predecessor. This is a violation of the alleged system of regress (tasalsul) and its nature, and evidence that there is an external influence beyond the monotonous system of regress.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage refutes the notion of infinite regress (tasalsul) in the chain of causes. The author begins by describing a dialogue with an atheist. When asked for the cause of an existent, the atheist repeatedly points to a previous existent, never terminating the chain. The author warns that this is a deception: the atheist is unable to provide a real cause and instead escapes into an imaginary infinite past. He then provides a decisive refutation based on empirical observation: we observe that species become extinct. If the chain were truly infinite with each link being both effect and cause, extinction would be impossible because the last link would be a cause for subsequent existents. Since extinction occurs, we know that the last link is only an effect, not a cause. This breaks the supposed infinite regress and indicates an external influence beyond the chain. The argument is presented in a logical, step-by-step manner, first exposing the evasion, then delivering the empirical refutation.

Key Terms
التسلسل
علة
معلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Infinite regress is a valid explanation for why things exist.
Correction: Buti shows that an infinite chain does not provide a real cause, because each link is itself in need of a cause. The chain simply postpones the question indefinitely.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why is the atheist's response of infinite regress not a real answer?
A) Because the chain is too long to be known
B) Because the chain does not provide a cause for the first existent
C) Because the atheist is lying about the past
D) Because the chain has no beginning

Key Takeaway
Infinite regress is not a causal explanation but an illusory escape from the real question.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face the ultimate question of why there is something rather than nothing, do you ever distract yourself with endless secondary causes to avoid the reality of the First Cause? How will you stop fleeing today?
?
In your own faith, are there areas where you rely on an infinite chain of justifications (like 'my parents believed' or 'scholars say') without ever grounding them in the foundational truth of God's existence? What step will you take to anchor your belief in the First Cause itself?
?
If the atheist's argument is rooted in self-deception, what self-deceptions about your need for God might you still be harboring? Will you honestly confront them today and ask God to reveal the truth to you?

Empirical Evidence Against Infinite Regress: Extinction
Buti refutes infinite regress using the empirical fact of species extinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the observable extinction of species disproves the possibility of an infinite causal regress.

Core Idea
Extinction proves that the last link is an effect, not a cause.

Having exposed the evasion, Buti now delivers a decisive refutation. He appeals to sense and observation: we witness species becoming extinct. If the causal chain were truly infinite with each link causing the next, no link could ever go extinct because it would be necessary for subsequent links. The fact of extinction shows the chain is finite and requires an external cause.

Guided Path
1
State the empirical fact
Read the passage and note that Buti begins with an observable fact: we know that species have become extinct and ended.
The Arabic uses 'na'lamu' (we know) to emphasize certainty.
2
Derive the contradiction
Buti argues that if infinite regress were true, extinction would be impossible. Understand his reasoning: each link is both effect and cause, so the last link would have to cause future existents, preventing its own extinction.
Focus on the conditional: 'law sahha...' (if it were true...).
3
Draw the conclusion
Since extinction is observed, infinite regress is false. Therefore, the last link is only an effect, not a cause. This implies an external influence beyond the chain.
The phrase 'thamma mu'aththiran kharijiyyan' means there is an external cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا قلت للملحد : ما هي علة وجود هذا الموجود الذي يحتاج إلى علّة موجدة ، فأجاب بأنها وجود موجود آخر يتقدمه ... ثم قلت له : وماذا علة وجود ذلك الموجود المتقدم فأجاب بأنها وجود موجود ثالث أقدم في الوجود ، ومثل الثاني في الحاجة إلى العلة الموجدة ، ولم يقطع سلسلة الجواب على هذا المنوال مهما أطلت وتوغلت في السؤال - فاعلم أن هذا الخصم يخدعك ويغالطك ويعللك في أجوبته بما ليس من الجواب في شيء ، كما يخدع نفسه قبلك ويغالطها ويعللها . أعني أنه يعجز عن أن يريك علة لوجود ذلك الموجود الذي سألته أولاً وجوده ، فيفر من الجواب على سؤالك غير شاعر أنه يفر . ثم يحاول أن يستر فراره من الجواب بإحالة الأمر على ظلمات ماض لا بداية له . والذي يخيله إليك أنه علة قبل علة ثم يستمر في هذا التخيل حتى تحصل من ذلك سلسلة العلل لا بداية لها ، فليس شيء من ذلك العلة إذ لا أصل لها ولا وجود . وبعد هذا كله فإن فرض التسلسل منقوض بالحس والمشاهدة نفسها ذلك أننا جميعاً نعلم بأن هناك مخلوقات نوعية انقرضت وانتهت فلو صح أن الموجودات تتسلسل إلى ما لا نهاية بأن يكون كل حلقة فيها معلولاً لما قبلها وعلة لما بعدها لما انقرضت هذه الموجودات . إذ كيف تنقرض وهي علة لما بعدها ؟ فلما دلّ الحس ودلّت المشاهدة على انقراضها وعدم استمرارها في التوالد علمنا أن الحلقة الأخيرة فيها معلولة فقط وليست بعلة كسابقتها ، وهذا إخلال بنظام التسلسل المزعوم وطبيعته ، ودليل على أن ثمة مؤثراً خارجياً زيادة على نظام التسلسل الرتيب
If you say to the atheist: 'What is the cause of the existence of this existent that needs an efficient cause?' and he answers that it is the existence of another preceding existent... then you say: 'And what is the cause of the existence of that preceding existent?' and he answers that it is the existence of a third existent even more ancient, and the second is like the first in need of the efficient cause, and he does not stop this chain of answers no matter how long you prolong and delve into questioning – then know that this opponent is deceiving you and deluding you and giving you answers that are not answers at all, just as he deceives his own soul before you and deludes it. I mean, he is unable to show you a cause for the existence of that existent you first asked about, so he flees from answering your question without realizing he is fleeing. Then he tries to conceal his escape from the answer by referring the matter to darknesses of the past without beginning. What he makes you imagine is a cause before a cause, then he continues in this imagination until you obtain from that a chain of causes without beginning. None of that is a cause, because it has no origin and no existence. After all this, the supposition of infinite regress (tasalsul) is refuted by sense and observation themselves. That is, we all know that there are species of creatures that have become extinct and ended. If it were true that existents regress infinitely such that every link is an effect of what precedes it and a cause of what follows it, then these existents would not become extinct. For how could they become extinct when they are a cause of what comes after them? Since sense and observation indicate their extinction and their lack of continuity in generation, we know that the last link among them is only an effect (ma'lulah) and not a cause like its predecessor. This is a violation of the alleged system of regress (tasalsul) and its nature, and evidence that there is an external influence beyond the monotonous system of regress.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage refutes the notion of infinite regress (tasalsul) in the chain of causes. The author begins by describing a dialogue with an atheist. When asked for the cause of an existent, the atheist repeatedly points to a previous existent, never terminating the chain. The author warns that this is a deception: the atheist is unable to provide a real cause and instead escapes into an imaginary infinite past. He then provides a decisive refutation based on empirical observation: we observe that species become extinct. If the chain were truly infinite with each link being both effect and cause, extinction would be impossible because the last link would be a cause for subsequent existents. Since extinction occurs, we know that the last link is only an effect, not a cause. This breaks the supposed infinite regress and indicates an external influence beyond the chain. The argument is presented in a logical, step-by-step manner, first exposing the evasion, then delivering the empirical refutation.

Key Terms
الفرض
الحس والمشاهدة
انقراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The universe is expanding
B) Species become extinct
C) Matter cannot be created or destroyed
D) Humans have free will

Key Takeaway
The observable fact of extinction destroys the possibility of an infinite causal chain and points to a first cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Proof of the Invalidity of Circularity (Dawr)
Buti defines circular causation and proves its impossibility with an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what circular causation (dawr) is and why it is logically impossible.

Core Idea
Circular causation makes existence impossible.

Buti presents a concrete refutation of a materialistic evolutionary hypothesis by showing it leads to an absurd logical loop. He defines circular causation (dawr) and illustrates it with a memorable example. This lesson establishes why dawr is rationally impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the hypothetical objection
Notice how the skeptic accepts an originated world but posits a natural process. This sets up the refutation.
2
Identify Buti's diagnosis of circularity
He shows the hypothesis leads to dawr. Understand the definition: A depends on B, B depends on A.
3
Study the college example
The example clarifies why dawr is impossible. Reflect on the conclusion: both goals cannot be achieved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً - برهان بطلان الدور : ثم إننا نفرض أن المتشكك فكر ملياً ثم قال : فأنا أرجع إلى أن العالم حادث كما قلت أولاً ، وله علة أثرت في إيجاده ، ولكن لا تتمثل هذه العلة في أكثر من التفاعل الذاتي المتدرج . فلم يكن الوجود أول نشأته أكثر من هواء يملأ الفراغ ، ثم وجد السديم وتعقدت منه أبخرة وغازات معينة ثم تكاملت من ذلك العناصر الأولية للحياة كالكربون والأيدروجين والأكسجين ، فتلاقت من ذلك مركبات عضوية لا حصر حصر لها . ومرَّت على ذلك ملايين السنوات وهي تتفاعل خلال ذلك متنقلة من طور إلى طور بعامل الزمن والاستمرار ، إلى أن تكاملت أخيراً عناصر الموجودات الحية وغيرها ، فالعالم حادث، ولكن الذي سبب حدوثه ووجوده هو هذا التفاعل الذي بدأ بأبسط الموجودات ثم ترقى صعداً إلى أعقدها وأعلاها فالجواب أن هذا الفرض يستلزم القول بالدور ، والدور فرضية باطلة لا تتحقق باتفاق العقلاء. ومعنى الدور الباطل أن يتوقف الشيء ، في وجوده المطلق أو تكييف معين له ، على شيء آخر . إلا أن هذا الشيء متوقف في ذلك الوجود أو التكييف وفي نفس الوقت على ذلك الشيء الأول . فمن المحال إذا أن يوجد أو يتكيف هذا الشيء أو ذاك . ولا يمكن أن تجد عاقلاً يقول : بل إنها تعاونا فأوجد كل منهما الآخر. مثال ذلك ما لو فرضنا أنك حاولت الانتساب إلى كلية التربية ، فقيل لك إن ذلك متوقف على أن تكون موظفاً في سلك التدريس الرسمي ، ولما حاولت أن تدخل في سلك التدريس قيل لك إن ذلك متوقف على أن تكون متخرجاً من كلية التربية . إن من البدهي أنك لن تستطيع أن تحقق لنفسك أي الغرضين ما دام الأمر كذلك
Third: The Proof of the Invalidity of Circularity (Dawr). Then we suppose that the skeptic thought deeply and said: 'I concede that the world is originated (hadith) as you said first, and it has a cause that brought it into existence, but this cause is nothing more than gradual self-interaction. At its beginning, existence was nothing but air filling the void, then nebula formed and from it certain vapors and gases developed, then from that the primary elements of life like carbon, hydrogen, and oxygen evolved, then from that countless organic compounds came together. Millions of years passed while they interacted, moving from stage to stage by the factor of time and continuity, until finally the elements of living and non-living existents evolved. So the world is originated, but what caused its occurrence and existence is this interaction which began with the simplest existents and then gradually ascended to the most complex and highest.' The answer is that this hypothesis necessitates the claim of circularity (dawr), and circularity is a false hypothesis that cannot be realized by the consensus of rational people. The meaning of false circularity is that a thing depends, in its absolute existence or a specific qualification, on another thing, yet that other thing also depends, in that same existence or qualification, at the same time on the first thing. Therefore, it is impossible for either thing to exist or be qualified. You cannot find a rational person who says, 'Rather, they cooperate and each brings the other into existence.' An example of that is if you tried to enroll in a college of education, and you were told that this depends on your being a teacher in the official teaching service. Then when you tried to enter the teaching service, you were told that this depends on your being a graduate of the college of education. It is obvious that you will not be able to achieve either goal as long as things are like that.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of the invalidity of circular causation (dawr). It begins by constructing a hypothetical objection from a skeptic who accepts that the world is originated but posits a naturalistic evolutionary process as the cause. The author then diagnoses that this hypothesis entails circularity. He defines dawr: when thing A depends on thing B, and B in turn depends on A for the same existence or qualification. This makes both impossible, because each requires the other first. He dismisses any notion of reciprocal cooperation as irrational. The example of college enrollment and teaching service illustrates the absurdity: you cannot enroll without being a teacher, and you cannot be a teacher without being a graduate. Thus circular dependence prevents any realization. The argument is clear and pedagogical, using a concrete analogy.

Key Terms
الدور
التفاعل الذاتي
الفرضية
التوقف
الاستحالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think circular causality is possible if both causes act simultaneously.
Correction: Buti states that no rational person says they cooperate; circular dependence makes existence impossible regardless of simultaneity.

Checkpoint
What does Buti mean by dawr (circularity)?
A) A chain of causes without end
B) Two things each depending on the other for their existence
C) A single cause for all effects
D) The gradual evolution of species

Key Takeaway
Circular causation (dawr) is logically impossible because it demands each thing to precede itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, have you ever found yourself in a cycle where you waited for a spiritual condition before performing an act of worship, yet that condition itself depended on the same act? How does the example of enrollment in college and teaching service expose the absurdity of that cycle, and what concrete step can you take today to break it by relying solely on Allah as the ultimate cause?
?
This lesson proves that circular causation is impossible. Consider your understanding of the universe: do you ever subconsciously assume that the cosmos is self-caused or that cause and effect can loop infinitely? How does the logical impossibility of dawr challenge that assumption, and what does that mean for your conviction in Allah as the First Cause?
?
The skeptic's hypothesis claimed that the world evolved through gradual interaction. Yet Buti shows it leads to circularity. Do you have any lingering doubts about the universe's origin that parallel this flawed reasoning? What would it take for you to fully accept that only an uncaused cause can break the chain, and how will you act on that belief today?

Summary of Three Refutations: The World Needs a Creator
Author enumerates three refuted positions and draws the necessary conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes three alternatives about the world's origin (sudden creation, pre-eternity, self-causation) and concludes that it must have a necessary Creator, which is Allah.

Core Idea
Three rational dead ends all lead to one necessary conclusion: the world needs a Creator.

The author has already argued that the world is originated. Here he summarizes three alternative positions that one might think could explain the world's existence: sudden creation without cause, the world being eternal, or the world being its own cause. He shows each leads to a self-evident absurdity. This leaves only one possibility: the world was created by an independent, necessary Being—Allah. This lesson will walk you through each refutation and the final conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: it lists three refuted positions and then states the conclusion.
The passage uses the phrase 'وتبين أن' (and it has become clear that) for each refutation.
2
Identify the three refuted positions
Find each of the three claims that the author shows to be false: sudden origination without cause, the world being eternal (qadīm), and self-causation.
Each leads to a self-evident absurdity: preponderance without preponderant, infinite chain, circularity.
3
Understand the logical error of each
For each refuted position, trace why it leads to an impossibility. The author calls these impossibilities 'self-evident' (badīhī) or 'necessary' (ḍarūrī).
The three absurdities are: tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ, tasalsul, and dawr.
4
Grasp the conclusion
After eliminating the three alternatives, the author concludes that the world must have an independent creator. Note that this creator does not need a creator Himself—He is the Necessary Being.
This conclusion is the core of the argument for God's existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والآن : تبين لك أن القول بحدوث العالم طفرة بدون أي علة تؤثر فيه . لأنه يستلزم فرضية بدهية البطلان وهي : الرجحان بدون مرجح وتبين أن القول بكونه قديماً باطل لأنه يستلزم تسلسل الممكنات إلى ما لا نهاية ، والتسلسل باطل بالبداهة أيضاً وتبين أن القول بكون العالم علة نفسه والمؤثر في إيجاده ، يستلزم القول بالدور ، وهو أيضاً من الأمور الباطلة بالضرورة . فما الذي بقي ؟ بقي أن العالم لا بد له من موجد مستقل عنه أوجده ، وهذا الموجَد لا يحتاج بدوره إلى موجد له ، وهو ما نسميه بالذات الواجبة الوجود وهو الله سبحانه وتعالى .
And now: it has become clear to you that the statement of the world's origination (ḥudūth) as a sudden leap without any cause effecting it is false, because it entails a self-evidently false hypothesis: preponderance without a preponderant. And it has become clear that the statement of its being eternal (qadīm) is false because it entails an infinite chain of possibles, and an infinite chain (tasalsul) is also false by self-evidence. And it has become clear that the statement that the world is its own cause and the effecter in its bringing into existence entails the statement of circularity (al-dawr), which is also among things false by necessity. So what remains? It remains that the world must have an independent extender (mūjid) that brought it into existence, and this extended does not in turn need a extender for itself, and that is what we call the Necessary Being (al-dhāt al-wājib al-wujūd), and He is Allah, exalted and high.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a concluding summary that collects three refuted positions and draws the necessary conclusion. The author presents three claims about the world and shows each leads to an impossibility: (1) that the world came into existence suddenly without any cause leads to the self-evident absurdity of 'preference without a preponderant' (tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ); (2) that the world is eternal (qadīm) leads to an infinite chain of possibles (tasalsul), which is also self-evidently false; (3) that the world is its own cause leads to circularity (al-dawr), which is necessarily false. Having eliminated all three, he concludes that the world must have an independent creator (mūjid) who does not depend on another, i.e., the Necessary Being (al-dhāt al-wājib al-wujūd), who is Allah. The structure is a classic disjunctive argument: the world is either created (by a cause), or eternal, or self-caused—all but one are refuted, establishing the existence of God.

Key Terms
حدوث (origination)
قديم (eternal)
تسلسل (infinite chain)
دور (circularity)
مرجح (preponderant)
ذات واجبة الوجود (Necessary Being)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
After refuting sudden creation without cause, pre-eternity, and self-causation, the only remaining rational conclusion is that the world was created by an independent, necessary Being—Allah.

The Trilemma Proof for the Existence of God
Buti presents a trilemma and proves the necessity of an independent creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti uses a trilemma to prove the necessity of an independent creator by eliminating three impossible explanations for the existence of the world.

Core Idea
Only an independent, self-sufficient Creator can explain the world's existence.

Buti presents a powerful logical argument for God's existence. He shows that the world must have an origin, and then eliminates every possible explanation except one: a creator who does not need a creator. This trilemma is a concise yet rigorous proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Buti refutes three positions one by one before concluding.
The passage is a single logical argument. Read it as a whole.
2
Identify the three refuted positions
Find the three statements that Buti calls false. List them in order: spontaneous generation, eternal existence, self-causation.
Each is introduced with 'تبين أن القول...'
3
Understand the logical flaws
For each refuted position, identify the logical problem: preponderance without a preponderant, infinite regress, and circular reasoning.
These are all considered self-evidently false (بدهية البطلان).
4
See the conclusion
After eliminating three impossibilities, only one possibility remains: the world has an independent creator who is the Necessary Being (واجب الوجود).
This creator does not need a creator Himself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والآن : تبين لك أن القول بحدوث العالم طفرة بدون أي علة تؤثر فيه . لأنه يستلزم فرضية بدهية البطلان وهي : الرجحان بدون مرجح وتبين أن القول بكونه قديماً باطل لأنه يستلزم تسلسل الممكنات إلى ما لا نهاية ، والتسلسل باطل بالبداهة أيضاً وتبين أن القول بكون العالم علة نفسه والمؤثر في إيجاده ، يستلزم القـول بالدور ، وهو أيضاً من الأمور الباطلة بالضرورة . فما الذي بقي ؟ بقي أن العالم لا بد له من موجد مستقل عنه أوجده ، وهذا الموجد لا يحتاج بدوره إلى موجد له ، وهو ما نسميه بالذات الواجبة الوجود وهو الله سبحانه وتعالى . وقد ظهر وجود الله عز وجل ، بالدليل اليقيني القائم على برهان التلازم المرتكز على الاستقراء التام .
And now: it has become clear to you that the statement that the world originated by a leap without any cause affecting it is false, because it necessitates a self-evidently false assumption: preponderance without a preponderant. And it has become clear that the statement that it is eternal is false, because it necessitates the regress of possibles to infinity, and regress is also self-evidently false. And it has become clear that the statement that the world is its own cause and the agent in its own bringing into existence necessitates circular reasoning, which is also among necessarily false matters. So what remains? Remains that the world must have an independent originator who brought it into existence, and this originator does not in turn need an originator for himself, and He is what we call the Self-Subsistent Necessary Being, and He is Allah, glorified and exalted. And the existence of Allah, mighty and majestic, has appeared by the certain proof based on the proof of concomitance relying on complete induction.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a proof by elimination (trilemma) for God's existence. Buti lists three invalid positions: (1) the world came into existence by chance without a cause – this is impossible because it would require a preponderance (preferring existence over non-existence) without any preponderant factor, which is rationally absurd. (2) The world is eternal – this is impossible because it would require an infinite regress of contingent beings (possible existents), and an infinite regress is self-evidently impossible. (3) The world is its own cause – this is impossible because it leads to circular reasoning (the world causing itself before it exists). After refuting these three, the only remaining possibility is that the world has an independent creator who does not need a creator Himself, i.e., the Necessary Being (واجب الوجود), who is Allah. Buti then states that this is a certain proof based on the proof of concomitance (برهان التلازم) built on complete induction (الاستقراء التام).

Key Terms
الرجحان بدون مرجح
تسلسل الممكنات
الدور
واجب الوجود
برهان التلازم
الاستقراء التام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The trilemma is a false dichotomy or incomplete enumeration.
Correction: Buti's trilemma exhausts all logical possibilities for the origin of the world: spontaneous generation, eternal existence, self-causation, or external causation. After eliminating three, only external causation remains.

Checkpoint
What logical problem does Buti identify with the claim that the world is its own cause?
A) It leads to an infinite regress.
B) It leads to circular reasoning (دور).
C) It requires a preponderant.
D) It contradicts complete induction.

Key Takeaway
Buti's trilemma proves that the world must have an independent, self-sufficient creator, who is Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly internalized that without a Creator the universe is impossible, would your daily actions reflect that certainty? What is one habit that shows you still live as if the world is self-sufficient?
?
You have just seen that every possible explanation for existence apart from Allah collapses into absurdity. Does your heart now feel the weight of His necessity? Will you thank Him today for being the only One who truly exists on His own?
?
Buti’s proof eliminates every excuse to ignore the Creator. If you have been putting off a sincere turn to Allah, what has held you back? Will you let this logical certainty move you to action right now?
