The First Rational Proof: God Cannot Be Composed of Parts
Buti presents the first rational proof against God being a composite whole.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that God cannot be a whole composed of parts, because that would imply dependence and resemblance to contingent things.

Core Idea
If God were made of parts, He would need them — and need is imperfection.

Buti begins his rational proofs for God's oneness by addressing the possibility that God could be a composite whole. This would imply need and resemblance to creation, which is impossible for the Creator. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the conditional structure: 'if... then...'.
Notice the logical flow: supposition leads to implications.
2
Identify the consequences
The passage lists two consequences of God being composed of parts. Identify them and reflect on why each is impossible for God.
3
Connect to oneness
Ask: How does this proof establish that God is one? Understand that composite implies need, which contradicts divinity.
This is a form of reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الدليل العقلي على نفيهما ، أي أنه سبحانه ليس كلاً قابلاً للتجزء ولاكلياً يندرج فيه أفراد وأعداد ، فهو ما يلي : أولاً - لو صح أنه سبحانه وتعالى كلّ مركب من أجزاء ، لاستلزم ذلك أن يكون عاجزاً بنفسه محتاجاً إلى غيره ، وللزم من ذلك أن يكون مشابهاً للحوادث ، وذلك باطل في حق الله كما قد علمت ثانياً ـ لو صح أنه سبحانه وتعالى كلي مكون من أفراد ، لأمكن أن يقوم بينهم تمانع في الإرادة والخلق ؛ وذلك بأن يريد واحد منهم إيجاد شيء ويريد الآخر إعدامه . وحينئذ إما أن يحصل الأمران فيجتمع النقيضان وهو محال ، أو يحصل أحدهما فيظهر عجز الآخر وهو مناف للألوهية ، أو يتصادمـا فلا هذا ولا ذاك فيظهر عجزهما معاً ؛ ومادام وقوع هذا التمانع ممكناً فإن صفة الكمال لهما تصبح غير ضرورية . وقد ذكر الله هذا البرهان بأسلوب مبسط في قوله : لَوْ كَانَ فِيهما آلِهَةٌ إلا اللهُ لَفَسَدَتا ... ﴾ [ الأنبياء : ٢٢ ] .
As for the rational proof of negating both, i.e., that He, exalted, is not a whole divisible into parts nor a universal comprising individuals and numbers, it is as follows: First - if it were true that He, exalted, is a whole composed of parts, then it would necessitate that He is helpless by Himself, in need of others, and that would necessitate that He resembles contingent things, and that is false regarding God as you have known. Second - if it were true that He, exalted, is a universal composed of individuals, then it would be possible for conflict to arise between them in will and creation; that is, one of them wills to bring something into existence and another wills to annihilate it. Then either both occur and the two opposites would combine, which is impossible, or one occurs and the incapacity of the other becomes apparent, which contradicts divinity, or they clash and neither occurs, so the incapacity of both becomes apparent; and as long as the occurrence of such conflict is possible, the attribute of perfection for them becomes non-necessary. And God has mentioned this proof in a simplified manner in His saying: 'If there were gods besides Allah, both would have been corrupted' [Al-Anbiyaa: 22].
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents two rational proofs (adilla 'aqliyya) for God's oneness. The first proof argues that if God were a whole composed of parts (kull murakkab min ajza'), He would be dependent on those parts and would resemble contingent things (hawadith), which is impossible for God. The second proof argues that if God were a universal comprising multiple individuals (kulli mukawwan min afrad), conflict (tamani') could arise between these individuals in will and creation. Such conflict leads to one of three impossible outcomes: (1) both wills occurring simultaneously, combining opposites; (2) one will prevailing, showing the other's incapacity; or (3) neither occurring, showing both's incapacity. Since God must be perfect, multiple gods are impossible. The author cites the Qur'anic verse (21:22) as a simplified expression of this argument.

Key Terms
الكل
المركب
الأجزاء
العاجز
الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God could be composed of parts but still be perfect.
Correction: Having parts implies dependence on those parts, which contradicts God's self-sufficiency and absolute perfection.

Checkpoint
According to the first rational proof, if God were composed of parts, what would be a necessary consequence?
A) He would be independent
B) He would resemble contingent things
C) He would be all-powerful
D) He would be simple

Key Takeaway
God cannot be composed of parts because that would imply need and contingency, contradicting His perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's independence means He has no need of any part, what does your constant craving for others' approval reveal about your understanding of God's sufficiency? Will you today rely on God alone for your worth?
?
The proof shows that true perfection excludes any need. Are you willing to let go of one thing you feel you 'need' to be happy, in order to trust in God's perfect independence? Name it and commit to releasing it.
?
If resembling contingent things is false for God, why do you still try to make God fit your own limited expectations? How can you humbly accept that God is beyond any image or concept you have?

The Second Rational Proof: Multiple Gods Lead to Conflict
Buti presents the second rational proof against multiple gods using the impossibility of conflict.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that if there were multiple gods, conflict in will would necessarily arise, leading to impossibility or imperfection.

Core Idea
Multiple gods cannot coexist because their wills would clash.

Buti's second proof tackles the possibility of multiple gods. If God were a universal comprising many individuals, conflict would be possible. Such conflict leads to contradiction or weakness, both incompatible with divinity. This lesson explores the three impossible outcomes and the Quranic confirmation.

Guided Path
1
Read the scenario
Read the passage that sets up the hypothesis: if God were a universal with individuals, conflict in will is possible.
The key term is 'tamani'' (mutual conflict).
2
Analyze the three outcomes
The passage lists three possibilities when conflicting wills occur. Examine each one and why it is impossible or contradictory to divinity.
These are: both happen (contradiction), one prevails (weakness), neither happens (both weak).
3
See the Quranic support
Note that Buti cites verse 21:22 to show the same proof in revelation. Reflect on how the rational argument aligns with Scripture.

Source Text

And God has mentioned this proof in a simplified manner in His saying: 'If there were gods besides Allah, both would have been corrupted' [Al-Anbiyaa: 22].

The Necessity of Human Purpose After Proving God
Buti argues that reason cannot accept a purposeless existence after affirming a wise Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in a wise Creator logically requires human purpose and accountability, and why purposelessness is an absurd contradiction.

Core Idea
If God is Wise, existence cannot be meaningless.

This lesson follows Buti's proofs for God's existence and attributes. After establishing that the Creator is Wise and that absurdity is impossible for Him, Buti now poses a series of rhetorical questions. These questions force the reader to confront the logical outcome: human life must have a purpose; otherwise, the entire creation would be an absurdity inconsistent with God's wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a sense of the rhetorical flow and the questions Buti raises.
Notice the repetition of 'هل' (interrogative) which builds the argument.
2
Identify the key premises
Buti reminds us that we have concluded that God exists as a Wise Manager, and that absurdity cannot be attributed to Him. These premises are the foundation of the argument.
The attribute of wisdom (ḥikma) and negation of absurdity (ʿabath) are crucial.
3
Examine the rhetorical questions
List the scenarios Buti presents as unacceptable: living like animals, the intellect being a meaningless accident, the universe ending in nothing. For each scenario, ask why it would contradict God's wisdom.
The questions are not merely rhetorical; they are logical reductions to absurdity.
4
Understand the conclusion
Recognize that the ultimate absurdity is a perfectly coordinated universe subjugated to man ending in nothing. The impossibility of this absurdity logically entails that human existence must have a purpose and accountability.
The conclusion is implicit: if absurdity is impossible, then purpose is necessary.
5
Reflect on personal significance
Consider how this reasoning grounds moral responsibility and the need for religion in one's life. If life has purpose, then we must seek it.
This connects theology to daily life and ethics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الآن، وقد انتهينا من البحث في وجود الله عز وجل، ورأينا كيف أن العقل لا يتردد في الإيمان بوجود مدبّر للكون مالك لأمره، وعلمنا الخصائص والصفات التي يتصف بها هذا الخالق العظيم - هل يسعنا أن نتساءل عن وظيفتنا في هذا الوجود؟ وإذا تساءلنا عنها، فهل يسعنا أن نتصور أن ليس لنا أي وظيفة، ولا ترتبط بنا أية مسؤولية.. وهل يصدق العقل - بعد الذي انتهينا إليه من الإيمان بالله وبأنه مدبر وحكيم - أن لا شأن لنا في الدنيا إلا ما هو شأن الدواب والحيوانات الأخرى، نسرح ونمرح بين المأكل والمشرب والملبس والمنكح، حقبة قصيرة أو طويلة من الزمن حيث يلتقمنا بعد ذلك جوف الهلاك والموت؟! وهل كان ما يمتاز به الإنسان عن سائر المكونات الأخرى وهو العقل الذي يستجلي أغوار الكون بمظاهره المختلفة، مجرد ظاهرة صادف أن امتاز بها على غيره، ثم لا تعني شيئاً أكثر من ذلك؟ إن أي عاقل لا يمكن (بعد أن انتهى من مرحلة الإيمان بوجود الخالق) أن يتصور شيئاً من هذه الفرضيات، فضلاً عن أن يعتقدها ويتبناها. فقد علم هذا العاقل أن من أجلى صفات الله عز وجل أنه حكيم في خلقه وعامة أحكامه، وأنه لا يتصور في حقه العبث، وأي عبث أعبث من أن تكون هذه الأكوان المنسقة غاية التنسيق، ثم المسخرة للإنسان غاية التسخير بما أودع فيه من السر العجيب الذي لن تنتهي حيرة الإنسان منه - منتهية أخيراً إلى لا شيء، ومتصدعة إلى غير غاية!
Now, having concluded our research into the existence of Allah Almighty, and having seen how the intellect does not hesitate to believe in the existence of a Manager of the universe, Possessor of its command, and having learned the characteristics and attributes with which this Great Creator is described — can we question our function in this existence? And if we question it, can we imagine that we have no function, nor any responsibility attached to us? And does the intellect — after we have arrived at belief in Allah and that He is a Manager and Wise — affirm that we have no concern in this world except that of beasts and other animals, roaming and frolicking among food, drink, clothing, and marriage, for a short or long period after which the belly of destruction and death swallows us?! And was that by which man is distinguished from all other creations — namely the intellect that unveils the depths of the universe in its various manifestations — merely a phenomenon that happened to distinguish him from others, then means nothing more than that? Indeed, no rational person can (after having completed the stage of belief in the existence of the Creator) imagine any of these hypotheses, let alone believe and adopt them. For this rational person has learned that one of the most evident attributes of Allah Almighty is that He is Wise in His creation and all His judgments, and that absurdity cannot be conceived in His regard. And what absurdity is more absurd than that these universes, coordinated to the utmost degree, then subjugated to man to the utmost subjugation, by means of the wondrous secret deposited in him which man's bewilderment will never end — finally ending up as nothing, and shattered for no purpose!
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a rhetorical argument that follows the proofs of God's existence. It aims to demonstrate that human existence must have a purpose and accountability, otherwise belief in a wise Creator would be contradicted. The author begins by recalling that we have concluded the investigation into God's existence, and the intellect readily affirms a Manager of the universe with attributes of wisdom and power. He then poses a series of rhetorical questions: can we ask about our function? Could we imagine having no function or responsibility? Would the intellect accept that we are merely like animals, eating, drinking, and procreating until death? He questions whether the intellect, which distinguishes humans and allows them to explore the universe's depths, is just a meaningless accident. The answer is that no rational person, after believing in a wise Creator, can even imagine such hypotheses, let alone believe them. The reason is that it is a clear attribute of God that He is Wise (ḥakīm) in all His creation and judgments, and absurdity (ʿabath) is inconceivable for Him. The ultimate absurdity would be to have this perfectly coordinated universe, subjugated to man with his wondrous intellect, end in nothingness and shatter without a goal. Thus, human purpose and a final accountability are necessary conclusions from the nature of God.

Key Terms
وظيفة
مسؤولية
عبث
حكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that acknowledging God does not automatically entail human purpose; perhaps God created for no reason or for purposes we cannot know.
Correction: The passage argues that God's attribute of wisdom (ḥikma) logically excludes any absurdity (ʿabath) in creation. A creation without purpose would be absurd, contradicting God's wisdom. Therefore, human existence must have a purpose and accountability.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it impossible for a rational person to believe that human existence is purposeless after affirming God's existence?
A) Because the intellect has proven that humans are superior to animals.
B) Because God's attribute of wisdom (ḥikma) excludes any absurdity (ʿabath) in creation.
C) Because the universe is perfectly organized, so it must continue forever.
D) Because humans possess intellect, which must have a purpose beyond mere survival.

Key Takeaway
Because God is Wise, He cannot create without purpose; therefore, human existence must have meaning and accountability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe God is Wise and does not create in vain, then what specific change must you make today to align your daily actions with the purpose He has designed for you?
?
When you think about the times you live as if life were just about eating, drinking, and entertainment, are you not effectively denying God's wisdom? How will you respond to that contradiction starting tomorrow?
?
The intellect that distinguishes you is not meaningless. What is one way you have used your intellect this week that shows you believe your existence has accountability?

Creation Implies Accountability
Buti argues from creation's implication and cites Quran verses against purposelessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the existence of creation rationally implies a Creator and moral accountability, as reinforced by Quranic verses against purposelessness.

Core Idea
Creation demands accountability — you are not a cosmic accident.

This lesson presents a powerful argument from creation itself: if a force brought you and the universe into existence, shouldn't you be concerned about your relationship with it? Buti then reinforces this rational inference with Quranic verses that explicitly reject the notion of purposeless creation, affirming that human life has meaning and that we will be held accountable.

Guided Path
1
Read the rhetorical opening
Start with the rhetorical question: should you not be concerned about the force that created you? Let it sink in before analyzing.
Buti uses a direct, provocative style to engage the reader.
2
Note the cautionary footnote
In the source, Buti warns that calling Allah a 'force' is improper. Understand why such language is problematic.
This shows the author's precision in using proper theological language.
3
Examine the argument from universal responsibility
Observe the analogy: all creatures have assigned responsibilities; humans, being unique in reason, must also have responsibility.
4
Study the Quranic verses
Read the two verses from Al-Mu'minun and Al-Anbiya carefully. They directly state that creation is not in vain or for sport.
These verses are the scriptural foundation for the argument.
5
Connect to the core idea
Reflect on how the rational argument and the Quranic proofs together establish that life has purpose and accountability.
This is the takeaway: you are not here by accident.

Perception should (as far as every thinker's mind understands) place itself before a long path for new thinking. And it should walk this path with all seriousness, precision, and caution.
(1)
(A miraculous force created you and created this universe! Should it not disturb you regarding the command of this force and the extent of what authority it may have over you? Should you not think and research long until you are reassured that you are not responsible to it for anything? And how can you imagine that you are not responsible to it for anything, while you are the unique creature in whom the secret of thought and reason was deposited, whereas you see all your other fellow creatures that are below you in everything. Each of them has been assigned a specific responsibility, devoted to it, going on in its performance, not resting nor tiring!
It is) in order to clarify this grave truth and confirm it, that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, repeats in His address to us, drawing attention to the fact that He, Exalted, could not have created man in vain, so that he may amuse himself for days and then die; and He calls upon minds to pay attention to this evident truth: 'Did you think that We created you in play and that you would not be returned to Us? So exalted is Allah, the Sovereign, the Truth; there is no god except Him, Lord of the Noble Throne' [Al-Mu'minun: 115-116]. And 'We did not create the heaven and the earth and that between them in sport. Had We intended to take a diversion, We could have taken it from [what is] with Us – if We were to do so' [Al-Anbiya: 16-17].

(1) We placed this word in parentheses to indicate that it is a corrupt word that is not permissible to express the essence of Allah, the Exalted, because Allah, the Exalted, is not a miraculous force, but an essence characterized by miraculous power and all attributes of perfection, just as Allah, the Exalted, is not 'a shelter' nor 'peace' as some say... But we quoted these people's speech verbatim as a depiction of their reality, and a transmission of their speech indicating corruption in its style and content.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the implication of creation. It begins with a rhetorical question: should you not be concerned about the powerful force that created you and the universe? The author then adds a cautionary footnote explaining that the term 'miraculous force' is corrupt and improper for describing God; God is not a force but an essence with attributes of perfection. The main argument continues: if all other creatures have assigned responsibilities, how can you think you have no responsibility? To confirm this, the author cites two Quranic verses: Surah Al-Mu'minun 115-116, which rebukes those who think they were created for play and not accountable, and Surah Al-Anbiya 16-17, which states that God did not create the heavens and earth in sport. The verses together establish that creation has a serious purpose and that humans will be returned to God for judgment.

مسؤولية
خلق الإنسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people refer to Allah as a 'force' or 'power' in a pantheistic or impersonal sense, suggesting that God is merely an abstract energy rather than a personal, attribute-possessing Being.
Correction: The author explicitly warns that referring to Allah as a 'force' is corrupt and improper, because Allah is an essence characterized by miraculous power and all attributes of perfection, not a mere force.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the Quranic verses from Al-Mu'minun and Al-Anbiya primarily prove?
A) That human beings are the most powerful of creatures.
B) That God created the universe without any purpose.
C) That human creation is not in vain and that there is accountability.
D) That the heavens and earth were created for amusement.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verses establish that creation is not in vain and that humans will be held accountable before their Creator.

?

General Science's Affirmation of Miracles
Buti uses personified science to argue for miracle possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why general science—having proven God's existence—cannot deny the possibility of miracles without contradicting itself.

Core Idea
If God exists as the cause of all causes, miracles are not only possible but expected.

Buti now turns to what he calls 'general science'—not experimental science but the broader rational science that includes theology. Having already proven God's existence through decisive proofs, this science is now asked about miracles. Buti shows that if general science were to deny miracles, it would be contradicting its own conclusions about God being the Creator and cause of all things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Buti personifies 'science' and uses rhetorical questions to make his point.
The passage is a single paragraph with a dramatic tone.
2
Identify the two contradictions
The passage contains two 'how can you expect' questions. Find them and see what science would have to contradict in each case.
These contradictions highlight the logical inconsistency of denying miracles after affirming God.
3
Connect to the existence of God
Recall that Buti previously proved God's existence. Now see how this proof leads directly to the possibility of miracles.
4
Reflect on the necessity of miracles
Ask yourself: If God is the cause of causes, could He choose to break the patterns He created? Why or why not?
This is the heart of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندئذ تتحول عنه لتسأل العلم ) بمعناه الثاني الأعم ( عن رأيه في المعجزة وحكمه عليها . فيقول لك : تسألني عن إمكان المعجزة التي هي الأمر الخارق للعادة ، وقد سألتني قبل الآن عن وجود الله عز وجل فأجبتـك بـأنـه واجب الوجود وهو الذي لا شبهة ولا شك في ذاته ؟! .. أتراني ( وقد أوضحت لـك وجود الله عز وجل بقواطع الأدلة والبراهين الساطعة ، وبينت لك أنه هو الخالق للأشياء وأسبابها وانتظاماتها ( أناقض نفسي وأقول : إن المعجزة ( التي ليست أكثر من خرق للعادة ( قسم من المستحيل الذي لا يمكن وقوعه ! .. وكيف تنتظر من العلم أن يناقض ذاته ، فيثبت مرة أن الله هو المسبب للأسباب والرابط بينها وبين مسبباتها ثم ينفي ذلك أخرى ليقول : إنّ نظام الأسباب والمسببات واجب لا يمكن أن ينخرم ، كيف تنتظر من العلم أن يقول لك : إن نظام الكون من قبيل الممكن ثم يعود ليقول لك : لا إنه من قبيل الواجب ؟!
Then you turn from it and ask science—in its second, more general sense—about its opinion on miracles and its judgment on them. It will say to you: 'You ask me about the possibility of the miracle, which is the extraordinary matter breaking custom, and you asked me before about the existence of God Almighty, and I answered you that He is the Necessary Being, who has no doubt or uncertainty in His essence?! Do you think—after I have clarified to you the existence of God Almighty with decisive proofs and brilliant evidences, and shown you that He is the Creator of things, their causes, and their regularities—that I would contradict myself and say that the miracle (which is nothing more than a breaking of custom) is part of the impossible that cannot occur?! How can you expect from science to contradict itself: once it establishes that God is the cause of causes and the link between them and their effects, then deny that another time to say that the system of causes and effects is necessary and cannot be broken? How can you expect from science to say to you: the system of the universe is of the category of the possible, then turn around and say: no, it is of the category of the necessary?!'
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is the second part of the answer, now from general science. Buti personifies 'science' speaking. General science (which includes rational proofs) has already proven that God exists as the Necessary Being and Creator of causes and effects. Therefore, it would be contradictory for this same science to deny the possibility of miracles, which are simply breaches of the usual pattern of cause and effect. If God is the ultimate cause, He can override secondary causes. Thus, the possibility of miracles is a logical consequence of theism.

Key Terms

خرق العادة
مسبب الأسباب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Science (as a whole) has shown that miracles cannot happen because they violate natural laws.
Correction: Buti argues that 'general science' (which includes rational proofs for God's existence) actually supports miracles: if God exists as the cause of causes, He can freely break the patterns He instituted.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why must general science affirm the possibility of miracles?
A) Because science has witnessed them.
B) Because if God exists as the cause of causes, He can break natural patterns.
C) Because the universe is necessary and cannot change.
D) Because science has no authority.

Key Takeaway
General science, having proven God as the Necessary Being and cause of all causes, logically affirms the possibility of miracles as acts of a free Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Consistency of General Science: Miracles Are Possible
Buti presents the response of general science on miracles, including quotes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how science in its broadest sense, when it affirms God as Creator, must also affirm the possibility of miracles as breaches of natural regularities.

Core Idea
A consistent science that acknowledges God cannot deny miracles.

In this passage, Buti continues the dialogue with the skeptic who has previously been convinced of God's existence. When asked about miracles, science in its general meaning responds by pointing out the logical contradiction of denying miracles after affirming a Creator. Through rhetorical questioning and supporting quotes, Buti shows that the possibility of miracles follows necessarily from belief in God.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Recall that the questioner has just accepted the proof of God's existence through general science. Now they ask about miracles.
This sets up the contradiction that science will point out.
2
Identify the rhetorical strategy
Science uses a rhetorical question to highlight the inconsistency: if God is the Creator of causes, how can miracles be impossible?
The passage 'How can you expect science to contradict itself...' is key.
3
Examine the supporting quotes
Malebranche and William Jones are cited to reinforce the argument. Malebranche notes the hidden divine link; Jones argues that 'inconceivable' is relative.
These quotes are from Western philosophers, showing the argument transcends traditions.
4
Note the final address to atheists
Buti distinguishes between those who deny God and those who affirm Him. An atheist may deny miracles, but cannot speak in the name of science.
This sharpens the point: science itself does not oppose miracles.
5
Connect to the main argument
The possibility of miracles is a rational consequence of theistic belief. A consistent worldview must accept both the Creator and His ability to intervene.
This lesson solidifies the logical link between divine existence and miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

-
أجل . هذا هو جواب العلم في كلمات مختصرة واضحة . وهو جواب يستطيع أن يسمعه ويعيه كل عاقل أخلص للعلم على وجه الأرض
يقول الفيلسوف مالبرانش : « إنما نرى نحن توالي الحادثات ولا نرى الرابطة التي تربط أحد الطرفين بالآخر ، فلماذا تبقى هذه الرابطة متخفية عنـا ؟ لكونها شيئاً إلهياً لا يوجد مثله في المخلوق »
واسمع ما يقوله العالم الإنكليزي « وليم جونز » :
القدرة التي خلقت العالم ، لا تعجز عن حذف شيء منه أو إضافة شيء إليه ، ومن السهل أن يقال عنه : إنه غير متصور عند العقل ، ولكن الذي يقال عنه إنه غير متصور ، ليس غير متصور إلى درجة وجود العالم أي إنه لو لم يكن جزء من هذا العالم موجوداً ، وقيل لـواحد ممن ينكر المعجزات والخوارق ولا يتصور وجودها : سيوجد عالم بالشكل الفلاني ، فإنه سيبادر قائلاً : إن هذا غير متصور ، ويأتي نفيه لذلك أشد من نفي المعجزة التي ينكرها ، مع أنها بعد وجودها لا تحرك شيئاً من الاستغراب أو الدهشة في عقله وينظر إليها دون أن يقول : إن وجود هذا الشيء أمر غير ممكن أو متصور !! ..
أما إن كنت لا تؤمن بوجود الله عز وجل أصلاً ، فلك الحق كله في أن تنكر المعجزات ولا تتصور وقوعها . ولكن ليس لك حينئذ أن تسأل ذلك عن العلم ، أو أن تتكلم باسمه أو تروي شيئاً عنه ، اعتقد ما شئت وعبر عن اعتقادك كما تشاء . ولكن دون أن تلوك كلمة ( العلم ) في فمك أو تجمـل بـه شيئاً من حديثك .
إن العلم لا يلبث أن يقول لك عند أول مقابلة معه : إن هذا الذي تراه في (1) انظر كتاب موقف العقل والعلم : ٤ - ٣٤ . (2) المرجع السابق : ٢ / ١٢٣
Then you turn from it to ask science (in its second, more general meaning) about its opinion on the miracle and its judgment on it. He says to you: You ask me about the possibility of the miracle, which is the extraordinary matter, and you asked me before about the existence of God Almighty and I answered you that He is the Necessary Existence, He in whose essence there is no ambiguity or doubt?! Do you think – after I have clarified to you the existence of God Almighty with decisive proofs and brilliant demonstrations, and shown you that He is the Creator of things, their causes and their regularities – that I would contradict myself and say: The miracle (which is nothing more than a breaking of custom) is part of the impossible that cannot occur?! How can you expect science to contradict itself, establishing once that God is the Cause of causes and the link between them and their effects, then denying that another time to say: The system of causes and effects is necessary and cannot be breached? How can you expect science to say to you: The system of the universe is of the category of the possible, then return to say to you: No, it is of the category of the necessary?!
Yes. This is the answer of science in brief clear words. And it is an answer that every rational person sincere to science on the face of the earth can hear and comprehend.
The philosopher Malebranche says: 'We only see the succession of events and we do not see the link that connects one end to the other. So why does this link remain hidden from us? Because it is a divine thing, the like of which does not exist in creation.'
And listen to what the English scientist William Jones says:
'The power that created the world is not incapable of deleting something from it or adding something to it. It is easy to say about it: It is inconceivable to the mind, but that which is said to be inconceivable is not inconceivable to the degree of the existence of the world. That is, if a part of this world did not exist, and it was said to one who denies miracles and marvels and does not conceive their existence: A world of such and such form will come into existence, he will hasten to say: This is inconceivable, and his denial of that will be stronger than his denial of the miracle that he denies, while after its existence it does not stir any astonishment or surprise in his mind, and he looks at it without saying: The existence of this thing is impossible or inconceivable!!
But if you do not believe in the existence of God Almighty at all, you have every right to deny miracles and not conceive their occurrence. But then you have no right to ask that of science, or to speak in its name, or to relate anything about it. Believe what you wish and express your belief as you like, but without chewing the word 'science' in your mouth or adorning your speech with it.
Science does not delay in saying to you at the first meeting with it: This that you see in (1) See the book 'The Position of Reason and Science': pp. 4-34. (2) Previous reference: 2/123.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage continues the dialogue. After science in its first sense declines to judge miracles, the questioner turns to science in its second, more general sense (which includes rational and theological knowledge). This science replies by pointing out a contradiction: if the questioner already accepts the proof for God's existence – that He is the Necessary Being, the Creator of causes and their regularities – then it would be contradictory to deny the possibility of miracles, which are simply God's breaking of those regularities. Miracles are not impossible; they are merely extraordinary. Science in this sense would be inconsistent if it affirmed a necessary, unbreakable causal system after having proven that God is the free Creator who established that system. The passage then quotes Malebranche and William Jones in support: Malebranche notes that the causal link between events is not observed empirically, but is a divine reality; Jones argues that the same mind that finds a miracle 'inconceivable' would find the non-existence of a part of the world even more inconceivable, showing that inconceivability is not a reliable criterion. Finally, the author addresses the atheist: if one denies God altogether, one may logically deny miracles, but then one should not invoke science – because science itself (in its full sense) is grounded in the recognition of God. The last line reinforces that science does not claim to have a problem with miracles; rather, the problem is with those who misuse the word 'science'.

المعجزة
الخارق للعادة
واجب الوجود
نظام الأسباب والمسببات
مالبرانش
وليم جونز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Science (in its general sense) must deny miracles as impossible.
Correction: Science in its broader meaning, which includes rational and theological knowledge, cannot consistently deny miracles because it has already affirmed God as the Creator who established the causal regularities. Miracles are possible as acts of that same Creator.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what logical consequence follows from affirming God's existence as the Creator of causes?
A) The universe is eternal.
B) Miracles are impossible because they break the causal laws.
C) Miracles are possible since God can breach the regularities He created.
D) Science has no opinion on miracles.

Key Takeaway
General science, when consistent, does not deny miracles; rather, it affirms their possibility as acts of the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter something that seems impossible by natural laws, does your heart immediately dismiss it as impossible, or do you remember that the Creator of those laws can break them? What would change if you truly internalized this lesson?
?
Have you ever used the word 'science' to justify a doubt about a miracle or divine intervention in your life? In what specific situation? What would it mean for you to stop 'chewing the word science' and instead submit to God's absolute power?
?
If you were in a situation where all natural hope was lost—like a terminal illness or an impossible financial crisis—would your faith in God's ability to intervene be stronger than your fear of what seems 'inconceivable' to your mind? What step can you take today to build that certainty?

Science, Causality, and Miracles: A Warning to Deniers of God
Warns atheists not to speak in the name of science, then science explains causality is habitual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying God does not give one the authority to speak in the name of science, and how science itself affirms that causality is only a constant correlation that can be broken by the First Cause, making all of creation a miracle.

Core Idea
Science does not deny miracles; it reveals that everything is a miracle.

This passage addresses those who reject God's existence but claim to speak for science. The author warns them not to misuse the term 'science' and then presents what science truly says: causality is a habitual correlation, not a necessary law, and the First Cause can undo it. Moreover, both familiar and unfamiliar phenomena are equally miraculous when seen without the veil of familiarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking, then read the translation. Let the author's voice come through before analysis.
2
Identify the conditional warning
Notice the opening: those who do not believe in God have rights but lose the right to speak for science. This sets the stage.
The author is addressing atheists who might try to use science as an authority against miracles.
3
Understand science's definition of causality
Science says causality is only a constant correlation, not a necessary connection. The First Cause can break it at will.
This is a key point: science itself does not assert necessity in causality.
4
Reflect on the list of miracles
The passage lists many phenomena as miracles: planets, gravity, plants, the human mind, etc. Consider why familiarity hides their miraculous nature.
The author ends by explaining that we ignorantly think a miracle must be unexpected, but everything is a miracle.

أما إن كنت لا تؤمن بوجود الله عز وجل أصلاً ، فلك الحق كله في أن تنكر المعجزات ولا تتصور وقوعها . ولكن ليس لك حينئذ أن تسأل ذلك عن العلم ، أو أن تتكلم باسمه أو تروي شيئاً عنه ، اعتقد ما شئت وعبر عن اعتقادك كما تشاء . ولكن دون أن تلوك كلمة ( العلم ) في فمك أو تجعل به شيئاً من حديثك . إن العلم لا يلبث أن يقول لك عند أول مقابلة معه : إن هذا الذي تراه في الأشياء مما تسميه نظام السببية ليس أكثر من رابطة مطردة تراها بعينك وهيهات أن يكون ذلك مستلزماً لوجوب الاستمرار واستحالة الانفكاك . إن المسبب الأول لا يعجزه شيء عن إبطال هذا التلازم والترابط الصوري الذي تراه . وإن كان طول الإلف واستمرار الاتصال يثير فيك العجب والاستغراب من وقوع ذلك . بل العلم يقول لك : إنك لو تأملت ، لرأيت أن المألوف وغير المألوف من مظاهر الكون معجزة في الحقيقة إذا ما غفلت عن ملاحظة الخالق العظيم . فالكواكب معجزة ، وحركة الأفلاك معجزة . وقانون الجاذبية معجزة ، والنباتات معجزة ، والعقل البشري معجزة والمجموعة العصبية في الإنسان معجزة والدورة الدموية فيه معجزة ، والإنسان في ذاته معجزة ! .. غير أنك تنسى - لطول الإلف واستمرار الرؤية - وجه المعجزة في هذا كله ، فتحسب جهلاً وغروراً أن المعجزة ليست إلا تلك التي تفاجئ ما اعتـدتـه وألفتـه بـالمعاكسة والتغيير .
But if you do not believe in the existence of God Almighty at all, then you have every right to deny miracles and not conceive of their occurrence. But you have no right then to ask about that in the name of science, or to speak in its name or relate anything about it. Believe what you wish and express your belief as you like. But without chewing the word 'science' in your mouth or using it in any of your speech. Science does not delay in telling you upon first meeting it: This that you see in things, that which you call the system of causality, is nothing more than a constant correlation that you see with your eye, and far be it that this entails necessary continuation and impossibility of separation. The First Cause is not incapable of nullifying this apparent correlation and connection that you see. Even if prolonged familiarity and continuous connection arouses in you wonder and astonishment at its occurrence. Rather, science tells you: If you reflected, you would see that the familiar and unfamiliar manifestations of the universe are in reality a miracle if you neglect to notice the Great Creator. So the planets are a miracle, the movement of the spheres is a miracle, the law of gravity is a miracle, plants are a miracle, the human mind is a miracle, the nervous system in man is a miracle, the circulatory system in him is a miracle, and man himself is a miracle! But you forget—due to prolonged familiarity and continual sight—the aspect of miracle in all this, so you ignorantly and arrogantly suppose that the miracle is only that which surprises what you are accustomed to and familiar with by opposition and change.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a conditional warning followed by an exposition. The author first addresses those who do not believe in God at all: they have the right to deny miracles, but they lose the right to speak in the name of science. They may hold their own beliefs but must not misuse the word 'science'. Then the author gives science's own speech. Science says that what is called causality is only a constant observed correlation, not a necessary connection. The First Cause (God) can break this correlation at will. Prolonged habit leads to astonishment at anything out of the ordinary, but in reality, both familiar and unfamiliar phenomena are equally miraculous when viewed apart from God. The author lists examples: planets, movement of spheres, gravity, plants, the human mind, nervous system, circulatory system, and man himself—all are miracles. But due to familiarity, people forget the miraculous aspect and wrongly think a miracle must be a violation of the usual order.

Key Terms
السببية
الرابطة المطردة
المسبب الأول
الإلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Science proves causality is a necessary law that cannot be broken.
Correction: Science actually says causality is only a constant correlation, and the First Cause (God) can break it at will.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does science say about the system of causality?
A) It is a necessary and unbreakable natural law.
B) It is a constant correlation that the First Cause can nullify.
C) It is an illusion with no basis in reality.
D) It is the only evidence for God's existence.

Key Takeaway
The universe, in both its familiar and unfamiliar aspects, is a miracle pointing to the Creator, and science does not contradict this truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that the familiar is a miracle. What is one thing in your life that you have taken for granted, and how would your relationship with the Creator change if you saw it as a miracle right now? Will you make a sincere intention to thank Him for it today?
?
The passage warns atheists not to use 'science' to deny God. But what about you—do you ever use intellectual arguments to avoid submitting to the reality of God in your daily life? What is one area where your actions betray a belief in causality as necessary rather than a sign of Allah's power?
?
If all of creation is a miracle from God, why do you still find yourself bored, ungrateful, or disconnected from Him? What specific habit of 'familiarity' (al-ulf) has blinded you, and what step will you take tomorrow to break it?

The Limits of Reason in Knowing Man's Origin
Buti establishes the epistemic limitation for knowing man's origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human reason cannot achieve certainty about the first creation of man, and why divine revelation is necessary.

Core Idea
Reason alone cannot uncover man's origin; only revelation brings certainty.

Buti begins by establishing a fundamental epistemic principle: matters not clarified by Allah and His Messenger are left to Allah's knowledge, unless they are subject to empirical investigation. He then applies this to the origin of man, showing that it falls outside the realm of experiment and observation, leaving only weak conjecture. Thus, without divine revelation, no certain creed can be formed.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the epistemic principle
Read the first sentence: Buti states that what Allah and His Messenger have not clarified is left to Allah alone, except what is subject to research and experiment. This sets the framework for the discussion.
Notice the exception for empirical matters — Buti is not rejecting all human knowledge.
2
Identify the two weak indicators
Buti says that for the historical narrative of man's first creation, human reasoning can only use conjecture (tawassum) and inference (istirdād), which are illusory and cannot produce certainty. Understand why these are insufficient for creed.
Conjecture and inference are based on incomplete evidence, unlike direct observation or revelation.
3
Understand the necessity of revelation
The passage concludes that without a definitive divine report, no certain belief can be established. This leads to the need for a true, mass-transmitted report (khabar mutawātir) from Allah.
This sets up the next lesson where the scriptural evidence is presented.

وسنة رسوله أن نكل علم مالم يبينه الله عز وجل ولا رسوله إلى علم الله وحده اللهم إلا ماكان من ذلك خاضعاً لوسائل البحث والتجربة والمشاهدة ، فقد دعتنا كلام الله تعالى إلى البحث عن الحقيقة والتنقيب عن اليقين في ذلك ج - الإنسان مخلوق منذ النشأة الأولى في أتم مظهر وأحسن تقويم : ( والحديث عن النشأة الأولى للإنسان ، لا يخضع هو الآخر لبراهين التجربة والمشاهدة المحسوسة ، إذ هو في جملته حديث تاريخي لن تستطيع أن تعمل فيه الفكر والنظر بأكثر من دليلي التوسم والاسترداد ، وهما دليلان وهميان كما سبق أن أوضحنا ذلك ، يستحيل إقامة عقيدة قطعية على شيء من نتائجها . • ولو أن الله عز وجل لم يحدثنا بشيء قطعي في هذا الصدد ، لما التزمنا في شأنه بأي حكم نعتقده ونقطع به ولكن الخبر الصادق المتواتر ، وضعنا في ذلك أمام مالا مجال للشك أو الظن فيه . وهو قوله تعالى : ( لقد خلقنا الإنسان في أحسَن تقويم ﴾ [ التين : ٤ ] و « أل » الداخلة على الإنسان للاستغراق كما هو معلوم ، فهي عامة للأفراد كلهم .. ومثل ذلك قوله تعالى و يا أيها الإنسانُ ماغَرَّكَ بِرَبِّكَ الكَرِيمِ الَّذِي خَلَقَكَ فَسَوَّاكَ فَعَدَلَكَ ﴾ [ الانفطار : ٦ - ٧] أي جعلك سوياً مستقيماً معتدل القامة منتصبها في أحسن الهيئات والأشكال. ومن مؤكدات هذه الحقيقة التي قررها القرآن ، ماروي في الصحيحين عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه أن رسول الله قال : « خلق الله آدم على صورته .. » أي أنه منذ خُلق إنما كانت صورته هي الصورة ذاتها التي استمر عليها وعرف بها ، أي لم يُنَشَّأ متنقلاً من شكل إلى آخر . فالضمير في صورته راجع إلى آدم . وهناك رأي آخر ، يرى أن الضمير راجع إلى ذات الله تعالى ، والمقصود بالصورة الصفة ، أي خلقه عالماً مريداً حكيماً سميعاً بصيراً .. وتلك صفات هي الله تعالى ( انظر ص ۱۳۸ من هذا الكتاب ) . وسواء أعدت الضمير على آدم ، كما هو رأي الجمهور ويدل عليـه ظـاهر الحديث ، أو أعدته إلى ذات الله تعالى ، فالحديث تأكيد للدلالة القطعية في القرآن ، إذ البحث في معرض بيان تكريم الله لآدم منذ أول خلقه · وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، وجب أن نعلم بأن الإنسان لم يتنقل . خلال تاريخه كله ، في أي تطور نوعي . كأن يقال إنه ترقى من فصيلة إلى أخرى ، أو تدرج من مظهر نوعي في الهيئة والشكل إلى مظهر آخر وهذا الحكم نتيجة قطعية للأمور الثلاثة التي ذكرناها عن الإنسان ، وهي : أنه أفضل المخلوقات وأشرفها أنه مخلوق من التراب ، ومتكاثر من آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام . أنه خلق ) في نشأته الأولى ( في أحسن تقويم .
And the Sunnah of His Messenger is that we delegate knowledge of what Allah Mighty and Majestic and His Messenger have not clarified to the knowledge of Allah alone, except for what is subject to the means of research, experiment, and observation. For the speech of Allah Almighty has called us to search for the truth and to dig for certainty in that. (J) Man is created since the first beginning in the most complete appearance and the best form. And the discussion of the first beginning of man is not subject to proofs of experiment and sensory observation, for it is in its entirety a historical narrative; thought and reflection cannot work in it beyond the two indicators of conjecture (tawassum) and inference (istirdād), and they are two illusory indicators as we have explained before; it is impossible to establish a definitive creed (ʿaqīda qaṭʿiyya) on anything from their results. And if Allah Almighty had not told us something definitive in this regard, we would not have been obligated concerning it with any ruling that we believe and are certain of. But the true and mass-transmitted report (al-khabar al-ṣādiq al-mutawātir) has placed us in front of that which leaves no room for doubt or conjecture. It is His saying: 'Indeed, We created man in the best form' (Quran 95:4). And the definite article 'al' entering upon 'insān' is for universal inclusion (istiġrāq) as is known, so it is general for all individuals. And likewise His saying: 'O man, what has deceived you concerning your Lord, the Generous, Who created you, then proportioned you, and then balanced you?' (Quran 82:6-7), meaning He made you sound, straight, moderate in stature, upright in the best forms and shapes. And from the affirmations of this fact that the Quran has established is what is narrated in the two Sahihs on the authority of Abu Hurayra, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Allah created Adam upon His image' – meaning that from the time he was created, his form was the very same form that he continued upon and was known by, i.e., he was not raised moving from one form to another. So the pronoun in 'His image' refers back to Adam. And there is another opinion which holds that the pronoun refers to the Essence of Allah Almighty, and the intended meaning of 'image' is the attribute; i.e., He created him knowing, willing, wise, hearing, seeing – and these are attributes of Allah Almighty (see p. 138 of this book). Whether you refer the pronoun to Adam, as is the opinion of the majority and indicated by the apparent meaning of the hadith, or you refer it to the Essence of Allah Almighty, the hadith is a confirmation of the definitive indication in the Quran, since the discussion is in the context of expressing Allah's honor for Adam since his first creation. And if that is the case, then it becomes necessary that we know that man did not, throughout his entire history, undergo any typological evolution (taṭawwur nawʿī), as if it were said that he advanced from one species to another, or progressed from one typological appearance in form and shape to another. And this ruling is a definitive result of the three matters that we have mentioned about man: that he is the most excellent and most honorable of created beings; that he is created from dust, and multiplied from Adam, peace and blessings be upon him; that he was created (in his first beginning) in the best form.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument establishing the origin of man as known through revelation, not empirical science, and refuting evolutionary theory. The author begins by stating the general principle that matters not clarified by Allah and His Messenger are left to Allah's knowledge alone, except those subject to research, experiment, and observation. Then he specifies that the first creation of man is not subject to such experimental proofs because it is a historical narrative; human reasoning can only employ the indicators of conjecture (tawassum) and inference (istirdād), which are illusory and cannot produce certainty. Therefore, without a definitive divine report, no certain creed could be established. However, Allah has provided a true mass-transmitted report (khabar mutawātir) that leaves no room for doubt. The author cites Quran 95:4, 'Indeed, We created man in the best form,' explaining that the definite article 'al' in 'al-insān' indicates universal inclusion, so it applies to all human individuals. He also cites Quran 82:6-7, explaining that 'balanced you' means He made man upright and well-proportioned. The hadith from Sahihain, 'Allah created Adam upon His image,' is then discussed. The author presents two interpretations: the majority opinion that the pronoun refers to Adam (i.e., Adam was created in his own final form from the beginning, not evolving) and another opinion that the pronoun refers to Allah, meaning Adam was created with attributes like knowledge, will, wisdom, hearing, and sight. Both interpretations confirm the definitive Quranic indication of man's original honor and completeness. Based on these evidences, the author deduces a categorical conclusion: Man did not undergo any typological evolution (taṭawwur nawʿī) throughout history, advancing from one species to another or changing bodily forms. This conclusion is a necessary result of three previously mentioned facts about man: (1) he is the most excellent and honorable creation, (2) he was created from dust and multiplied from Adam, and (3) he was created in the best form from the beginning. The argument is presented in a logical sequence: statement of epistemic limitation, necessity of revelation, scriptural proofs, interpretation of hadith, and final definitive ruling against human evolution.

Key Terms
النشأة الأولى
التوسم
الاسترداد

Checkpoint
According to Buti, why can human reason not achieve certainty about the first creation of man?
A) Because it is a matter of faith, not reason
B) Because it is a historical narrative that cannot be observed or experimented on
C) Because the Quran prohibits speculation
D) Because the hadith are contradictory

Key Takeaway
Human reason alone cannot achieve certainty about man's origin; only divine revelation can provide a definitive creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you feel uncertain about your origins, do you turn to revelation with full trust, or do you seek to fill the gaps with speculation? What would it take for you to submit completely to divine reports on matters beyond your experience?
?
Think of a belief you hold about your creation that you have never questioned. Is it based on certain revelation or mere conjecture? If it is conjecture, are you ready to abandon it for the sake of certainty?

Scriptural Proof of Man's Original Perfection
Buti presents scriptural evidence and concludes against typological evolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitive scriptural evidence from Quran and hadith that man was created in the best form from the beginning, and how this leads to the conclusion that no typological evolution occurred.

Core Idea
Scripture proves man was created perfect from the start, refuting any evolutionary change.

Having shown the insufficiency of reason, Buti now presents the decisive evidence: the true mass-transmitted report of revelation. He cites Quranic verses and a hadith, discussing their interpretations. This evidence leads to a categorical conclusion: man did not undergo any typological evolution throughout history.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the definitive nature of khabar mutawātir
Buti states that the true mass-transmitted report leaves no room for doubt. Understand that this type of report provides certainty.
Khabar mutawātir is a report transmitted by so many narrators that collusion on falsehood is impossible.
2
Examine Quran 95:4 and its universal scope
The verse 'Indeed, We created man in the best form' is cited. Buti explains that the definite article 'al' in 'al-insān' indicates universal inclusion, applying to all humans.
This establishes that all humans were created in the best form from the start.
3
Analyze the hadith and its two interpretations
The hadith 'Allah created Adam upon His image' is discussed. Buti presents two interpretations: the majority view that the pronoun refers to Adam (i.e., Adam was created in his final form), and another that it refers to Allah (i.e., Adam was created with divine attributes like knowledge). Both confirm the original perfection.
Neither interpretation supports evolution; both affirm Adam's creation in a complete, non-evolutionary state.
4
Draw the conclusion against typological evolution
Based on the three facts about man (honor, creation from dust, and best form), Buti concludes that man did not undergo any typological evolution throughout history.
This is a definitive result, not a speculative opinion.

So the pronoun in 'His image' refers back to Adam. And there is another opinion which holds that the pronoun refers to the Essence of Allah Almighty, and the intended meaning of 'image' is the attribute; i.e., He created him knowing, willing, wise, hearing, seeing – and these are attributes of Allah Almighty (see p. 138 of this book). Whether you refer the pronoun to Adam, as is the opinion of the majority and indicated by the apparent meaning of the hadith, or you refer it to the Essence of Allah Almighty, the hadith is a confirmation of the definitive indication in the Quran, since the discussion is in the context of expressing Allah's honor for Adam since his first creation. And if that is the case, then it becomes necessary that we know that man did not, throughout his entire history, undergo any typological evolution (taṭawwur nawʿī), as if it were said that he advanced from one species to another, or progressed from one typological appearance in form and shape to another. And this ruling is a definitive result of the three matters that we have mentioned about man: that he is the most excellent and most honorable of created beings; that he is created from dust, and multiplied from Adam, peace and blessings be upon him; that he was created (in his first beginning) in the best form.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument establishing the origin of man as known through revelation, not empirical science, and refuting evolutionary theory. The author begins by stating the general principle that matters not clarified by Allah and His Messenger are left to Allah's knowledge alone, except those subject to research, experiment, and observation. Then he specifies that the first creation of man is not subject to such experimental proofs because it is a historical narrative; human reasoning can only employ the indicators of conjecture (tawassum) and inference (istirdād), which are illusory and cannot produce certainty. Therefore, without a definitive divine report, no certain creed could be established. However, Allah has provided a true mass-transmitted report (khabar mutawātir) that leaves no room for doubt. The author cites Quran 95:4, 'Indeed, We created man in the best form,' explaining that the definite article 'al' in 'al-insān' indicates universal inclusion, so it applies to all human individuals. He also cites Quran 82:6-7, explaining that 'balanced you' means He made man upright and well-proportioned. The hadith from Sahihain, 'Allah created Adam upon His image,' is then discussed. The author presents two interpretations: the majority opinion that the pronoun refers to Adam (i.e., Adam was created in his own final form from the beginning, not evolving) and another opinion that the pronoun refers to Allah, meaning Adam was created with attributes like knowledge, will, wisdom, hearing, and sight. Both interpretations confirm the definitive Quranic indication of man's original honor and completeness. Based on these evidences, the author deduces a categorical conclusion: Man did not undergo any typological evolution (taṭawwur nawʿī) throughout history, advancing from one species to another or changing bodily forms. This conclusion is a necessary result of three previously mentioned facts about man: (1) he is the most excellent and honorable creation, (2) he was created from dust and multiplied from Adam, and (3) he was created in the best form from the beginning. The argument is presented in a logical sequence: statement of epistemic limitation, necessity of revelation, scriptural proofs, interpretation of hadith, and final definitive ruling against human evolution.

Key Terms
أحسن تقويم
الخبر الصادق المتواتر
صورة آدم
تطور نوعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the hadith 'upon His image' supports anthropomorphism (that Allah has a physical form).
Correction: Buti clarifies that the majority view refers the pronoun to Adam, meaning Adam was created in his own final image. The alternative view refers to Allah's attributes, not physical form. Both avoid anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint

B) Man underwent some evolutionary changes but remained the same species

D) The evidence is inconclusive

Key Takeaway
The Quran and hadith decisively prove that man was created in the best form from the beginning, and therefore no typological evolution occurred.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The hadith says Adam was created upon his image. How does your belief about the origin of humanity affect the way you see every person you meet, regardless of their appearance or background? What will you do this week to treat someone as the noble creature Allah made them?

Distinguishing Evolution from the Gradation in Creation
Buti distinguishes evolution from the natural graded order in creation, citing Ibn Khaldun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti distinguishes the hypothesis of human evolution from the observable graded order in creation, and how the latter serves as a proof for God's existence.

Core Idea
Evolution is a hypothesis; the hierarchical order in creation is an undeniable sign of the Creator.

Buti has just finished discussing the hypothesis of human evolution. Now he emphasizes that this should not be confused with the obvious gradual hierarchy present in the universe from minerals to humans. This gradation, observed by all scientists, is a powerful proof of divine design. Let's read his words.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get a sense of Buti's argument.
Notice the cut-off at the end of the Ibn Khaldun quote.
2
Identify the two concepts Buti distinguishes
Find where Buti separates 'the idea of evolution' from 'gradual gradation'. Understand the difference he is drawing.
3
Understand the description of gradation
Buti describes the gradation as a 'chain of categories' like beads of a necklace. Reflect on why this imagery strengthens the argument for design.
4
Analyze the Ibn Khaldun quote
Read Ibn Khaldun's description of the progression from minerals to plants to animals. Note the connections at boundaries.
This quote is a classical example of observing order in nature.
5
Reflect on the overall proof
Consider how this gradation serves as a clear proof of the Creator's existence and creativity, distinct from evolutionary theory.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكرة التطور شيء .. والتدرج المتراصف بين الأجناس شيء ثم اعلم أن كل هذا الذي ذكرناه إنما يتعلق بفرضية تطور الإنسان ، بعد نشأته الأولى ، من فصيلة حيوانية إلى أخرى . أما التدرّج المتراصف والموجود في أصل التكوين بدءاً من الجمادات إلى النباتات ، إلى الحيوانات ، إلى الإنسان . فتلك حقيقة ثابتة منذ أقدم العصور إلى يومنا هذا ، لا العين إنكارها ، فضلاً عن العقل والفكر . فسلسلة أصناف يسع الموجودات فيها من التناسق في طريق الصعود إلى الأعلى ما يجعلها شبيهة بحبات عقد متساوقة في التدرج نحو الأكثر جمالاً وندرة • وقد تحدث العلماء جميعاً عن ظاهرة هذا التراصف المتصاعد الدال بأجلى برهان على وجود الخالق وعظيم إبداعه يقول ابن خلدون : « ثم انظر إلى عالم التكوين كيف ابتدأ بالمعادن ، ثم النبات ثم الحيوان ، على هيئة بديعة من التدرج ! .. آخر أفق المعادن متصل بأول أفق النبات ، مثل الحشائش وما لا يلد له ، وآخر أفق النبات مثل النخل والكرم متصل بأول أفق الحيوان ، مثل الحلزون والصدف . ولم يوجد لها إلا قوة
The idea of evolution is one thing, and the gradual gradation between species is another. Then know that all that we have mentioned pertains only to the hypothesis of human evolution, after its first creation, from one animal family to another. As for the gradual gradation present in the original formation, beginning from inanimate objects to plants, to animals, to man — that is a fixed truth from the earliest ages to this day, which the eye cannot deny, let alone the intellect and thought. For it is a chain of categories in which existents have such harmony on the path of ascent to the higher that makes them resemble beads of a necklace synchronized in gradation toward more beauty and rarity. And all scientists have spoken about the phenomenon of this ascending gradation, which indicates with the clearest proof the existence of the Creator and His great creativity. Ibn Khaldun says: 'Then look at the world of creation how it began with minerals, then plants, then animals, in a wonderful gradual manner! ... The last horizon of minerals is connected to the first horizon of plants, such as herbs and non-seed plants, and the last horizon of plants such as palm and vine is connected to the first horizon of animals, such as snails and shellfish. And they have only power...'
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a critical distinction and a positive argument. Buti begins by separating two concepts: 'the idea of evolution' (fiktat al-tatawwur) and 'gradual gradation between species' (al-tadarruj al-mutarasif bayna al-ajnas). He clarifies that all previous discussion about human evolution concerned the hypothesis that humans evolved from one animal family to another after their first creation. Then he introduces a different phenomenon: the gradual gradation present in the original formation of the universe, from inanimate objects to plants to animals to humans. This, he asserts, is a fixed truth observable since ancient times, undeniable by sight, let alone reason. He describes it as a chain of categories with harmony in ascending order, like beads of a necklace progressing in beauty and rarity. He then notes that all scientists have spoken about this ascending gradation as a clear proof of the Creator's existence and magnificent creativity. To support this, he quotes Ibn Khaldun, who describes the gradual progression from minerals to plants to animals, noting the connections at the boundaries. The quote is cut off but reinforces the idea of a designed gradation rather than random evolution. The lesson thus distinguishes the rejected hypothesis of human evolution from the accepted fact of a hierarchical order in creation, which serves as a proof of God.

تطور
تدرج متراصف
تراصف متصاعد
ابن خلدون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think the observable graded order in creation is the same as the theory of evolution.
Correction: Buti clarifies that evolution is a hypothesis about changes within species, whereas the gradation is a fixed, observable hierarchy that points to a Creator, not a natural process.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The hierarchical gradation from minerals to humans is a clear observable sign of the Creator's wisdom and power, and must not be confused with theories of evolution.

Distinction between Evolution and Progressive Gradation
Buti distinguishes evolution hypothesis from observed gradation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the crucial distinction between the hypothesis of evolution and the observed phenomenon of progressive gradation in creation, and why the latter is a fixed reality.

Core Idea
Evolution is a hypothesis; progressive gradation is a visible truth.

Buti draws a sharp line between two often-conflated ideas: the theory of evolution (specifically regarding human origins) and the undeniable fact of progressive gradation in the natural world. Before engaging with the details, he wants us to see that these are completely different things — one is a speculative hypothesis, the other is an observable reality.

Evolution is linked to a hypothesis about human origins; gradation is about the entire chain of creation.

Quotes from Ibn Khaldun and Ibn Miskawayh on Gradation
Buti presents quotations from Ibn Khaldun and Ibn Miskawayh on the gradation of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the ascending gradation of creation serves as a proof for the existence and wisdom of the Creator.

Core Idea
The ascending gradation of creation is a clear proof of the Creator's existence and wisdom.

Buti reinforces his argument by citing two renowned scholars: Ibn Khaldun and Ibn Miskawayh. Their descriptions of the interconnected levels of creation—from minerals to plants to animals to humans—reveal a deliberate design. As you read, notice how each scholar uses vivid imagery to illustrate the unity and gradation of existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation

وقد تحدث العلماء جميعاً عن ظاهرة هذا التراصف المتصاعد الدال بأجلى برهان على وجود الخالق وعظيم إبداعه يقول ابن خلدون : « ثم انظر إلى عالم التكوين كيف ابتدأ بالمعادن ، ثم النبات ثم الحيوان ، على هيئة بديعة من التدرج ! .. آخر أفق المعادن متصل بأول أفق النبات ، مثل الحشائش وما لا يلد له ، وآخر أفق النبات مثل النخل والكرم متصل بأول أفق الحيوان ، مثل الحلزون والصدف . ولم يوجد لها إلا قوة اللمس فقط . ومعنى الاتصال في هذه المكونات أن آخر أفق منها مستعد بالاستعداد الغريب لأن يصير أول أفق الذي بعده ، واتسع عالم الحيوان وتعددت أنواعه ، وانتهى في تدريج التكوين إلى الإنسان صاحب الفكر والروية (۱) إلخ . ويقول ابن مسكويه : « فأما اتصال الموجودات التي نقول إن الحكمة سارية فيها ، حتى إذا أوجدتها وأظهرت التدبير المتقن من قبل الواحد الحق في جميعها ، حتى اتصل آخر كل نوع بأول نوع آخر ، فصار كالسلك الواحد الذي ينظم خرزاً كثيراً على تأليف صحيح ، وحتى جاء من الجميع عقد واحد ، فهو الذي ننبه عليه بالدلالة بمعونة الله ) ثم بدأ يطيل في تفصيل هذا التدرج وبيانه على النحو الذي أوضحه ابن خلدون .

And the meaning of connection in these formations is that the last horizon of them is prepared with a strange readiness to become the first horizon of what follows it, and the animal world expanded and its types multiplied, and it ended in the gradation of formation to man, the possessor of intellect and deliberation.' Then he began to elaborate on this gradation and its explanation in the manner that Ibn Khaldun clarified.

Gradation: An Observed Fact vs. Darwinian Evolution
Buti concludes with a reaffirmation of gradation and a rejection of evolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the gradation observed in nature is a factual reality distinct from the baseless hypothesis of Darwinian evolution, and why seeking Islamic validation for Western theories is misguided.

Core Idea
The observed gradation in the universe is a fact; evolution is a baseless hypothesis.

Buti concludes his discussion by reaffirming the universal observation of gradation in the cosmos. He then contrasts this with Darwinian evolution, which he dismisses as a false hypothesis. Finally, he warns against a trend among some Muslims to find Islamic backing for every Western theory, pointing to the misuse of statements by Ibn Khaldun and Ibn Miskawayh.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.

2
Distinguish between gradation and evolution

3
Understand the critique of religious validation

This connects to the learning objective about avoiding misguided validation.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
The common misunderstanding is that Ibn Khaldun's descriptions support Darwinian evolution. Buti implies they do not. Why? Because gradation is a fixed hierarchy, not transformation.
This is a key point for the lesson.

Correction: Buti indicates that this is a misinterpretation: the gradation described by those scholars is a fixed observed order, not a process of transformation from one species to another.

Checkpoint
How does the author regard the Darwinian theory of evolution?
A) A hypothesis that needs more evidence
B) A false hypothesis with no basis
C) A plausible theory
D) A proven scientific fact

Key Takeaway
The gradation in creation is an undeniable fact; Darwinian evolution is a baseless hypothesis not supported by Islamic sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a new scientific theory, do you immediately search for an Islamic justification, or do you first evaluate it based on the Qur'an and Sunnah? How can you train yourself to submit to revelation before being swayed by Western ideas?
?
The passage calls the search for Islamic support for evolution 'amusing' but also a serious error. Have you ever accepted an idea because it came from the West and then tried to find it in Islam? What did that reveal about your heart's attachment—is it to truth or to the prestige of Western scholarship?
?
Buti states the gradation in creation is an undeniable fact witnessed by all rational observers. Does your awe of creation lead you to the Creator? Or have you become so familiar with the universe that you no longer see the hand of Allah in its perfect order?
