The Gradation of Creation: An Islamic Perspective
Buti explains the Islamic gradation of creation and quotes Ibn Miskawayh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic concept of the gradation of creation and how the universe is connected through divine wisdom.

Core Idea
Creation is a single, interconnected hierarchy culminating in humanity.

Before addressing modern evolutionary theories, Buti establishes the true Islamic understanding of the cosmic order. He explains how each level of creation is linked to the next in a purposeful chain, from the simplest elements to human beings. This passage presents this concept as an observed reality, deeply rooted in Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of 'connection'
Focus on how the last horizon of each level is prepared to become the first of the next. This is the key mechanism of the gradation.
Note the phrase 'استعداد غريب' – a unique readiness.
2
Examine Ibn Miskawayh's analogy
He compares the connected existents to a single string of beads, emphasizing the unity and order created by divine wisdom.
3
Understand the observational claim
Buti asserts that this gradation is an empirical fact seen by all rational observers, not a theoretical construct.
This sets the stage for refuting Darwinism in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللمس [؟] فقط . ومعنى الاتصال في هذه المكونات أن آخر أفق منها مستعد بالاستعداد الغريب لأن يصير أول أفق الذي بعده ، واتسع عالم الحيوان وتعددت أنواعه ، وانتهى في تدريج التكوين إلى الإنسان صاحب الفكر والروية إلخ. (1) ويقول ابن مسكويه : « فأما اتصال الموجودات التي نقول إن الحكمة سارية فيها ، حتى إذا أوجدتها وأظهرت التدبير المتقن من قبل الواحد الحق في جميعها ، حتى اتصل آخر كل نوع بأول نوع آخر ، فصار كالسلك الواحد الذي ينظم خرزاً كثيراً على تأليف صحيح ، وحتى جاء من الجميع عقد واحد ، فهو الذي ننبه عليه بالدلالة بمعونة الله » (2) ثم بدأ يطيل في تفصيل هذا التدرج وبيانه على النحو الذي أوضحه ابن خلدون . فهذه حقيقة وصفية مشاهدة ، قائمة كما هي منذ أقدم العصور التي وعاها الإنسان ، يراها ويتحدث عنها جميع العلماء ، بل يراها ويعجب بها جميع الناظرين العقلاء . ولا شأن لها إطلاقاً بما افترضه الداروينيون ونحوهم من تطور كل نوع من النوع الذي دونه ، سواء بالنسبة للإنسان وغيره . فهي فرضية باطلة لا أصل لها كما قد علمت . ومن الطرائف أن بعضاً ممن لا تزال تستهويهم بحوث الغربيين وأفكارهم ، يبحثون لكل فكرة يقول بها باحث غربي عن تأكيد لها في بطون القرآن أو السنة أو فيما دوّنه عالم من علماء المسلمين !... ولما سمعوا بنظريات التطور ، أسرعوا يبحثون عن مؤيد لها في أي مصدر إسلامي ، حتى إذا عثروا على هذا الذي يقوله كثير من علماء المسلمين من أمثال ابن خلدون وابن مسكويه ، وضعوا أيديهم من ذلك على ما يشبه كنزاً ثميناً اكتشفوه . وراحوا يؤكدون ببالغ الزهو والفرح بأن علماء المسلمين قد سبقوا داروين بمئات السنين !.. ونحن نقول : لو أن عالماً من علماء المسلمين سبق داروين إلى نظريته التي جاء بها ، لما دلّ ذلك إلا على سبق ذلك العالم عليه في السخف والباطل اللذين نبرأ إلى الله منهما . ألا إن من أشد أنواع الظلم ، أن يجرّد الكلام السليم من معناه ، ثم يلصق به الباطل ، دعماً لوساوس المبطلين ، وإمعاناً في تقليدهم والسير وراءهم أنى ساروا .
The touch [?] only. And the meaning of connection in these components is that the last horizon of them is prepared with a strange readiness to become the first horizon of what comes after it, and the animal world expanded and its species multiplied, and it ended in the gradation of formation to man, the possessor of intellect and vision, etc. (1) And Ibn Miskawayh says: 'As for the connection of existing things in which we say wisdom is flowing, such that when you bring them into existence and show the precise management from the One Truth in all of them, until the last of every kind is connected to the first of another kind, so it becomes like a single thread that strings many beads in a correct arrangement, and until from all there comes a single knot, that is what we point to by indication with the help of God.' (2) Then he began to elaborate in detail this gradation and its explanation in the manner that Ibn Khaldun clarified. So this is an observed descriptive reality, existing as it is since the earliest ages that man has recorded, all scholars see it and speak about it, rather all rational observers see it and marvel at it. And it has absolutely nothing to do with what the Darwinians and their like assumed of the evolution of each species from the species below it, whether with respect to man or other than him. So it is a false hypothesis with no basis, as you have learned. And among the oddities is that some of those who are still attracted by Western research and ideas are searching for every idea that a Western researcher comes up with to find confirmation for it in the depths of the Qur'an or the Sunna or what a scholar of Muslim scholars wrote!... And when they heard about the theories of evolution, they hastened to search for support for it in any Islamic source, until they came across this which many Muslim scholars like Ibn Khaldun and Ibn Miskawayh say, they seized upon it as if it were a precious treasure they had discovered. And they began to proclaim with utmost pride and joy that Muslim scholars had preceded Darwin by hundreds of years!.. And we say: If a Muslim scholar had preceded Darwin in the theory he brought, that would only indicate that that scholar preceded him in the foolishness and falsehood from which we seek refuge in God. Indeed, among the worst types of injustice is to strip sound speech of its meaning and then attach falsehood to it, in support of the whisperings of the falsehood-mongers, and persistence in imitating them and following them wherever they go.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Darwinian evolution and a clarification of the Islamic concept of the cosmic hierarchy. The author begins by explaining the meaning of 'connection' in the components of creation: the last horizon of each level is uniquely prepared to become the first of the next level, leading to the expansion of the animal world and culminating in man. He then quotes Ibn Miskawayh, who describes the interconnectedness of all existing things as a single string of beads arranged by divine wisdom through the agency of the One Truth. The author notes that Ibn Miskawayh elaborates this gradation in the manner clarified by Ibn Khaldun. Next, the author asserts that this is an observed descriptive reality, witnessed since ancient times by all scholars and rational observers, and it has absolutely nothing to do with Darwinian assumptions about evolution from one species to another. He declares the Darwinian hypothesis to be false and baseless. He then criticizes certain contemporary Muslims who, fascinated by Western ideas, seek support for every Western theory in Islamic sources. Upon discovering the concept of gradation in Muslim scholars like Ibn Khaldun and Ibn Miskawayh, they mistakenly claim this as a precursor to Darwinism, boasting that Muslims anticipated Darwin by centuries. The author forcefully rejects this, arguing that if a Muslim scholar had actually preceded Darwin, it would only indicate that he preceded him in foolishness and falsehood, from which we seek refuge in God. He concludes by denouncing the injustice of distorting sound speech from its meaning and attaching falsehood to it in order to support the whisperings of the falsehood-mongers and to persist in imitating them.

Key Terms
تدرج التكوين
اتصال الموجودات
الحكمة السارية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Miskawayh's analogy, what does the connection of existents resemble?
A) A growing tree
B) A single thread stringing many beads
C) A ladder with steps
D) A river flowing to the sea

Key Takeaway
The Islamic view of creation is a divinely ordered, interconnected hierarchy, not a random evolution.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says that the last of each horizon is ‘prepared with a strange readiness’ to become the first of the next. Look at your own life: what ‘last horizon’ are you in right now, and are you consciously preparing to transition to the next level that Allah has ordained for you? What specific step can you take today to fulfil that readiness?
?
Ibn Miskawayh describes creation as a ‘single thread that strings many beads in a correct arrangement.’ If your life is one bead on that thread, how does your daily actions either align with or disrupt the divine arrangement? Examine one habit that you know is out of place — what will you do to restore the correct order?
?
The author states that this reality is ‘observed’ and that ‘all rational observers see it and marvel at it.’ When was the last time you truly marvelled at the order in Allah's creation — not as an intellectual concept, but with your heart? Commit to a time this week to sit in reflection on one aspect of the natural world and let it move you to awe and gratitude.

Darwinism: A False Hypothesis Misattributed to Islamic Sources
Buti refutes Darwinism and criticizes those who claim Islamic sources support it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti rejects Darwinian evolution and how he criticizes those who seek Islamic support for it.

Core Idea
Darwinian evolution is incompatible with Islam's observed hierarchy of creation.

Having presented the Islamic view of the cosmic hierarchy, Buti now confronts Darwinian evolution head-on. He argues that the gradation he described has nothing to do with evolution from one species to another. He then sharply critiques contemporary Muslims who, dazzled by Western theories, wrongly claim that Muslim scholars like Ibn Khaldun anticipated Darwin. This lesson highlights the danger of misinterpreting classical Islamic texts to fit modern theories.

Guided Path
1
Identify Buti's refutation of Darwinism
He states the observed hierarchy has no relation to Darwinian evolution and calls it a false hypothesis with no basis.
2
Examine the critique of Muslim apologists
Buti criticizes those who seek confirmation of Western theories in Islamic sources. They mistakenly see the gradation as support for evolution.
He calls this a 'oddity' (من الطرائف).
3
Understand the strong rejection
Buti says that if a Muslim scholar had actually preceded Darwin, it would only mean he preceded him in foolishness and falsehood.
This is a powerful rhetorical move.
4
Reflect on the broader lesson
The passage concludes with a warning against distorting the meaning of sound speech to support falsehood.
This is an ethical principle for engaging with Islamic texts.

?

?

?

As you read the Qur'an and Sunnah, will you resolve to preserve their intended meanings, even when it costs you popularity or approval? What one step will you take today to avoid this injustice?

The Foolishness of Denying the Jinn
Buti criticizes those who deny jinn due to lack of sensory experience, tracing it to blind imitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying the existence of jinn based solely on lack of personal sensory experience is irrational and rooted in blind imitation.

Core Idea
Denying jinn because you haven't seen them is ignorance, not science.

Buti begins by targeting a common modern attitude: a person who claims to be a Muslim yet argues against the Quranic teaching on jinn using the flimsy excuse that he has never seen them. He traces this denial to blind imitation of Western critics who label belief in jinn as superstition. This lesson unpacks that critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening critique
Read the first few lines where Buti identifies the astonishing foolishness. Notice the accusation that the denier's only argument is ignorance.
2
Understand the root: blind imitation
Buti explains that this denial is not based on evidence but on mimicking the claims of 'intellectual invaders'. The critics simply repeat what they heard without critical thought.
3
Spot the contradiction
Buti then shows that the same people later blindly believe in spirit summoning when their masters shift topics. This reveals their lack of intellectual independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير أن السخف العجيب إنما يكمن عند من يزعم أنه مسلم يؤمن بالله ورسوله وكتابه، ثم يمضي يجادلك، أو يجادل القرآن بتعبير أصح، في وجود الجن مثلاً. ولا دليل يخاصمك به إلا أنه لم ير الجن ولم يحس بهم، أي لا دليل له يخاصمك به إلا مجرد جهله كما قلنا. والمسألة في جذورها، مجرد تقليد ومحاكاة، لمحترفي الغزو الفكري ضد الإسلام وأهله. فقد ألقوا الآذان إليهم، فسمعوهم يقولون: إن الاعتقاد بالجن والشياطين والملائكة، إنما هو من (الإحيائية) والخرافات التي كانت سائدة عند العرب، فدعا إليها بعد ذلك محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام باسم الدين والإسلام ..! فأحنوا رؤوسهم لما سمعوا وأغمضوا العين والعقل عن التفكر في دليل هذه الدعوى وبواعثها وبراهينها العلمية، ثم انطلقوا يرددون هذا الكلام، دون أن يختلف أي اختلاف عن صوت سادتهم !.. ثم لما عاد أولئك السادة أنفسهم يتحدثون عن الأرواح وقصة تحضيرها وكيفية مناجاتها، عاد هؤلاء مرة أخرى يستمعون، وعادوا مرة أخرى ينغضون رؤوسهم مؤمنين معتقدين، دون أن يكشفوا غطاء العقل لأي تأمل أو برهان علمي. ثم انطلقوا هذه المرة يعتقدون بالأرواح، ويعلمون الناس السبيل إلى تحضيرها ومكالمتها واستكشاف خفايا الماضي السحيق والمستقبل البعيد بواسطتها (١). (١) لا بد أنك تتساءل عن موقف العقيدة الإسلامية من قصة تحضير الأرواح، وما شاع من نبأ ذلك في أوربا ثم في جهات كثيرة من العالم العربي. والجواب، أن العالم ممتلئ بالأرواح المختلفة، بدون شك، ولكن الإسلام علمنا أن لا نصدق أحداً في تحضير روح أو مكالمتها إلا إذا ثبت ذلك ببرهان التجربة المشاهدة، إذ التحضير والمكالمة من الأمور الخاضعة للحس، فلا يمكن أن يكون دليلها أيضاً إلا الحس وقد مضى بيان ذلك في تمهيد هذا الكتاب. فإن ثبت أمامك ببرهان التجربة والمشاهدة على ذلك، فلا مانع من تصديقه، لا مناص من تصديقه، ولكن الذي لا يزال مجهولاً بعد ذلك، هو ماهية هذه الروح ... ولا يكفي لرفع الجهل أن تنطق الروح أو تكتب أو تزعم بواسطة ما، أنها روح فلان من الناس، = تلك المظهر !.. هي السخافة التي لا يمكن أن تتمثل في أحط ولا أشنع من هذا. يتبجح لك أحدهم منكراً، باسم العلم ودليل العلم، عندما تضعه أمام البرهان العلمي طبق منهجه الفكري الدقيق. ثم تراه يتضاءل ذلاً ويلوي رأسه في انصياع منكسر وإيمان أعمى، عندما تضعه أمام دعاوى فارغة لبعض مفكري الغرب أو مستشرقيهم. فأي علم هذا الذي يتقلقل في دماغه ويتبجح به، وهو لم يكسبه بعد حتى الشخصية الاستقلالية التي تجعله قادراً على أن يفكر بعقله ؟ رحم الله ذلك العربي الذي عرف مكمن الداء في هذا وأمثاله، يوم أن قال: أنت في الماء، ورأس في السماء !.. (١) فهذا الخبر يحتمل الصدق والكذب. ولا دليل على صدقه، وكما أن في الناس أشراراً دأبهم الكذب والتلاعب بعقول الناس، فإن في الجن أيضاً كذلك. فمن أين لك أن الذي يناجيك أو يكتب لك جواب أسئلتك من قاع السلة، ليس شيطاناً مريداً جاء ليلبس عليك دينك ويلهو بمخادعتك ويلتذ بالكذب عليك ؟ أولم تقرأ أن أكثر أسباب الحماقة في المنحرفين أو المجانين الذين ادعوا أنهم أنبياء أو عظماء إنما هو هواجس من هؤلاء الشياطين، إذ هتفوا في أعماق أفئدتهم أو على طبلة آذانهم أنهم أحباء الله وعظماؤه .. وأن الله قد أكرمهم باسقاط تكاليفه عنهم. فربا الغرور في أوداجهم وثقلت رؤوسهم الفارغة بالخديعة وراحت تهتز منهم الأعطاف .. وأيقنوا أنهم وزراء الله المدللون في الأرض بينه وبينهم نسب الأرواح الطاهرة التي تناجيهم، مع أنها ليست إلا أرواحاً حقيرة من أرواح مردة الشياطين التي تحط عادة فوق قمامات العقول والأفكار تتلهى بإغوائها واللعب بها. فالأرواح لاشك في وجودها، ولكنها لا ينبغي أن تكون صادقة، إذا قالت لك إحداها أنها روح أحد الأنبياء، ثم راحت تقدم لك المبادئ والعظات بناء على أنها كذلك. إنها بدون ريب روح شريرة تلهو بمخادعتك !.. (١) هو مثل عربي يضرب لمن يتبجح بما ليس أهلاً له.
However, the astonishing foolishness lies only with one who claims to be a Muslim believing in God, His Messenger, and His Book, then proceeds to argue with you, or argue with the Qur'an to be more accurate, about the existence of jinn, for example. And he has no argument to dispute with you except that he has not seen the jinn nor perceived them, i.e., he has no argument to dispute with you except mere ignorance as we said. And the matter in its roots is mere imitation and mimicry of the professionals of intellectual invasion against Islam and its people. For they lent their ears to them, and heard them saying: 'Belief in jinn, devils, and angels is nothing but (animism) and superstitions that were prevalent among the Arabs, then Muhammad, peace be upon him, called to them afterward in the name of religion and Islam!' So they bowed their heads when they heard and closed their eyes and minds from reflecting on the evidence of this claim, its motives, and its scientific proofs, then they began repeating this speech, without differing in any way from the voice of their masters!.. Then when those same masters themselves began to talk about spirits and the story of summoning them and how to communicate with them, these people again listened, and again they nodded their heads believing and convinced, without uncovering the veil of the mind for any reflection or scientific proof. Then this time they began to believe in spirits, and teach people the way to summon them, speak to them, and uncover the secrets of the distant past and the far future through them (1). (1) You must be wondering about the stance of the Islamic creed on the story of spirit summoning, and what has become widespread of that news in Europe and then in many parts of the Arab world. The answer is that the world is full of various spirits, without doubt, but Islam taught us not to believe anyone in summoning a spirit or speaking to it unless that is established by the proof of witnessed experience, for summoning and communication are matters subject to the senses, so their evidence can only be the senses, and the explanation of that has already passed in the introduction of this book. If it is established before you by the proof of experience and witnessing, then there is no objection to believing it, there is no escape from believing it, but what remains unknown after that is the essence of this spirit... and it is not sufficient to remove ignorance that the spirit speaks or writes or claims, by some means, that it is the spirit of so-and-so, = that appearance!.. It is the foolishness that cannot be represented in anything lower or uglier than this. Someone denies arrogantly to you, in the name of science and the evidence of science, when you put before him the scientific proof according to his precise intellectual method. Then you see him becoming humbled and bowing his head in submissive compliance and blind faith, when you put before him empty claims of some Western thinkers or orientalists. So what kind of science is this that wobbles in his brain and he boasts with it, while it has not yet given him even an independent personality that enables him to think with his own mind? May God have mercy on that Arab who knew the location of the disease in this and its likes, the day he said: 'You are in the water, and your head is in the sky!'.. (1) So this report is subject to truth and falsehood. And there is no evidence for its truth, and just as among people there are evil ones whose habit is lying and manipulating people's minds, so among the jinn there are also such. So how do you know that the one who communicates with you or writes you the answer to your questions from the bottom of the basket is not an obstinate devil who came to confuse your religion for you, entertain himself by deceiving you, and delight in lying to you? Have you not read that most of the causes of foolishness in deviants or madmen who claimed to be prophets or great men are only whispers from these devils, when they shouted in the depths of their hearts or on the eardrums of their ears that they are beloved of God and His great ones.. and that God has honored them by removing His obligations from them. So arrogance grew in their veins and their empty heads became heavy with deception and their shoulders began to sway.. and they became convinced that they are God's pampered ministers on earth, between Him and them a kinship of pure spirits that communicate with them, while they are nothing but contemptible spirits from the spirits of rebellious devils that usually settle on the garbage dumps of minds and thoughts, amusing themselves by seducing them and playing with them. So spirits, there is no doubt about their existence, but they should not be truthful, if one of them tells you that it is the spirit of one of the prophets, and then proceeds to offer you principles and sermons on the basis that it is so. It is without doubt an evil spirit amusing itself by deceiving you!.. (1) It is an Arab proverb struck for one who boasts of what he is not worthy of.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a critique of two contradictory intellectual attitudes and an explanation of the Islamic stance on spirit summoning. Buti begins by identifying the 'astonishing foolishness' of someone who claims to be a Muslim yet argues against the existence of jinn, using the sole argument that he has not seen or sensed them. Buti labels this as mere ignorance. He then traces the root of this attitude to blind imitation of 'professional intellectual invaders' who dismiss belief in jinn, angels, and devils as animism and superstition, and attribute them to Muhammad (peace be upon him). The critics accept this without examining evidence. Buti then points out a contradiction: the same masters later speak about spirits and their summoning, and the same followers blindly believe in that too, again without critical thought. This shows their lack of intellectual independence. Buti then addresses the Islamic position on spirit summoning in a footnote: the world is full of spirits, but Islam requires empirical proof for any claim of summoning or communication, as it is a sensory matter. If proven by witnessed experience, it must be accepted, but the essence of the spirit remains unknown. Buti then returns to the main critique, calling the behavior 'foolishness': someone who denies scientific proofs when presented correctly but meekly accepts empty claims from Western thinkers. He quotes a proverb about being in water but head in the sky, indicating self-contradiction. Finally, Buti warns that reports of spirit communication are subject to truth and falsehood; there is no guarantee that the spirit is not a devil deceiving the person. He gives examples of deviants who were misled by whispers from devils into thinking they were prophets or beloved of God. Thus, while spirits exist, one should not trust claims of communication from them, especially if they claim to be prophets. The passage overall argues for intellectual consistency and reliance on empirical evidence for sensory claims, while affirming the unseen realities (jinn, angels) as taught by revelation.

Key Terms
الجن
الإحيائية
الغزو الفكري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that denying jinn based on lack of personal observation is a rational or scientific stance.
Correction: Buti shows that it is actually mere ignorance and blind imitation, not science, because it dismisses revelation and ignores the possibility of unseen realities.

Checkpoint
What is the primary flaw Buti identifies in those who deny the existence of jinn?
A) They rely on scientific evidence.
B) They argue based on lack of personal sensory experience.
C) They follow the teachings of the Quran.
D) They believe in spirit summoning.

Key Takeaway
Denying the jinn due to lack of sensory experience is not rational but a blind imitation of critics of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a claim about Islam from a respected scholar without verifying it from the Qur'an and Sunnah, simply because you trusted the source? How is that different from the blind imitation Buti criticizes?
?
Think of a time you felt embarrassed to affirm a belief of Islam (like the existence of jinn) because it seemed unscientific to others. Did your hesitation come from a lack of evidence or from a fear of being seen as irrational?
?
If you were to adopt the same standard of evidence for Islamic teachings as you do for modern secular claims, which beliefs would you have to reject? Would that be consistent with being a Muslim?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
Islamic Stance on Spirit Summoning and Warning Against Deception
Buti explains Islamic stance on spirit summoning and warns of deception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic position on spirit summoning: spirits exist, but claims of communication require sensory evidence, and one must beware of deception by devils.

Core Idea
Spirits exist, but don't trust every spirit that speaks.

In this passage, Buti addresses the widespread curiosity about spirit summoning. He affirms the existence of spirits but clarifies that Islam requires empirical proof for any claim of communication. He then warns that such communications are often deceptive, with devils masquerading as righteous spirits. This lesson explains that position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Islamic stance on spirits and proof
Buti states that the world is full of spirits, but we must not believe claims of summoning without sensory evidence.
2
Understand the requirement of empirical proof
Since summoning is a sensory matter, its proof must be sensory. If proven, we must accept it, but the essence remains unknown.
3
Consider the possibility of deception
Buti warns that just as there are liars among humans, there are devils among jinn. A claim to be a prophet's spirit could be a devil's trick.
4
Reflect on the final critique
Buti ends with a proverb about intellectual inconsistency, tying back to the main theme of blind imitation.

However, the astonishing foolishness lies only with one who claims to be a Muslim believing in God, His Messenger, and His Book, then proceeds to argue with you, or argue with the Qur'an to be more accurate, about the existence of jinn, for example. Commentary
This passage is a critique of two contradictory intellectual attitudes and an explanation of the Islamic stance on spirit summoning. Buti begins by identifying the 'astonishing foolishness' of someone who claims to be a Muslim yet argues against the existence of jinn, using the sole argument that he has not seen or sensed them. Buti labels this as mere ignorance. He then traces the root of this attitude to blind imitation of 'professional intellectual invaders' who dismiss belief in jinn, angels, and devils as animism and superstition, and attribute them to Muhammad (peace be upon him). The critics accept this without examining evidence. Buti then points out a contradiction: the same masters later speak about spirits and their summoning, and the same followers blindly believe in that too, again without critical thought. This shows their lack of intellectual independence. Buti then addresses the Islamic position on spirit summoning in a footnote: the world is full of spirits, but Islam requires empirical proof for any claim of summoning or communication, as it is a sensory matter. If proven by witnessed experience, it must be accepted, but the essence of the spirit remains unknown. Buti then returns to the main critique, calling the behavior 'foolishness': someone who denies scientific proofs when presented correctly but meekly accepts empty claims from Western thinkers. He quotes a proverb about being in water but head in the sky, indicating self-contradiction. Finally, Buti warns that reports of spirit communication are subject to truth and falsehood; there is no guarantee that the spirit is not a devil deceiving the person. He gives examples of deviants who were misled by whispers from devils into thinking they were prophets or beloved of God. Thus, while spirits exist, one should not trust claims of communication from them, especially if they claim to be prophets. The passage overall argues for intellectual consistency and reliance on empirical evidence for sensory claims, while affirming the unseen realities (jinn, angels) as taught by revelation.

Key Terms

التجربة المشاهدة
الشياطين
الأرواح

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that any spirit communication is trustworthy and should be accepted without question.
Correction: Buti explains that just as there are liars among humans, there are devils among jinn. Spirit communications can be deceptive, and one must require empirical proof and be cautious.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is required before believing a claim of spirit summoning?

The Argument from Harmony and Causality for a Single Creator
Buti argues that harmony and causality in the universe prove a single First Cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti uses the observed harmony in the universe and the principle of causality to prove the existence of a single Creator, and why this argument leads to the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
Harmony in the universe compels the mind to infer a single First Cause.

In this passage, Buti responds to an objection by presenting the most powerful evidence for the existence of God: the harmony and causality pervasive in the universe. He argues that the very fact that things are arranged in interdependent order forces the intellect to ascend from many causes to a single ultimate cause. This lesson walks through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the role of harmony
Buti begins by stating that the most prominent evidence for the Creator is the harmony and consistency (al-tanāsuq wa al-insijām) in the universe. This is not just complexity but a specific type of order.
He contrasts this with other possible evidences.
2
See causality as the core of harmony
Harmony is defined as the phenomenon of causality and causation (sababiyya wa 'illiyya) that runs through all parts of the universe. Without causality, there would be no harmony.
Causality means things are in need of each other.
3
Trace the causal chain backwards
As you examine the interconnected causes, you notice that the number of distinct causes decreases the deeper you go. Eventually, you reach a single great cause behind everything – the Necessary Being.
This is a logical deduction, not a leap of faith.
4
Apply the analogy of the watch
Buti uses an analogy: scattered machine parts cannot be attributed to one maker unless they fit together harmoniously. Similarly, the universe's harmony points to one Creator.
The more you see harmony, the more certain you become of the unity of the maker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب : إن أبرز مظاهر دلالة هذا الكون على وجود الخالق عز وجل ، إنما هو مظهر التناسق والانسجام فيه ، كما أوضحنا ذلك من قبل . وليس معنى التناسق والانسجام فيه شيئاً غير ظاهرة السببية والعلية الشائعة والسارية في كل صوره وأجزائه : إذن فلكي يدلَّ الكون دلالة باهرة على وجود الله عز وجل ينبغي أن يكون متناسقاً ولكي يتم فيه التناسق ، ينبغي أن يكون مرتباً بعضه على بعض بأن يكون هذا محتاجاً وذاك محتاجاً إليه فيتلاقيان طبقاً للحاجة التي بينهما . فإذا تجلى لك من الكون هذا التناسق ، تنبهت لما قلناه من ضرورة تناقص العلل في المسائل المتناسقة كلما أمعنت النظر أكثر ، وكلما سبرت مزيداً من أغوار هذه العلل والمعلولات ؛ فتسير متأملاً في هذا السبيل ، إلى أن تنتهي بك هذه العلل الكثيرة المختلفة إلى العلة الوحيدة الكبرى الكامنة خلف كلّ ما قد رأيت ، أي إلى واجب الوجود وهو الله عز وجل . إنَّ الذي يتأمل أجهزة وآلات معينة ومنتشرة ، لا يمكن أن يصدق أنها جميعاً من صنع شخص واحد هو الموجد لها ، إلا إذا تأمل فرآها متممة بعضها لبعض ، متعاونة لدى التركيب في إيجاد عمل نوعي معين ، وكلما ازداد لمساً لهذا الانسجام وسبر مزيداً من دقائقه ، ازداد يقيناً بوحدة الصانع وذلك كأن يعمد فيركبها إلى بعضها تركيبها الصحيح المتصور وإذا هي قد انقلبت في يده سـاعـة تضبط الزمن ، وإذا هي من صنع معمل معين معروف وهكذا اقتضت رحمة الله بعباده أن يجعل من كـونـه أفصح بيـان نـاطـق بألوهية الله وحده وبأنه الخالق والمبدع للكون كله ، فجعلك في حاجة مستمرة إلى كثير من الأمور المعينة ، ثم جعل بينك وبين هذه الأمور حلقات من الوسائط والأسباب ، كلما تجاوزت واحدة منها إلى الأخرى تبدى لـك جـديـد من معنى الانسجام بين أجزاء الكون وجزئياته ووقفت على ما بينها من تعاون ومشاركة في سبيل تحقيق أغراضك وحاجاتك ، حتى تستيقن أخيراً بأن من وراء هذا الكون كله من يدبره هذا التدبير ويؤلف بينه هذا التأليف ولو أن الله خلقك غير محتاج إلى شيء وخلق المكونات الأخرى كذلك - وهو قادر أن يفعل ذلك - ، لما وُجدت أمامك أي فرصة لاكتشاف معنى التناسق والتلاؤم فيها ، ولفقدت بذلك أبرز مظهر من مظاهر الدلالة على وجود الله تعالى في الكون
The answer: The most prominent manifestation of this universe's indication of the existence of the Creator, may He be glorified and exalted, is the manifestation of harmony and consistency in it, as we have clarified before. And the meaning of harmony and consistency in it is nothing other than the phenomenon of causality and causation prevalent and current in all its forms and parts. Therefore, for the universe to indicate with dazzling indication the existence of God, may He be glorified and exalted, it must be harmonious. And for harmony to be achieved in it, it must be arranged, some parts upon others, such that this is in need and that is in need of it, so they meet according to the need between them. So if this harmony manifests to you from the universe, you become aware of what we said about the necessity of the decrease of causes in harmonious matters the more you examine, and the more you delve into the depths of these causes and effects; so you proceed reflecting in this path, until these many different causes lead you to the single great cause hidden behind all that you have seen, that is, the Necessary Being, who is God, may He be glorified and exalted. Indeed, one who contemplates specific and scattered devices and machines cannot believe that they are all the work of a single person who is their maker, unless he contemplates and sees them completing each other, cooperating in assembly to produce a specific type of work, and the more he touches this harmony and delves into its details, the more his certainty increases in the unity of the maker. This is like one who sets out to assemble them correctly as imagined, and then they become in his hand a clock that measures time, and they are from a well-known specific factory. Thus God's mercy to His servants necessitated that He make from His universe the most eloquent clear statement expressing the divinity of God alone and that He is the Creator and Originator of the whole universe. So He placed you in constant need of many specific things, then He placed between you and these things links of means and causes. Whenever you pass from one to another, a new aspect of the meaning of harmony between the parts and particulars of the universe appears to you, and you come upon the cooperation and participation among them in achieving your purposes and needs, until you finally become certain that behind this whole universe there is One who manages it with this management and composes it with this composition. And if God had created you in need of nothing and created the other components similarly – and He is able to do that – then you would have no opportunity to discover the meaning of harmony and congruity in them, and thereby you would lose the most prominent manifestation of the indications of the existence of God, may He be exalted, in the universe.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection and presents the argument from harmony and causality for the existence of a single Creator. The author begins by stating that the most prominent evidence for the Creator is the harmony and consistency in the universe. He clarifies that harmony is nothing other than the phenomenon of causality and causation pervading all aspects of the universe. For the universe to be a clear sign of God, it must be harmonious, and harmony requires order and interdependence: some things are in need of others, and they meet according to their needs. By observing this harmony, one realizes that as one examines deeper, the number of causes decreases, leading ultimately to a single great cause behind everything, which is the Necessary Being (God). The author then provides an analogy: a person who looks at scattered machines cannot believe they come from one maker unless they see them fitting together to produce a specific function, like a watch; the more one sees the harmony, the more certain one becomes of the unity of the maker. Similarly, God's mercy made the universe a clear statement of His divinity, placing humans in constant need of many things and establishing links of means and causes. As humans traverse these links, they discover more harmony and cooperation, culminating in certainty of a single manager behind the entire universe. Finally, the author notes that if God had not created humans in need, they would have no opportunity to discover this harmony, and thus would lose the strongest evidence for His existence. The argument follows a logical progression: from observed harmony to necessary causality, then from multiplicity of causes to a single first cause.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument assumes the principle of causality without evidence.
Correction: Buti does not assume causality; he deduces it from the observed harmony in the universe. The harmony itself implies interdependence and causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage says if you had no needs, you would lose the strongest evidence for God. Are you grateful for your neediness, or do you resent it? Write down one thing you desperately need and thank Allah for making it a means to know Him.

Need as a Window to Divine Harmony
Buti shows how human neediness enables the discovery of cosmic harmony, proving God's existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how human neediness serves as a pathway to discovering cosmic harmony and recognizing God's existence.

Core Idea
Need is not a defect — it is the key that unlocks the harmony of the universe pointing to God.

In this passage, the renowned scholar Ramadan al-Buti presents a profound argument: our very needs are divinely designed tools that lead us to recognize the intricate harmony of creation. By tracing the chain of causes and effects that fulfill our needs, we uncover a cosmic cooperation that points unmistakably to a wise Creator. Without need, this sign would be hidden from us.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two parts: the positive discovery through need, and the counterfactual scenario.
Pay attention to the conditional 'if' at the end.
2
Identify the chain of intermediaries
Buti mentions 'links of intermediaries and causes' (حلقات من الوسائط والأسباب). Trace how moving through these reveals harmony.
3
Understand the counterfactual argument
The author imagines a world without need and concludes that the most prominent sign of God would be lost. Reflect on why need is essential for this discovery.
This shows the wisdom behind human dependency.
4
Connect to your own experience
Think of a personal need you have and how its fulfillment through a chain of causes points to a greater order.
This makes the argument concrete.

كثير من الأمور المعينة ، ثم جعل بينك وبين هذه الأمور حلقات من الوسائط والأسباب ، كلما تجاوزت واحدة منها إلى الأخرى تبدى لـك جـديـد من معنى الانسجام بين أجزاء الكون وجزئياته ووقفت على ما بينها من تعاون ومشاركة في سبيل تحقيق أغراضك وحاجاتك ، حتى تستيقن أخيراً بأن من وراء هذا الكون كله من يدبره هذا التدبير ويؤلف بينه هذا التأليف ولو أن الله خلقك غير محتاج إلى شيء وخلق المكونات الأخرى كذلك - وهو قادر أن يفعل ذلك - ، لما وُجدت أمامك أي فرصة لاكتشاف معنى التناسق والتلاؤم فيها ، ولفقدت بذلك أبرز مظهر من مظاهر الدلالة على وجود الله تعالى في الكون

Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents a proof of God's existence based on the experience of need and the discovery of harmony. It begins by noting that God has placed between a person and various matters a chain of intermediaries and causes. By traversing these links, one observes increasing harmony and cooperation among parts of the universe, all directed toward fulfilling one's needs. This leads to certainty in a wise Designer. The author then uses a counterfactual: if God had created you without any need (which He could), you would miss the chance to discover this harmony, thus losing the clearest sign of God's existence. Therefore, neediness itself is a vehicle for recognizing divine design.

The True Source of All Effect: Allah Alone
Buti establishes the belief that only Allah has true effect and critiques scientific causation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Buti, only Allah has true effect in the universe, and that all apparent causes are merely created by Him.

Core Idea
Only Allah truly affects; everything else is merely a created cause.

In this passage, Buti lays out the fundamental belief that a Muslim must hold regarding causation: no thing has any real effect except Allah. He then addresses the role of science, explaining that it only describes correlations, not necessary connections. This sets the stage for understanding divine power and the nature of causality in Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Buti uses a very direct and emphatic style.
2
Identify the core claim
Find the statement that 'no thing has any effect in the universe except Allah'. This is the central belief.
The phrase 'عقيدة جازمة' indicates it must be held firmly.
3
Understand the nature of causes
Buti says all apparent causes are 'أسباب جعلية' – created causes. This means they have no independent power. Reflect on what this implies for everyday causality.
4
Analyze the critique of science
Buti argues that science only describes phenomena and finds correlations through repeated experiments; it does not prove necessary connection. Ask yourself why this distinction matters for theology.
The word 'مقارنة' (correlation) is key.
5
Reflect on the implication for tawhid
Consider how this belief preserves Allah's sole agency and prevents attributing independent power to creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
د - ما يجب على المسلم اعتقاده بناء على ذلك

إن على المسلم أن يعتقد عقيدة جازمة أن لا تأثير في الكون لأي شيء إلا الله عز وجل ، وأن كل ما يتراءى لنا من مظاهر الأسباب والعلل إنما هو أسباب وعلل جعلية ، جعلها الله عز وجل كذلك ، وأن ما قد يجده الباحث فيها مما يسميه العلم بالعوامل والمؤثرات وما إلى ذلك، إنما هو كذلك من حيث الظاهر فقط . والعلم لا شأن له بالأشياء إلا أنه يصفها على ما هي عليه في أدق مظاهرها ، ثم يمارس هذا الوصف بالتجربة في مجالات متكررة . وإذا كان العلم إنما يصف واقعاً لا يزيد عليه ، فإن هذا الواقع لا يزيد على المقارنة المستمرة أما إمكان الانفصال فشيء آخر . وهيهات أن يتوصل العلم إلى أن مقارنة الأسباب بمسبباتها أمر حتمي لا مناص من تلازمها ولا حيلة لانفكاكها

وإذ قد ثبت الدليل القطعي على ما قلناه ، فقد كان جحود ذلك كفراً بإجماع المسلمين . ولا معنى لإثبات ألوهية الله بعد هذا الجحود كما هو معلوم ، كما ذلك للإيمان بشيء من المعجزات والخوارق التي أكرم الله بها الأنبياء والمرسلين ، كتحول نار إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى برد وسلام ، وكـولادة عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بدون وساطة أب ، وكإبرائه الأكمه والأبرص وإحيائه الموتى . وكل ذلك مما نص القرآن عليه بصريح العبارة وجلي البيان وجماع كل هذا الذي ذكرناه ، قوله تعالى : إِنَّمَا أَمْرُهُ إِذَا أَرَادَ شَيْئاً أَنْ يَقُولَ لَهُ كُنْ فَيَكُونُ
D - What the Muslim must believe based on that.

Indeed, the Muslim must hold a firm belief that no thing has any effect in the universe except Allah, mighty and majestic, and that all that appears to us of the forms of causes and effects are only made-by-creation causes, which Allah, mighty and majestic, made so, and that what the researcher may find in them that is called by science 'factors and influences' and so on, is only so from the outward perspective. And science has no concern with things except that it describes them as they are in their most precise forms, then it practices this description through experimentation in repeated fields. And if science only describes a reality and does not add to it, then this reality is nothing but continuous correlation. As for the possibility of separation, it is something else. And how far is it from science to reach that the correlation of causes with their effects is necessary, with no escape from their inseparability and no way to break them apart.

And when the decisive proof has been established for what we have said, then denying that is disbelief by consensus of the Muslims. And there is no meaning to establishing the divinity of Allah after this denial, as is known, and likewise for believing in any of the miracles and marvels with which Allah honored the prophets and messengers, such as the transformation of the fire of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) into coolness and safety, and the birth of Isa (peace be upon him) without a father's mediation, and his curing of the blind and the leper, and his reviving the dead. And all of that is what the Quran has clearly and unambiguously stated. And the sum of all this we have mentioned is the saying of the Most High: 'His command, when He wills a thing, is only to say to it "Be," and it is.'
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal summary of what a Muslim must believe regarding causation and divine power. The author starts with a clear statement that the Muslim must have a firm belief that no thing has any real effect in the universe except Allah. All apparent causes and effects are merely created by Allah; they are not independent agents. Science, the author argues, only describes phenomena and establishes correlations through repeated experiments, but it cannot prove necessary connection. The possibility of separation remains. After establishing the decisive proof, the author declares that denying this is considered disbelief by the consensus of Muslims, because it nullifies the concept of God and undermines belief in miracles, which are necessary for prophethood. He gives examples of miracles from the Quran: the fire of Ibrahim becoming cool and safe, the birth of Isa without a father, and Isa's healings and reviving the dead. All these are clearly mentioned in the Quran. The overall point is summarized by the verse: 'His command, when He wills a thing, is only to say to it "Be," and it is.' This verse encapsulates the absolute power of Allah's will and the created nature of all things.

Key Terms
تأثير
أسباب جعلية
مقارنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many people think that science proves that causes necessarily produce their effects.
Correction: Buti clarifies that science only describes correlations, not necessary connections. The regularities we observe are due to Allah's custom, not intrinsic necessity.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what does science actually do when it studies causes and effects?
A) It discovers the necessary connection between them.
B) It describes phenomena and establishes correlations.
C) It proves that causes are independent.
D) It eliminates the need for God.

Key Takeaway
Buti argues that all apparent causes are merely created by Allah and that science only finds correlation, not necessary causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a natural event like rain or healing, do you genuinely attribute it to Allah as the true cause, or do your thoughts stop at the physical cause? What would change in your daily gratitude if you truly internalized that Allah is the only effecter?
?
If you believe that only Allah has true effect, why do you still feel anxiety about secondary causes? What does your fear of germs, accidents, or people's opinions reveal about your conviction?
?
Buti says science only describes correlations, not necessity. How does this affect your trust in scientific predictions or your reliance on material means? Are you willing to live as if Allah alone is the cause, even when the apparent causes seem inevitable?

The Consequence of Denying Divine Causation: Kufr and Miracles
Buti declares that denying exclusive divine causation is kufr and connects it to belief in miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying that only Allah has true effect is considered disbelief (kufr) and how this belief is necessary for accepting miracles.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's exclusive power over causation leads to kufr and undermines belief in miracles.

Having established that only Allah has true effect, Buti now draws the implications: rejecting this belief is not a minor error but outright disbelief. He explains that it nullifies the very concept of God and makes belief in miracles impossible, which are essential for prophethood. He then lists examples of miracles from the Quran, concluding with the verse that encapsulates Allah's absolute power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the strong language: 'جحود ذلك كفراً'.
2
Understand the claim that denial is kufr
Buti says that after the decisive proof, denying this belief is kufr by consensus. Why would it be so serious?
The word 'جحود' implies willful denial.
3
See why it nullifies tawhid and miracles
Buti explains that if one denies Allah's exclusive power, then affirming His divinity is meaningless, and belief in miracles—which are exceptions to normal patterns—becomes impossible.
4
Examine the miracle examples
Buti lists three miracles: the fire of Ibrahim, the birth of Isa, and Isa's healings and reviving the dead. How do these illustrate Allah's power over causation?
These are all clear in the Quran.
5
Reflect on the Quranic verse
The verse 'كن فيكون' summarizes the entire argument: Allah's will is sufficient for anything to happen. Consider how this verse supports the doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
د - ما يجب على المسلم اعتقاده بناء على ذلك

إن على المسلم أن يعتقد عقيدة جازمة أن لا تأثير في الكون لأي شيء إلا الله عز وجل ، وأن كل ما يتراءى لنا من مظاهر الأسباب والعلل إنما هو أسباب وعلل جعلية ، جعلها الله عز وجل كذلك ، وأن ما قد يجده الباحث فيها مما يسميه العلم بالعوامل والمؤثرات وما إلى ذلك، إنما هو كذلك من حيث الظاهر فقط . والعلم لا شأن له بالأشياء إلا أنه يصفها على ما هي عليه في أدق مظاهرها ، ثم يمارس هذا الوصف بالتجربة في مجالات متكررة . وإذا كان العلم إنما يصف واقعاً لا يزيد عليه ، فإن هذا الواقع لا يزيد على المقارنة المستمرة أما إمكان الانفصال فشيء آخر . وهيهات أن يتوصل العلم إلى أن مقارنة الأسباب بمسبباتها أمر حتمي لا مناص من تلازمها ولا حيلة لانفكاكها

وإذ قد ثبت الدليل القطعي على ما قلناه ، فقد كان جحود ذلك كفراً بإجماع المسلمين . ولا معنى لإثبات ألوهية الله بعد هذا الجحود كما هو معلوم ، كما ذلك للإيمان بشيء من المعجزات والخوارق التي أكرم الله بها الأنبياء والمرسلين ، كتحول نار إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى برد وسلام ، وكـولادة عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بدون وساطة أب ، وكإبرائه الأكمه والأبرص وإحيائه الموتى . وكل ذلك مما نص القرآن عليه بصريح العبارة وجلي البيان وجماع كل هذا الذي ذكرناه ، قوله تعالى : إِنَّمَا أَمْرُهُ إِذَا أَرَادَ شَيْئاً أَنْ يَقُولَ لَهُ كُنْ فَيَكُونُ
D - What the Muslim must believe based on that.

Indeed, the Muslim must hold a firm belief that no thing has any effect in the universe except Allah, mighty and majestic, and that all that appears to us of the forms of causes and effects are only made-by-creation causes, which Allah, mighty and majestic, made so, and that what the researcher may find in them that is called by science 'factors and influences' and so on, is only so from the outward perspective. And science has no concern with things except that it describes them as they are in their most precise forms, then it practices this description through experimentation in repeated fields. And if science only describes a reality and does not add to it, then this reality is nothing but continuous correlation. As for the possibility of separation, it is something else. And how far is it from science to reach that the correlation of causes with their effects is necessary, with no escape from their inseparability and no way to break them apart.

And when the decisive proof has been established for what we have said, then denying that is disbelief by consensus of the Muslims. And there is no meaning to establishing the divinity of Allah after this denial, as is known, and likewise for believing in any of the miracles and marvels with which Allah honored the prophets and messengers, such as the transformation of the fire of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) into coolness and safety, and the birth of Isa (peace be upon him) without a father's mediation, and his curing of the blind and the leper, and his reviving the dead. And all of that is what the Quran has clearly and unambiguously stated. And the sum of all this we have mentioned is the saying of the Most High: 'His command, when He wills a thing, is only to say to it "Be," and it is.'
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal summary of what a Muslim must believe regarding causation and divine power. The author starts with a clear statement that the Muslim must have a firm belief that no thing has any real effect in the universe except Allah. All apparent causes and effects are merely created by Allah; they are not independent agents. Science, the author argues, only describes phenomena and establishes correlations through repeated experiments, but it cannot prove necessary connection. The possibility of separation remains. After establishing the decisive proof, the author declares that denying this is considered disbelief by the consensus of Muslims, because it nullifies the concept of God and undermines belief in miracles, which are necessary for prophethood. He gives examples of miracles from the Quran: the fire of Ibrahim becoming cool and safe, the birth of Isa without a father, and Isa's healings and reviving the dead. All these are clearly mentioned in the Quran. The overall point is summarized by the verse: 'His command, when He wills a thing, is only to say to it "Be," and it is.' This verse encapsulates the absolute power of Allah's will and the created nature of all things.

معجزات

Denial of Miracles is Kufr
The author states that denial of miracles after definitive proof is kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying miracles after definitive proof is considered kufr by consensus, and how this relates to belief in Allah and His prophets.

Core Idea
Denial of miracles is kufr because miracles are inseparable from divine revelation.

Having established the definitive proof of Allah's existence and the truth of prophethood, Shaykh Buti now confronts a common error: thinking one can accept Allah's existence while rejecting the miracles of His prophets. He asserts that once the proof is clear, rejecting any part of it—especially the miracles attested in the Qur'an—amounts to disbelief. In this lesson, we will examine his argument, the specific miracles he cites, and the Quranic basis for this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice how the author moves from a general principle to specific examples and a Quranic seal.
The passage begins with 'wa idh qad thabata...' – pay attention to the logical connector.
2
Identify the logical flow
Break down the argument: premise (definitive proof established), conclusion (denial is kufr), support (consensus, meaninglessness of affirming divinity without miracles), evidence (Qur'anic miracles), and final summary verse.
3
Reflect on the list of miracles
The author mentions three miracles of Ibrahim and Isa. Consider why these are highlighted and how they demonstrate Allah's power beyond natural law.
Each is explicitly mentioned in the Qur'an.
4
Understand the role of consensus
The author invokes ijma' (consensus) of the Muslims. Why is this important? It shows that this ruling is not personal opinion but a settled matter in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذ قد ثبت الدليل القطعي على ما قلناه، فقد كان جحود ذلك كفراً بإجماع المسلمين. ولا معنى لإثبات ألوهية الله بعد هذا الجحود كما هو معلوم، كما لا معنى للإيمان بشيء من المعجزات والخوارق التي أكرم الله بها الأنبياء والمرسلين، كتحول نار إبراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام إلى برد وسلام، وكولادة عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بدون وساطة أب، وكإبرائه الأكمه والأبرص وإحيائه الموتى. وكل ذلك مما نص القرآن عليه بصريح العبارة وجلي البيان وجماع كل هذا الذي ذكرناه، قوله تعالى: {إنما أمره إذا أراد شيئاً أن يقول له كن فيكون}.
And since definitive proof has been established for what we have said, the denial of that is kufr by consensus of the Muslims. And there is no meaning to affirming the divinity of Allah after this denial, as is known, nor is there any meaning to believing in any of the miracles and extraordinary events with which Allah honored the prophets and messengers, such as the transformation of the fire of Ibrahim, peace be upon him, into coolness and safety, and the birth of Isa, peace be upon him, without the mediation of a father, and his healing of the blind and the leprous and his raising of the dead. And all of that is what the Qur'an textually states with clear wording and manifest exposition, and the summary of all this we have mentioned is His statement, the Exalted: {His command, when He wills a thing, is only to say to it 'Be' and it is}.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is an argument establishing that denial of miracles after accepting the definitive proofs of Islam constitutes kufr (disbelief) by consensus of the Muslims. The author first states that once definitive proof (dalil qat'i) confirms the truth of the message, rejecting any part of it—especially the miracles of the prophets—is kufr. He explains that it is meaningless to affirm Allah's divinity while simultaneously denying the signs He has sent with His prophets. Then he lists specific miracles: Ibrahim's fire becoming cool and safe, Isa's birth without a father, his healing of the blind and leprous, and his raising the dead. All these are textually established in the Qur'an with clear and manifest wording. He concludes by citing the verse that encapsulates the principle: Allah's command when He wills something is simply 'Be' and it is—emphasizing that miracles are direct acts of Allah, not subject to natural limitations.

Correction: The author argues that once the definitive proof of Allah's message is established, rejection of miracles constitutes kufr, because miracles are integral to recognizing prophethood and Allah's absolute power. Affirming Allah's divinity while denying His signs is self-contradictory.

Man as Master of the Universe and the Qur'anic Evidence
States the required belief about the cosmos and man's role as master with intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief that man is the master of the universe by divine wisdom, with the cosmos subjugated to him, and the Quranic evidence for this.

Core Idea
Man is master of the universe, endowed with intellect, as revealed in the Quran.

This passage summarizes the required belief about the cosmos. The author explains that God's wisdom made man the master of the universe, with all phenomena subjugated to serve him, and he is given intellect—a sacred reality—to exercise authority. A Quranic verse confirms this truth, while a footnote clarifies that 'man' refers to the essence of humanity, not every individual.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and footnote

The passage states man is master (sayyid) of the universe, with phenomena subjugated (musakhkhar) to serve him.
Intellect is described as a sacred reality (haqiqa qudsiyya).

فهذا مجمل ما يجب اعتقاده بالنسبة لشؤون الكون ومظاهره. وقد أوضحنا براهينه العلمية المتعلقة به. ولعلك قد علمت خلال ما ذكرناه، أن حكمة الله عز وجل اقتضت أن يكون الإنسان هو سيد هذا الكون، وأن تكون مظاهر الكون المختلفة من حوله مسخّرة لخدمته مسيَّرة لتحقيق مصالحه، وأن يكون له من عقله - وهو حقيقة قدسية لم تمنح لغيره - ما يمكنه من بسط سلطانه على كثير من شؤون الكون والتصرف بها طبق إرادته. (١) نقصد بالإنسان حقيقته وماهيته، بقطع النظر عن استقصاء الأفراد، ولو قصدنا به الجنس وعامة الأفراد لما صدق هذا الكلام كما هو ظاهر. ولقد أوضح كلام الخالق جل جلاله هذه الحقيقة بشكل لا يدع فيها لبساً ولا خفاء: ( ألم تَرَوْا أَنَّ اللهَ سَخَّرَ لَكُم مَا في السَّمواتِ ومَا في الأرضِ وَأَسْبَغَ عَلَيْكُم نِعَمَهُ ظَاهِرَةً وَبَاطِنَةً، وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يُجادِلُ في الله بغير علم وَلا هُدى وَلا كِتاب مُنير ﴾ [لقمان : ٢٠ ].
This is the total of what must be believed regarding the affairs of the cosmos and its phenomena. And we have explained its scientific proofs related to it. And perhaps you have come to know, throughout what we have mentioned, that the wisdom of God Almighty required that man is the master of this universe, and that the various phenomena of the universe around him are subjugated to his service, directed to achieve his interests, and that he has from his intellect—which is a sacred reality not granted to others—what enables him to extend his authority over many affairs of the universe and to dispose of them according to his will. (1) By 'man' we mean his essence and reality, regardless of the exhaustive inclusion of individuals; and if we meant the species and all individuals, this statement would not be true, as is apparent. And indeed the speech of the Creator—majestic is His glory—has clarified this truth in a way that leaves no ambiguity nor concealment: 'Do you not see that God has subjected to you whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth, and has completed His blessings upon you, outward and inward; and among the people is he who disputes about God without knowledge, without guidance, and without an enlightening book' [Surah Luqman: 20].
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage summarizes the required belief about the universe and then elaborates on man's role. The author states that God's wisdom made man the master (sayyid) of the universe, with all phenomena subjugated (musakhkhar) to serve him, and man is endowed with intellect—a sacred reality unique to him—enabling him to exercise authority. A footnote clarifies that 'man' here refers to the essence and reality of humanity, not every individual; if applied to all individuals, it would not be true. The Quranic verse from Luqman is then cited to confirm this truth: God has subjected the heavens and earth to man, a sign of His grace. The verse also notes that some people argue about God without knowledge—a warning. This lesson establishes the Islamic worldview of human dominion through intellect, grounded in divine wisdom.

Correction: The footnote clarifies that 'man' means the essence and reality of humanity (حقيقته وماهيته), not every individual. If taken as every individual, the statement would not be true, as apparent from reality.

The Rational Proof for the Invalidity of Reincarnation
Al-Buti presents the rational argument that reincarnation is an unseen matter which reason cannot verify without certain revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why reason alone cannot affirm or deny reincarnation and how certain reports from God become decisive proof.

Core Idea
Reason cannot penetrate the unseen; only certain revelation can confirm it.

In this passage, Al-Buti addresses the common claim of reincarnation by clarifying the limits of human reason. He explains that reincarnation belongs to the realm of the unseen (ghaybiyat), which reason cannot access except through authentic reports from Allah or His Messenger. Let's follow his rational argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Al-Buti uses a very precise logical structure.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage states that reincarnation is an unseen matter. Find where this is asserted and note how the author frames it.
The key term is 'المغيبات' (unseen things).
3
Understand the role of reason vs. revelation
Ask yourself: according to Al-Buti, what is the intellect's position on unseen matters without revelation? How does revelation change that? The commentary will help clarify.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الدَّلِيلُ الْعَقْلِيُّ وَالْعِلْمِيُّ، فَهُوَ أَنَّ تَصَوُّرَ التَّنَاسُخِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ شَيْءٌ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْمَغِيبَاتِ، كَمَا هُوَ مَعْلُومٌ. وَالأُمُورُ الْغَيْبِيَّةُ لَا سُلْطَانَ لِلْعَقْلِ عَلَيْهَا مَادَامَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهَا حِجَابٌ لَا يَنْفُذُ مِنْهُ أَيُّ بُرْهَانٍ مِنَ الْبَرَاهِينِ التَّجْرِيبِيَّةِ وَالْمُشَاهَدَةِ أَوِ اللُّزُومِ الْبَيِّنِ أَوِ الْقِيَاسِ الأَوْلَى الْقَائِمَيْنِ عَلَى الاسْتِقْرَاءِ التَّامِّ، فَالْخَيَالُ قَدْ يَذْهَبُ فِي تَصَوُّرِ هَذِهِ الْمَغِيبَاتِ كُلَّ مَذْهَبٍ، وَلَكِنَّ الْعَقْلَ لَا يُصَدِّقُ أَيَّ مَذْهَبٍ مِنْهَا مَا لَمْ يَقُمْ عَلَيْهِ الْبُرْهَانُ السَّلِيمُ. وَلَوْلَا أَنَّ أَخْبَارًا يَقِينِيَّةً مُتَوَاتِرَةً قَدْ وَرَدَتْ عَنِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ أَوْ عَنْ رَسُولِهِ بِبَعْضِ الْمَغِيبَاتِ، لَكَانَ مَوْقِفُ الْعَقْلِ مِنْهَا نَفْسَ الْمَوْقِفِ، أَيِ الإِنْكَارِ وَالْجُحُودِ مَادَامَ أَنَّهُ لَا بُرْهَانَ عَلَيْهَا. وَلَكِنْ لَمَّا وَرَدَ الْخَبَرُ الْيَقِينِيُّ عَمَّنْ قَامَ الْبُرْهَانُ الْعِلْمِيُّ عَلَى وُجُودِهِ وَصِدْقِهِ، كَانَ ذَلِكَ مُوجِبًا لِلتَّصْدِيقِ وَالإِذْعَانِ، إِذْ هَذَا الْخَبَرُ نَفْسُهُ، فِي مِثْلِ هَذِهِ الْحَالِ، بُرْهَانٌ عِلْمِيٌّ قَاطِعٌ. فَهَذِهِ هِيَ الْحَقَائِقُ الْغَيْبِيَّةُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَةُ بِالْمَوْتِ، عَرَضْنَاهَا مَعَ إِيضَاحِ بَرَاهِينِهَا.
As for the rational and scientific proof, it is that the conception of reincarnation is only something related to unseen things, as is known. And the unseen matters have no authority of the intellect over them as long as there is between them a veil through which no proof penetrates from the experimental proofs, observation, or clear necessary implication, or the a priori syllogism based on complete induction. So imagination may go in conceiving these unseen matters every way, but the intellect does not affirm any way among them unless a sound proof is established for it. And were it not that certain mutawatir reports have come from Allah Almighty or from His Messenger concerning some unseen matters, the intellect's position towards them would be the same position, i.e., denial and rejection as long as there is no proof for them. But when the certain report came from the one whose existence and truthfulness have been proven by scientific proof, that necessitated affirmation and submission, for this report itself, in such a case, is a decisive scientific proof. So these are the unseen facts related to death, which we have presented with an explanation of their proofs.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage presents the rational and scientific proof (dalil 'aqli wa 'ilmi) for the invalidity of reincarnation. The author explains that reincarnation is an unseen matter (ghaybiyat). Reason has no authority over unseen matters because they are veiled from empirical proof, observation, necessary implication, or a priori reasoning based on complete induction. Imagination can roam freely, but reason only accepts what has sound proof. If there were no certain mutawatir reports from God or His Messenger about some unseen realities, reason would reject them. However, when such reports come from the one whose existence and truthfulness are proven by scientific proof (i.e., God and His Messenger), those reports themselves become a decisive proof. The author concludes by stating that these are the unseen facts related to death, presented with their proofs.

Key Terms
الدليل العقلي
المغيبات
البرهان العلمي
الخبر اليقيني
التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think reason alone can prove or disprove reincarnation.
Correction: Reason cannot access the unseen; it requires certain revelation to affirm or deny unseen matters.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of the intellect towards unseen matters when no certain report from God or His Messenger exists?
A) It affirms them through imagination.
B) It denies and rejects them.
C) It remains neutral.
D) It seeks experimental proof.

Key Takeaway
Reincarnation is an unseen matter that reason cannot verify; only certain reports from God or His Messenger can provide decisive evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about death and what comes after, do you find yourself relying on your own imagination or on the certain reports from Allah and His Messenger? Which does this lesson say is the only valid basis for belief?
?
Is there any unseen matter in your faith that you have doubted because your reason could not grasp it? How does the argument that the report from the proven source is itself a decisive proof challenge you to submit?
?
If someone presented you with a claim about the afterlife that seemed plausible to your mind but lacked a certain report from revelation, would you accept it? What does this passage teach you about the limits of reason and the necessity of revelation?

The Logical Path to Acknowledging Allah's Sovereignty
Al-Buti recaps earlier conclusions and poses a decisive rhetorical question.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Buti builds an airtight logical case for Allah's exclusive legislative authority based on previously established truths.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's sovereignty while affirming His existence is rationally incoherent.

In the passage you are about to read, al-Buti brings together all the previous arguments—the existence of God, the purposefulness of creation, human responsibility, and prophethood—and asks a decisive question: can you consistently affirm all of these and still deny that Allah alone is the Ruler and Legislator? His answer is a resounding no. This lesson walks through that culminating logical step.

Guided Path
1
Recall the established truths
Read the first sentence listing what you have already accepted: existence of the Creator, purposeful creation, human responsibility, and prophethood. Notice how each is a logical prerequisite.
These are the building blocks of the argument.
2
Follow the rhetorical question
Identify the key question: 'هل يخالجك أدنى شك...' (Does any doubt assail you...?). Understand that this challenges the reader's consistency.
3
See the impossibility of denial
Al-Buti asserts that no rational person can combine belief in those truths with denial of Allah's sovereignty. Reflect on why he considers it impossible.
This is the core of the logical argument.
