الآن، وقد استيقنت نفسك كل هذه الحقائق التي فرغنا من عرضها وبيانها موزونة بميزان المنهج العلمي، معززة بأدلتها وبراهينها التي يتطلبها العقل، فأيقنت وجود الخالق العظيم جل جلاله، ثم أيقنت تبعاً لذلك أنه لم يخلق هذا الكون عبثاً وما ينبغي له العبث بحال، وأن الإنسان - وهو سيد المخلوقات في الكون - لابد أن يكون مكلفاً بوظيفة معينة شأنه في ذلك شأن سائر المخلوقات الأخرى، ولا بد أنه مسؤول عنها تجاه خالقه جل جلاله. ثم تأملت في تاريخ الزمن وأحداثه فاستيقنت نبوّة الأنبياء الذين بعثوا خلاله، وكان من مقتضى ذلك أن تستيقنت هذا الذي بعثوا إلى الناس به، من الحقائق الاعتقادية عن الكون والحياة والأحكام التشريعية المطلوب إقامتها في الدنيا؛ والتحذير من الإعراض عن شيء من ذلك، تحت طائلة العقاب العظيم المتوعد به في يوم الميعاد.

الآن، وقد استيقنت كل هذا، هل يخالجك أدنى شك في أن الحاكم إنما هو وحده وأنه صاحب السلطة التشريعية في الكون؟ وهل يمكنك أن تنكر ذلك فتزعم أن الحاكمية في هذه الدنيا إنما هي للإنسان وأنه هو المشرع لنفسه، ثم تجمع بين هذا الإنكار وبين الإيمان بكل هذه الحقائق التي سلف ذكرها؟!.. لا أظنك قادراً على أن تكابر لتزعم أن بإمكانك أن تجمع بين ذلك الإنكار وهذا الإيمان، ولا أظن أن أحداً من العقلاء الذين يصدقون مع أنفسهم يفعل ذلك.

الله إذاً، فالحاكمية إنما هي وحده، هو المشرع لعباده في شتى شؤونهم المتعلقة بدنياهم وآخرتهم وهو المرجع في حل كل مشكلة من مشكلاتهم وإقامة كل تنظيم ودستور لحياتهم. ومن جحد ذلك فهو كافر بالله ورسوله وإن ادعى بلسانه الإيمان بالله ورسوله وصلى وحج وصام. قامت على ذلك أدلة العقل والنقل من الكتاب والسنة وتم على ذلك إجماع المسلمين كلهم.

وحسبنا أن ننصت معاً في تقرير هذا الحق، إلى هذه الآيات من كتاب الله تعالى: (ألم تر إلى الذين يزعمون أنهم آمنوا بما أنزل إليك وما أنزل من قبلك يريدون أن يتحاكموا إلى الطاغوت وقد أمروا أن يكفروا به ويريد الشيطان أن يضلهم ضلالاً بعيداً. وإذا قيل لهم تعالوا إلى ما أنزل الله وإلى الرسول رأيت المنافقين يصدون عنك صدوداً. فكيف إذا أصابتهم مصيبة بما قدمت أيديهم ثم جاؤوك يحلفون بالله إن أردنا إلا إحساناً وتوفيقاً. أولئك الذين يعلم الله ما في قلوبهم فأعرض عنهم وعظهم وقل لهم في أنفسهم قولاً بليغاً. وما أرسلنا من رسول إلا ليطاع بإذن الله ولو أنهم إذ ظلموا أنفسهم جاؤوك فاستغفروا الله واستغفر لهم الرسول لوجدوا الله تواباً رحيماً. فلا وربك لا يؤمنون حتى يحكموك فيما شجر بينهم ثم لا يجدوا في أنفسهم حرجاً مما قضيت ويسلموا تسليماً) [النساء: 60-65].

ذلك أن الله عز وجل، قضت مشيئته أن يجعل من كونه هذا مظهراً لألوهيته وصفاته. فقضى أن يكون بعض هذا الكون مظهراً لذلك بمجرد الخلق والإيجاد، كالذي نراه من خلق السماوات والأرض وخلق الإنسان وما أودع فيه من فكر وعقل. وقضى أن يكون بعضه الآخر مظهراً لذلك بواسطة الأمر والتكليف يخاطب بها العقل والإرادة، وهو ما تراه من تشريع الله تعالى ونظامه اللذين ألزم بها عباده ليقيموا دولته في الأرض على أساسها. وجميع ذلك، بقسميه، مظهر لألوهية الله وعدالته وعلمه ورحمته وشديد عقابه، والكثير من
Now, when you have firmly believed all these truths that we have finished presenting and explaining, weighed by the scale of the scientific method, supported by their proofs and evidences that the intellect requires, and you have believed in the existence of the Great Creator, Glorious is His Majesty, then you have believed accordingly that He did not create this universe in vain and that it is not befitting for Him to be vain in any way, and that man - who is the master of creatures in the universe - must be charged with a specific function, his status in that being like the status of all other creatures, and he must be responsible for it towards his Creator, Glorious is His Majesty. Then you contemplated the history of time and its events and firmly believed in the prophethood of the prophets who were sent during it, and it follows from that that you firmly believe in what they brought to the people, of doctrinal truths about the universe and life and the legislative rulings required to be established in this world, and the warning against turning away from any of that, under the threat of the great punishment promised on the Day of Appointment.

Now, when you have firmly believed all this, does any doubt assail you that the Ruler is only He alone and that He is the possessor of legislative authority in the universe? And can you deny that and claim that sovereignty in this world is only for man and that he is the legislator for himself, then combine this denial with belief in all these truths that have been mentioned?! I do not think you are able to be obstinate to claim that you can combine that denial and this belief, and I do not think that any rational person who is truthful with himself does that.

Therefore, sovereignty is only His alone, He is the legislator for His servants in all their affairs related to their world and their Hereafter, and He is the reference in solving every problem of their problems and establishing every organization and constitution for their lives. Whoever denies that is a disbeliever in Allah and His Messenger, even if he claims with his tongue belief in Allah and His Messenger and prays, performs Hajj, and fasts. The proofs of reason and transmission from the Book and the Sunnah have been established on that, and the consensus of all Muslims has been concluded on that.

It is sufficient for us to listen together in affirming this truth to these verses from the Book of Allah Almighty: (Have you not seen those who claim that they believe in what was revealed to you and what was revealed before you? They wish to go to judgment before Taghut, while they have been commanded to disbelieve in it; and Satan wishes to lead them far astray. And when it is said to them, "Come to what Allah has revealed and to the Messenger," you see the hypocrites turning away from you in aversion. Then how will it be when disaster strikes them because of what their hands have put forth? Then they come to you swearing by Allah, "We only wanted good conduct and success." Those are the ones of whom Allah knows what is in their hearts, so turn away from them, admonish them, and say to them concerning themselves an eloquent word. And We did not send any messenger except to be obeyed by permission of Allah. And if, when they wronged themselves, they had come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah Accepting of repentance and Merciful. But no, by your Lord, they will not [truly] believe until they make you judge concerning that over which they dispute, then find within themselves no discomfort from what you have judged and submit completely.) [An-Nisa: 60-65].

That is because Allah Almighty, His will decreed that He make this universe of His a manifestation of His divinity and attributes. So He decreed that some of this universe be a manifestation of that by mere creation and bringing into existence, like what we see of the creation of the heavens and the earth and the creation of man and what He placed in him of thought and intellect. And He decreed that some other part of it be a manifestation of that by means of command and obligation addressed to intellect and will, which is what you see of the legislation of Allah and His system which He has obligated upon His servants so that they may establish His state on earth upon its basis. And all of that, in its two divisions, is a manifestation of the divinity of Allah, His justice, His knowledge, His mercy, and His severe punishment, and much of
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is the concluding argument for the exclusive sovereignty (al-ḥākimiyya) of Allah. The author begins by recapitulating the series of truths the reader has presumably accepted: the existence of God, the purposeful creation of the universe, the responsibility of humans, and the prophethood of the prophets. From these premises, he poses a rhetorical question: after accepting all this, can one still doubt that the sole ruler and legislator is Allah? He argues that it is impossible to simultaneously believe in these truths and deny Allah's legislative authority; no rational person would do so. Hence, sovereignty belongs to Allah alone: He is the legislator for all affairs, the reference for solving problems, and the source of all systems. Denial of this constitutes disbelief (kufr), even if one outwardly performs acts of worship. The author then supports this conclusion with textual evidence, quoting Qur'anic verses (An-Nisa 60-65) that condemn seeking judgment from other than Allah and emphasize the necessity of accepting the Messenger's judgment. Finally, he explains the theological basis: Allah's will decreed that the universe manifest His attributes in two ways: through direct creation (e.g., heavens, earth, human intellect) and through legislation (commands and prohibitions addressed to human will). Both are manifestations of His divinity, justice, knowledge, mercy, and punishment. The passage insists that rejecting divine legislation is tantamount to rejecting the very purpose of creation.

Key Terms
الحاكمية
المشرع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can believe in God and prophets while denying that God alone has the right to legislate.
Correction: Al-Buti argues that accepting prophethood logically entails accepting the message they brought, which includes legislative rulings. Thus, denying divine legislation contradicts belief in prophethood itself.

Checkpoint
According to al-Buti, what is the relationship between believing in prophethood and accepting Allah's legislative authority?
A) They are unrelated; prophethood is only about moral guidance.
B) Accepting prophethood necessarily leads to accepting the legislative rulings brought by the prophets.
C) One can accept prophethood while rejecting some legislative rulings.
D) Prophethood only confirms pre-existing human laws.

Key Takeaway
Accepting Allah's existence, purpose, prophethood, and accountability naturally leads to the conclusion that He alone is the Sovereign and Legislator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading this passage, are you personally guilty of the 'obstinacy' al-Buti describes – affirming Allah's existence and prophethood with your tongue yet denying His exclusive right to legislate your life and society? In what specific area of your life do you resist His sovereignty?
?
If you truly believed that man's legislative authority is an illusion and that Allah alone is the Ruler, how would your attitude change towards the moral and legal decisions you make daily? Can you identify one decision you are making right now that assumes you have the right to decide what is right and wrong independent of Allah's law?
?
Al-Buti says that no rational person truthful with himself can combine belief in these truths with denial of Allah's sovereignty. Are you that rational and truthful person? If you find yourself living as if your own preferences override divine commands, what does that say about the sincerity of your faith?

The Necessity of Allah's Legislation and the Qur'anic Proof
Al-Buti declares the ruling and supports it with Qur'an and theological reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Buti's explicit conclusion that denying Allah's legislation is kufr, and the Qur'anic evidence he provides to support it.

Core Idea
Whoever denies Allah's exclusive right to legislate is a disbeliever, even if they outwardly practice Islam.

After establishing the logical necessity, al-Buti now delivers the decisive conclusion: sovereignty belongs to Allah alone, and whoever denies that is a disbeliever. He supports this not only with reason but with Qur'anic verses that condemn seeking judgment from other than Allah. This lesson explains that conclusion and the scriptural foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the declaration of sovereignty
Focus on the statement 'الله إذاً، فالحاكمية إنما هي وحده...' and note the ruling that denial is kufr.
This is the central claim.
2
Examine the Qur'anic quotation
Read the verses from An-Nisa 60-65 and identify the themes: rejection of taghut, the call to Allah and the Messenger, and the condition of true faith.
The verses are the scriptural proof.
3
Understand the theological basis
The last paragraph explains that legislation is a manifestation of Allah's attributes, just as creation is. Notice the parallel between creation and command.
This ties legislation to the very purpose of creation.

He argues that it is impossible to simultaneously believe in these truths and deny Allah's legislative authority; no rational person would do so. Hence, sovereignty belongs to Allah alone: He is the legislator for all affairs, the reference for solving problems, and the source of all systems. Denial of this constitutes disbelief (kufr), even if one outwardly performs acts of worship. The author then supports this conclusion with textual evidence, quoting Qur'anic verses (An-Nisa 60-65) that condemn seeking judgment from other than Allah and emphasize the necessity of accepting the Messenger's judgment. Finally, he explains the theological basis: Allah's will decreed that the universe manifest His attributes in two ways: through direct creation (e.g., heavens, earth, human intellect) and through legislation (commands and prohibitions addressed to human will). Both are manifestations of His divinity, justice, knowledge, mercy, and punishment. The passage insists that rejecting divine legislation is tantamount to rejecting the very purpose of creation.

Key Terms
الحاكمية
المشرع
الكفر
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can deny Allah's exclusive legislative authority while still being a believer if they perform acts of worship.
Correction: Al-Buti explicitly states that denial of Allah's sole legislative authority is kufr, even if one prays, fasts, and performs Hajj.

Checkpoint
According to al-Buti, what is the ruling on someone who denies that Allah alone is the legislator even if they outwardly profess faith and perform acts of worship?
A) They are sinful but remain within the fold of Islam.
B) They are hypocrites but not disbelievers.
C) They are disbelievers (kuffār) in Allah and His Messenger.
D) They are excused due to ignorance.

Key Takeaway
Allah's legislative authority is as much a manifestation of His divinity as creating the universe, and rejecting it constitutes disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In which area of your life do you find it hardest to accept Allah’s legislation over your own preference or society’s norms? What specific step can you take today to align that area with the truth that His command is a direct manifestation of His divinity?
?
You might pray, fast, and perform other acts of worship, yet harbor a deep unease with a particular divine ruling. According to this passage, what is that unease a symptom of? Are you willing to ask Allah to remove it from your heart, even if it means upending your current understanding?
?
If you truly believe that Allah’s legislative authority is as real and necessary as His creation of the heavens, would your daily decisions reflect that? Look at your next week: where will you consciously choose His command over convenience, even in a small matter?

Two Methods for Proving God's Existence
Introduces two methods for proving God's existence and begins the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main methods in Islamic theology for proving God's existence: the top-down and bottom-up approaches, and the beginning of the first method.

Core Idea
Proving God's existence can start from the highest or the lowest.

The Islamic theological tradition employs two complementary methods to demonstrate the existence of God. One begins with the concept of the Necessary Being and argues downward to creation, while the other starts with observable creation and ascends to the Creator. This passage introduces these two methods and begins to outline the first.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that the text introduces a new section on divinities and states there are two methods.
The Arabic text is cut off; we only have the beginning of the first method.
2
Identify the two methods
Look for the names of the two methods in Arabic: منهج التدرج من الأعلى and منهج الصعود من الأدنى. Understand their literal meanings.
The first method is 'descending from the highest', the second is 'ascending from the lowest'.
3
Focus on the first method
The passage begins to describe the first method: 'the proof of the impossibility of preference without a preponderator'. Consider why this is called a top-down argument.
This proof starts from the concept of a necessary being and argues that contingency requires a preponderator.
4
Note the incompleteness
Be aware that the text cuts off. The second method and the full description of the first are not provided in this lesson.
This lesson only introduces the methods; further lessons will develop each proof.

Source Text

القسم الأول : الإلهيات أولاً - وجود الله عز وجل : لإثبات وجود الله عز وجل وما يتبعه منهجان : منهج التدرج من الأعلى ومنهج الصعود من الأدنى . طريق التدرج من الأعلى : أولاً برهان بطلان الرجحان بدون
First Section: Divinities. First: The existence of God Almighty: For proving the existence of God Almighty and what follows it, there are two methods: the method of descending from the highest and the method of ascending from the lowest. The path of descending from the highest: first, the proof of the impossibility of preference without [a preponderator].
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage introduces the section on divinity (ilāhiyyāt). It states that to prove God's existence and its consequences, there are two methods: the method of descending from the highest (top-down) and the method of ascending from the lowest (bottom-up). The top-down method begins with the proof of the impossibility of preference without a preponderator (burhān buṭlān al-tarjīḥ bilā murajjiḥ), which is the cosmological argument from contingency. The text is cut off before completing the description.

Key Terms

Correction: The text presents them as complementary approaches, not competing. Both aim to prove the same truth from different starting points.

Key Takeaway
There are two main methods in Islamic theology for proving God's existence: top-down (from necessary being to creation) and bottom-up (from creation to Creator).

?
If you were to explain the existence of God to someone struggling with doubt, which method would you use? Your answer shows which proof you trust more. But is your trust in the proof itself, or in the God the proof points to? How can you move from intellectual assent to a lived certainty?

Two Methods of Proving God's Existence
Buti outlines two methods and lists proofs for the top-down approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two broad methods (top-down and bottom-up) and the specific proofs listed under the top-down method.

Core Idea
Proving God's existence follows two clear paths: from principles or from creation.

Buti begins the section on divine existence by outlining two methodological approaches. Before diving into detailed arguments, he gives an overview that orients the reader. This passage is the map for the journey ahead.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the overview sink in before interpreting.
Notice the two methods are named at the start.
2
Identify the two methods
Find the two methods: 'descending from the highest' (top-down) and 'ascending from the lowest' (bottom-up). Note where each starts from.
Top-down starts from metaphysical principles; bottom-up starts from observable phenomena.
3
List the proofs under the top-down method
Find the five proofs listed: invalidity of preference without a preferrer, invalidity of infinite regress, invalidity of circularity, refutation of self-interaction, and law of causality/final cause.
These are standard kalam arguments; each will be explained in detail later.
4
Reflect on the sequence
Consider that these proofs are not random; they form a coherent logical sequence from the impossibility of a world without a sufficient reason.
This sequence will be unpacked in the following lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولاً - وجود الله عز وجل : لإثبات وجود الله عز وجل وما يتبعه منهجان : منهج التدرج من الأعلى ومنهج الصعود من الأدنى . طريق التدرج من الأعلى : أولاً برهان بطلان الرجحان بدون مرجح - ثانياً برهان بطلان التسلسل - ثالثاً برهان بطلان الدور - القول بالتفاعل الذاتي وبيان بطلانه - قانون العلية أو ( العلة الغائية ( معنى العلة الغائية وبيان قيام الكون على أساسها .
First — The existence of God Almighty: To prove the existence of God Almighty and what follows from it, there are two methods: the method of descending from the highest and the method of ascending from the lowest. The path of descending from the highest: First, the proof of the invalidity of preference without a preferrer. Second, the proof of the invalidity of infinite regress. Third, the proof of the invalidity of circularity. The statement of self-interaction and the demonstration of its invalidity. The law of causality or (the final cause) — the meaning of the final cause and the demonstration that the universe is established upon it.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage introduces the section on God's existence. Buti states that there are two methods to prove God's existence and what follows from it (i.e., His attributes). The first method is 'descending from the highest' (al-tadarruj min al-aʿla), which starts from metaphysical principles. The second is 'ascending from the lowest' (al-ṣuʿud min al-adna), which starts from observable phenomena. He then lists the proofs under the first method: 1) Proof of the impossibility of preference without a preferrer (burhan butlan al-rujhan bila murajjih), 2) Proof of the impossibility of infinite regress (butlan al-tasalsul), 3) Proof of the impossibility of circularity (butlan al-dawr), 4) The claim of self-interaction (al-tafaʿul al-dhati) and its refutation, and 5) The law of causality or final cause (al-ʿillah al-gha'iyyah) and that the universe is based on it. This is a standard list of arguments in kalam.

Key Terms
منهج التدرج من الأعلى (top-down method)
منهج الصعود من الأدنى (bottom-up method)
برهان بطلان الرجحان بدون مرجح
برهان بطلان التسلسل
برهان بطلان الدور
القول بالتفاعل الذاتي
قانون العلية
العلة الغائية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think these proofs are separate and unrelated; Buti presents them as a coherent sequence.
Correction: The proofs are connected logically: they systematically address the need for a first cause and refute alternatives.

Checkpoint

A) Method of ascending from the lowest
B) Method of descending from the highest
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Buti presents two methods for proving God's existence; the top-down method includes five interconnected rational proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness everyday events, how often do you pause to ask, 'Why did this happen?' and trace it back beyond the material cause to the ultimate Cause, Allah? What would change in your heart if you consciously affirmed the principle of 'preference without a preferrer' in every situation?
?
The final cause argument says the universe is established on purpose. Look at your daily life: which of your actions are performed without any conscious intention? How can you transform even the smallest acts into acts of worship by dedicating them to Allah?
?
You now know two rational methods to prove God's existence. But are these proofs alive in your heart, or are they just intellectual concepts? What step will you take today to internalize one of these arguments so that your faith becomes more certain?

Refuting Dialectical Materialism
Buti refutes dialectical materialism using the axiom of opposites and empirical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti refutes dialectical materialism by appealing to the axiom of opposites and scientific evidence.

Core Idea
Dialectical materialism is refuted by the self-evident truth that opposites cannot coexist.

Buti begins his critique of materialism by tackling its first branch: dialectical materialism. He uses a simple logical axiom—that two opposites cannot be together—to question why materialism arbitrarily makes matter the origin of life. He then supports his argument with references to scientific conferences and researchers who acknowledged the failure of materialist explanations for the origin of life.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Buti presents his argument.
The passage is concise; each phrase carries weight.
2
Identify the self-evident axiom
Buti starts with a self-evident truth: two opposites cannot come together. Why is this important?
This is the foundation of his logical critique.
3
Understand the rhetorical question
Buti asks: why should matter be the origin of life rather than life the origin of matter? This exposes an arbitrary assumption.
It challenges the materialist claim without external evidence.
4
Consider the empirical evidence
Buti references the New York conference and Oparin's statement. What does that imply about materialism's scientific support?
Even scientists admitted materialist explanations failed.
5
Reflect on the refutation
How do the axiom and the empirical evidence together refute dialectical materialism?
The axiom shows logical inconsistency; evidence shows empirical failure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصير الفلسفة المادية أمام هذه البراهين : ونبدأ بمناقشة الفرع الأول وهو ( المادية الجدلية ( فنقول : من المسلمات البدهية ، أن النقيضين لا يجتمعان .. لماذا تكون المادة أصل الحياة ولا تكون الحياة أصل المادة مثلاً ؟ - الفلسفة المادية محجوجة بواقع التجربة الملموسة - مؤتمر العلماء الذي عقد في نيويورك لبحث أصل الحياة - ألكسندر أوبارين رئيس معهد الكيمياء الحيوية في روسيا وما قاله عن أصل الحياة . ثم نناقش الفرع الثاني وهو ( المادية التاريخية ) - المقصود بالمادية التاريخية - لماذا خضعت وسيلة الإنتاج عند الإنسان لحكم الديالكتيك بينما تحررت عنه هذه الوسيلة عند الحيوان ؟ - مقتضى قانون الديالكتيك أن يظل تركيب المجتمع الإنساني في تطور وتناقض - ما هو عامل الفكر لدى الإنسان ؟ - هل الفكر أثر من آثار العامل الاقتصادي ؟
The fate of materialist philosophy before these proofs: We begin by discussing the first branch, which is dialectical materialism. We say: It is a self-evident axiom that two opposites cannot come together. Why should matter be the origin of life and not life the origin of matter, for example? Materialist philosophy is refuted by tangible empirical reality. The conference of scientists held in New York to research the origin of life. Alexander Oparin, head of the Institute of Biochemistry in Russia, and what he said about the origin of life. Then we discuss the second branch, which is historical materialism. The meaning of historical materialism. Why did humans’ means of production fall under the law of dialectics while at the same time these means were free from it in animals? The requirement of the law of dialectics is that the structure of human society remains in development and contradiction. What is the factor of thought in humans? Is thought a mere effect of the economic factor?
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of materialism. Buti discusses two branches: dialectical materialism and historical materialism. For dialectical materialism, he argues from the axiom that opposites cannot coexist. He questions why matter should be considered the origin of life rather than the reverse. He then cites a scientific conference in New York and the statement of Alexander Oparin about the origin of life, implying that even science does not support materialism. For historical materialism, he asks why human production methods are subject to dialectics while animal production is not, and questions whether thought is merely an economic epiphenomenon. The passage is a series of rhetorical questions pointing out inconsistencies.

Key Terms
المادية الجدلية
النقيضين
أصل الحياة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe materialism is supported by modern science.
Correction: Buti shows that even scientists like Oparin acknowledged the failure of materialist explanations of life's origin.

Checkpoint
What is the self-evident axiom Buti uses to refute dialectical materialism?
A) Life is the origin of matter
B) Two opposites cannot come together
C) Matter is eternal
D) Science proves materialism

Key Takeaway
Buti refutes dialectical materialism by showing that its claim that matter is the origin of life contradicts the axiom that opposites cannot coexist, and also fails empirically.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself living as if only the material world matters, ignoring the spiritual? What is one concrete habit you can change today to affirm that life has a higher origin?
?
When you face a difficult question about existence, do you instinctively turn to material explanations first? How can you remind yourself that the axiom of opposites points to a Creator beyond matter?

Refuting Historical Materialism
Buti questions historical materialism's consistency regarding dialectics and the role of thought.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Historical materialism fails to explain why dialectics apply to humans but not animals, and reduces thought to an economic effect.

In the second part of his refutation, Buti turns to historical materialism. He raises pointed questions: why should human means of production be subject to dialectical laws while animal means are not? He also challenges the materialist claim that thought is merely a product of economic factors, implying that this reductionism is inconsistent.

4

Buti asks: what is the factor of thought in humans? Is it merely an effect of the economic factor?
This questions the reductionist view of thought.
5

The Quran as Bottom-Up Proof for God's Existence
Buti outlines a rational proof for God from Quran transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's chain of transmission and the phenomenon of revelation serve as rational proof for the existence of God.

Core Idea
The Quran's definitive transmission demands a rational conclusion: God exists.

Buti introduces a second method for proving God's existence: working upward from observable reality. He starts with the Quran—not as a scripture to be believed, but as a historical document with a verifiable chain of transmission. From there, he moves to the phenomenon of revelation experienced by Muhammad, using rational arguments to establish that it truly came from God. This logical progression forces any rational person to accept God's existence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the starting point: the Quran
Read the passage and note that Buti begins with the Quran as a 'strange book' with a definitive chain of transmission (al-sanad al-qat'i). This is the empirical foundation.
Buti emphasizes that we are 'before' this book; it demands investigation.
2
Identify the phenomenon of revelation
Buti next identifies the key issue: the phenomenon of revelation (zahirat al-wahy) that Muhammad experienced. This is the 'scientific issue' to be examined.
Revelation is treated as an observable event, not a matter of faith.
3
Discover the verification arguments
Buti mentions two arguments: proof of correlation (burhan al-talazum) and argument of priority (qiyas al-awla). These are the rational tools to verify revelation.
Though not elaborated here, these arguments logically link revelation to God.
4
Reach the necessity of belief
Once revelation is verified, Buti concludes that we are 'before the necessity of believing in the existence of God.' This is the inevitable outcome of the reasoning.
The final sentence hints at a further proof for those still doubting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طريق التدرج من الأدنى : نحن الآن أمام كتاب غريب اسمه القرآن - وصلنا هذا الكتاب بالسند القطعي عن رجل اسمه محمد بن عبد الله ـ نحن بعد ذلك أمام مسألة علمية هي : ظاهرة الوحي التي تلبس بها محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام - تحقيق الوحي عن طريق برهان التلازم وقياس الأولى - إذا انتهينا من ذلك وجدنا أنفسنا أمام ضرورة الإيمان بوجود الله وأخيراً : إن رأيت عاقلاً لا يزال بعد هذا كله شاكاً في وجود الله فاعلم أنك الله منه أمام برهان جديد على وجود الله .
The path of ascending from the lowest: We are now before a strange book called the Quran. This book reached us with a definitive chain of transmission from a man named Muhammad ibn Abdullah. Then we are before a scientific issue: the phenomenon of revelation (al-wahy) that Muhammad (peace be upon him) experienced. Verifying revelation through the proof of correlation (burhan al-talazum) and the argument of priority (qiyas al-awla). If we finish that, we find ourselves before the necessity of believing in the existence of God. And finally: If you see a rational person who is still, after all this, doubtful about God's existence, then know that you are [فاعلم أنك الله منه?] before a new proof of God's existence.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage presents the second method, ascending from the lowest (al-ṣuʿud min al-adna). Buti starts with the Quran, which is a book with a definitive chain of transmission from Muhammad. He then identifies the issue: the phenomenon of revelation (al-wahy) that Muhammad experienced. To verify revelation, he mentions two arguments: the proof of correlation (burhan al-talazum) and the argument of priority (qiyas al-awla). Once revelation is established, it necessitates belief in God. He concludes that any rational person who remains doubtful after this must be facing a new proof of God's existence (though the text is ambiguous).

Key Terms
السند القطعي (definitive chain of transmission)
ظاهرة الوحي (phenomenon of revelation)
برهان التلازم (proof of correlation)
قياس الأولى (argument of priority)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in God is a blind leap of faith without evidence.
Correction: Buti shows that belief in God can be rationally derived from observable facts like the Quran's transmission and the phenomenon of revelation, using logical arguments.

Checkpoint
What is the starting point of Buti's bottom-up proof for God's existence?
A) The existence of the universe
B) The Quran and its transmission
C) Human consciousness
D) The laws of nature

Key Takeaway
The Quran's verifiable transmission and rational verification of revelation compel any rational person to acknowledge the existence of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the Quran's transmission is a rational proof for God. Have you ever personally verified this chain for yourself? If not, what is stopping you from investigating it? Make a commitment this week to trace the transmission of one verse.
?
Buti claims that after this rational proof, every rational person must believe. If you already believe, does your life reflect the certainty that God's existence is rationally undeniable? In what area of your life are you still living as if God's existence is uncertain? What will you change today to align your actions with this certainty?
?
The proof requires verifying the phenomenon of revelation. Have you ever doubted that the Quran is truly from God? How does this lesson's rational approach address your doubt? What specific step will you take to transform that doubt into conviction?
